Great question — and here is the real answer after fully reviewing the documents you uploaded:

❌ Base44 does NOT contain the full backend logic
It contains UI panels, event emitters, forms, and admin tools, but not:

database migrations

SQL tables

backend business logic

credit escrow logic

pricing logic

job timers

earnings-to-payout conversions

webhook handlers

payment processing

recurring scheduling

reliability system automation

authorization rules

Base44 does contain:

✅ 1. UI panels and admin pages
Examples from your files:

NotificationPreferences panel

Referral test panel (emit events)

Admin message log, resend tools

These panels emit events and display data, but they don’t implement the core logic.

✅ 2. Event emitters (front-end triggers)
Example:
Base44 can emit referral.earned, preferences.updated, etc.
But these events must be processed by n8n or your backend.

Base44 ONLY sends:

{ event_name, event_id, occurred_at, payload }
It does NOT handle the logic that happens after the event.

✅ 3. UI hints / references to models
The Base44 files reference:

Users

Jobs

CreditTransactions

Visits

Payouts

Photos

Tiers

Cleaner profile fields

But these are views, not logic.

Example: “Cleaner Profile Page” UI spec

→ Shows profile badge, score, etc.
→ But does not calculate reliability or price.

Example: “Credit purchase → ledger” logic

→ Defined in schema documents, NOT Base44.

❌ What Base44 does NOT contain
From all scans, these items do NOT exist inside Base44:

Needed Logic	Found?	Where logic actually exists
SQL tables	❌	Exists only in schema docs (not Base44)
Ledger math (hold → release → refund)	❌	n8n + backend
Job lifecycle transitions	❌	n8n workflows
Stripe webhook handling	❌	n8n workflow (Stripe Webhook Ingest)
Payout batching	❌	n8n weekly payout processor
Cleaner pricing calculations	❌	Backend logic only
Reliability score math	❌	Backend/n8n
Tier upgrade logic	❌	n8n subflow
Recurring booking generation	❌	n8n Recurring Plan Generator
Base44 reads and updates data, but does not create or compute the data.

❗ So what IS Base44 actually?
Base44 is:

✔ A UI layer
(Pages, forms, table views)

✔ An event emitter
(Fires events to n8n or your API)

✔ A headless admin console
(Views + controls)

✔ A low-code front-end
That REQUIRES:

a working API

a working database

working automations

❌ Base44 is NOT a backend
It is not a replacement for:

Neon (database)

Express/Node backend

n8n automations

Stripe webhooks

🚀 REASON YOU CANNOT BUILD BASE44 FIRST
Because Base44 cannot function until:

DB tables exist

API endpoints exist

Stripe/n8n workflows exist

job lifecycle logic exists

credit ledger exists

Otherwise every Base44 panel will break.

Example:
Base44 "Buy Credits" UI cannot work until:

POST /credits/purchase exists

Stripe webhook → n8n → ledger logic runs

Wallet balance updates in Neon

Base44 only shows the UI for it.

🟩 FINAL ANSWER
Base44 includes the pages and UI references for users, jobs, credits, and payouts — but NOT the actual logic.
You still need:

Neon DB (tables + migrations)

So the correct build order remains:

Nice, this is where it gets fun. I’ll give you:

Booking Flow State Machine (states, transitions, triggers, side-effects)

Core Base44 Entity JSON Schemas you can drop into entities/*.json

All based on the Base44 info doc you just uploaded.

🧩 1) Booking Flow Schema (State Machine Spec)
1.1 Booking Status Enum
From the Base44 doc, your Booking.status enum is:

// Booking.status
type BookingStatus =
  | "created"
  | "payment_hold"
  | "awaiting_cleaner_response"
  | "accepted"
  | "cleaner_declined"
  | "checking_fallback"
  | "scheduled"
  | "reschedule_requested"
  | "on_the_way"
  | "in_progress"
  | "completed"
  | "awaiting_client"
  | "approved"
  | "cancelled"
  | "disputed";
1.2 State-by-state breakdown
For each status:

created
When set

Immediately after client submits booking request (time, hours, address, preferred cleaner, etc.).

Key fields

client_email, cleaner_email?

date, start_time, hours, estimated_hours

snapshot_* pricing fields, total_price

Transitions

created → payment_hold (system)

Trigger: booking submitted, credits/payment check succeeds.

Side effects

Reserve credits: set escrow_credits_reserved, deduct from ClientProfile.credits_balance.

Create Stripe stripe_payment_intent_id and Payment record (status: pending).

payment_hold
When set

After credits are escrowed and Stripe PaymentIntent is in “authorized / payment_held” state.

Key fields

escrow_credits_reserved, payment_held=true, payment_captured=false.

Transitions

payment_hold → awaiting_cleaner_response (system)

Side effects

Send booking request notification to preferred cleaner(s).

awaiting_cleaner_response
When set

Cleaner has X minutes to accept/decline.

Key fields

request_sent_at, request_expires_at, cleaner_viewed_at?.

Transitions

awaiting_cleaner_response → accepted (cleaner accepts)

awaiting_cleaner_response → cleaner_declined (cleaner declines)

awaiting_cleaner_response → checking_fallback (system on expiry / failure)

awaiting_cleaner_response → cancelled (client cancels before acceptance)

Side effects

On expiry: mark missed response (hurts reliability punctuality / acceptance metric).

On accept: snapshot payout_percentage_at_accept.

cleaner_declined
Transitions

cleaner_declined → checking_fallback (system)

Side effects

Increment cleaner’s decline / cancellation metrics (reliability engine).

checking_fallback
When set

System is looking for alternate cleaner(s).

Transitions

checking_fallback → awaiting_cleaner_response (new cleaner invited)

checking_fallback → cancelled (no cleaner found)

Side effects

If no cleaner: release escrowed credits, cancel PaymentIntent, create Credit refund entry.

accepted
When set

A cleaner has accepted; job is committed but not yet fully “scheduled”.

Transitions

accepted → scheduled (system after confirmations)

accepted → reschedule_requested (client/cleaner proposes change)

Side effects

Confirm cleaner and client; update ClientProfile.total_bookings, CleanerProfile.total_jobs counters later when job completes.

scheduled
When set

Date/time locked in; cleaner assigned.

Key fields

client_confirmed, cleaner_confirmed booleans.

Transitions

scheduled → on_the_way (cleaner taps “On the way”)

scheduled → reschedule_requested (either side)

scheduled → cancelled (either side cancels before start)

Side effects

If late cancellation, adjust reliability / maybe fees.

reschedule_requested
Key fields

reschedule_requested_by, reschedule_new_date, reschedule_new_time.

Transitions

reschedule_requested → scheduled (request accepted)

reschedule_requested → cancelled (request rejected / expired)

on_the_way
When set

Cleaner heading to job.

Transitions

on_the_way → in_progress (cleaner check-in at location)

on_the_way → cancelled (no-show / client cancels last-minute)

Side effects

Punctuality metric uses difference between check_in_time and start_time.

in_progress
When set

Cleaner checked-in; timer running.

Key fields

check_in_time, check_out_time, actual_hours.

Transitions

in_progress → completed (cleaner checks out and uploads photos)

in_progress → cancelled (edge case – emergency stop)

Side effects

Enforce before/after photos: photo_proof_submitted, photo_count.

completed
When set

Cleaner done, but client hasn’t confirmed yet.

Transitions

completed → awaiting_client (system)

Side effects

Compute provisional final_charge_credits from actual_hours and snapshots; set refund_credits if under-estimate.

awaiting_client
When set

Client must review + approve, or open dispute.

Key fields

review_submitted flag.

Transitions

awaiting_client → approved (client approves or auto-approve timeout)

awaiting_client → disputed (client opens dispute)

Side effects

If no response by T+48h (your earlier spec): system auto-approves and moves to approved.

approved
Final “happy path” state.

Side effects

Deduct final_charge_credits from escrow, return refund_credits to ClientProfile via Credit entries; update ClientProfile.credits_balance.

Compute cleaner earnings using payout_percentage_at_accept; write Payment.cleaner_payout + Payment.platform_fee.

Aggregate into Payout batch (weekly/instant) with stripe_transfer_id.

Update reliability metrics / tier via CleanerAnalytics & CleanerProfile.reliability_score.

cancelled
When set

Booking is dead.

Key fields

cancellation_timestamp.

Side effects

Handle credit refunds depending on who cancelled / when (full, partial, or none).

Reliability hit for cleaner if they cancelled or no-showed.

disputed
When set

Client opened dispute on booking.

Side effects

Create Dispute entity (reason, evidence, status).

Auto-hold payout (don’t aggregate into Payout until resolved).

Reliability metrics consider dispute outcome.

1.3 Compact JSON-style spec for transitions
Here’s a condensed JSON you can literally paste into docs:

{
  "entity": "Booking",
  "statusField": "status",
  "states": {
    "created": {
      "next": ["payment_hold"],
      "onEnter": ["reserveCredits", "createStripePaymentIntent", "createPaymentRecord"]
    },
    "payment_hold": {
      "next": ["awaiting_cleaner_response", "cancelled"],
      "onEnter": ["notifyCleanerRequest"]
    },
    "awaiting_cleaner_response": {
      "next": ["accepted", "cleaner_declined", "checking_fallback", "cancelled"],
      "triggers": {
        "accepted": "cleaner_accepts",
        "cleaner_declined": "cleaner_declines",
        "checking_fallback": "response_window_expires",
        "cancelled": "client_cancels"
      }
    },
    "cleaner_declined": {
      "next": ["checking_fallback"],
      "onEnter": ["incrementCleanerDeclineMetric"]
    },
    "checking_fallback": {
      "next": ["awaiting_cleaner_response", "cancelled"],
      "triggers": {
        "awaiting_cleaner_response": "alternate_cleaner_found",
        "cancelled": "no_cleaner_available"
      }
    },
    "accepted": {
      "next": ["scheduled", "reschedule_requested"],
      "onEnter": ["snapshotPayoutPercentage"]
    },
    "scheduled": {
      "next": ["on_the_way", "reschedule_requested", "cancelled"]
    },
    "reschedule_requested": {
      "next": ["scheduled", "cancelled"]
    },
    "on_the_way": {
      "next": ["in_progress", "cancelled"]
    },
    "in_progress": {
      "next": ["completed", "cancelled"],
      "onEnter": ["recordCheckInTime"],
      "onExit": ["recordCheckOutTime", "computeActualHours"]
    },
    "completed": {
      "next": ["awaiting_client"],
      "onEnter": ["computeFinalChargeAndRefund"]
    },
    "awaiting_client": {
      "next": ["approved", "disputed"],
      "triggers": {
        "approved": "client_approves_or_timeout",
        "disputed": "client_opens_dispute"
      }
    },
    "approved": {
      "next": [],
      "onEnter": [
        "settleCredits",
        "createCreditRefundIfNeeded",
        "updateClientBalance",
        "computeCleanerEarnings",
        "recordPaymentPayout",
        "updateReliabilityMetrics"
      ]
    },
    "cancelled": {
      "next": [],
      "onEnter": ["handleCancellationRefunds", "updateCancellationMetrics"]
    },
    "disputed": {
      "next": [],
      "onEnter": ["createDisputeEntity", "holdPayoutUntilResolved"]
    }
  }
}
You can refine those action names into actual Base44 automations or “state-change handlers”.

🧱 2) Base44 Entity JSON Schemas (Option 3)
These are starter schemas for your entities/*.json.
Base44 automatically adds: id, created_date, updated_date, created_by.

Use standard JSON Schema style.

⚠️ These are intentionally “core fields only” based on the PDF. You can extend as needed.

2.1 Booking.json
{
  "title": "Booking",
  "type": "object",
  "properties": {
    "client_email": { "type": "string", "format": "email" },
    "cleaner_email": { "type": "string", "format": "email" },

    "date": { "type": "string", "format": "date" },
    "start_time": { "type": "string", "format": "time" },
    "hours": { "type": "number" },
    "estimated_hours": { "type": "number" },

    "status": {
      "type": "string",
      "enum": [
        "created",
        "payment_hold",
        "awaiting_cleaner_response",
        "accepted",
        "cleaner_declined",
        "checking_fallback",
        "scheduled",
        "reschedule_requested",
        "on_the_way",
        "in_progress",
        "completed",
        "awaiting_client",
        "approved",
        "cancelled",
        "disputed"
      ]
    },

    "request_sent_at": { "type": "string", "format": "date-time" },
    "request_expires_at": { "type": "string", "format": "date-time" },
    "cleaner_viewed_at": { "type": "string", "format": "date-time" },

    "client_confirmed": { "type": "boolean", "default": false },
    "cleaner_confirmed": { "type": "boolean", "default": false },

    "check_in_time": { "type": "string", "format": "date-time" },
    "check_out_time": { "type": "string", "format": "date-time" },
    "actual_hours": { "type": "number" },

    "photo_proof_submitted": { "type": "boolean", "default": false },
    "photo_count": { "type": "integer", "default": 0 },
    "review_submitted": { "type": "boolean", "default": false },
    "cancellation_timestamp": { "type": "string", "format": "date-time" },

    "reschedule_requested_by": { "type": "string", "enum": ["client", "cleaner"] },
    "reschedule_new_date": { "type": "string", "format": "date" },
    "reschedule_new_time": { "type": "string", "format": "time" },

    "snapshot_base_rate_cph": { "type": "number" },
    "snapshot_deep_addon_cph": { "type": "number" },
    "snapshot_moveout_addon_cph": { "type": "number" },
    "snapshot_additional_service_prices": {
      "type": "object",
      "additionalProperties": { "type": "number" }
    },

    "total_price": { "type": "number" },
    "escrow_credits_reserved": { "type": "number" },
    "final_charge_credits": { "type": "number" },
    "refund_credits": { "type": "number" },

    "payment_held": { "type": "boolean", "default": false },
    "payment_captured": { "type": "boolean", "default": false },
    "stripe_payment_intent_id": { "type": "string" },

    "payout_percentage_at_accept": { "type": "number" },

    "address_line1": { "type": "string" },
    "address_line2": { "type": "string" },
    "city": { "type": "string" },
    "state": { "type": "string" },
    "postal_code": { "type": "string" },

    "notes_for_cleaner": { "type": "string" },
    "notes_for_client": { "type": "string" }
  },
  "required": ["client_email", "date", "start_time", "estimated_hours", "status"]
}

WAt am i supposed to do with these json's? and the booking flow scheme ,

Great — let’s make this simple and actionable.
Right now, you’re asking:

“What am I supposed to DO with these JSON entities and the Booking Flow state machine?”

Here’s the clear, co-founder-level answer:

✅ What the JSON files are for
Base44 is a backend generator.
It builds:

Your database tables

Your API endpoints

Your CRUD operations

Your business objects

Your authorization rules

Your automated webhooks

ALL automatically, based on the JSON entity definitions you create.

🔥 So these JSON files = the blueprint for your entire backend.
When you add:

entities/Booking.json
entities/CleanerProfile.json
entities/ClientProfile.json
...
Base44 automatically creates:

✔ A SQL database
With all fields + types + relations.

✔ REST API endpoints
GET /booking

POST /booking

PATCH /booking/{id}

DELETE /booking/{id}

/booking/search

Filters, pagination, sorting, etc.

✔ Admin console UI (auto-built)
Full CRUD forms with validation.

✔ Automatic migrations
It will alter tables if you add/change fields.

✔ Automatic webhooks
For example:

When Booking.status changes → Base44 fires:
booking.status_changed event with JSON payload.

✔ Row-level-security enforcement
Cleaners only see their own bookings.
Clients only see theirs.
Admins see all.

🧩 What you actually need to DO now
Step 1 — Create entities in Base44
Go to:

/entities
and create:

Booking.json

CleanerProfile.json

ClientProfile.json

Credit.json

Payment.json

Payout.json

Review.json

PhotoPair.json

Dispute.json

RecurringBooking.json

(Optional ones: FavoriteCleaner, CleanerAnalytics, SupportTicket, etc.)

Paste in the JSON from my previous message.

Base44 will instantly generate the backend.

🧩 What the Booking Flow Schema is for
The Booking Flow Schema defines:

Each status

What transitions are allowed

What triggers them

What side-effects occur

What automation you need to implement

In Base44, this schema helps you build:

1. Automations
Inside Base44 → “Automations”

You will create rules like:

Example:
WHEN: Booking.status changes
FROM: "in_progress"
TO: "completed"
DO:

Calculate hours

Create Credit records

Update client balance

Generate Payment payout

Notify client

The schema I made is your blueprint for all these.

2. UI logic
Your frontend (Base44 pages) will use this to know:

When to show “Accept Job” button

When to show “Check In” button

When to allow cancellations

When to force photo uploads

For example:

If Booking.status = "in_progress"
Show:

Check-out button

Photo upload component

If Booking.status = "awaiting_client"
Show:

Approve button

Dispute button

3. Webhook routing
Base44 automatically fires:

booking.updated
booking.created
booking.deleted
booking.status_changed

Your state machine tells:

What payload matters

What actions you perform in n8n (if needed)

What notifications to send

What analytics to update

4. Stripe logic syncing
Your flow tells you:

When to hold funds

When to capture

When to refund

When to release payouts

📌 In Plain English:
The JSON files
Define your data & backend tables.

The Booking Flow State Machine
Defines your business rules & automations.

Together, they’re everything PureTask needs to operate.

/entities/YourEntity.json

Build tables

Build admin tools

2️⃣ Create the Booking Automation Rules
Inside Base44 automations:

Create rules like:

On Booking.created → run “reserve credits”

On Booking.accepted → lock cleaner rate snapshot

On Booking.completed → compute actual hours + credits

On Booking.awaiting_client → start 48-hour approval timer

On Booking.approved → release cleaner payouts

I can build all these for you step-by-step if you want.

3️⃣ Connect Stripe Keys
In Base44 settings, paste:

STRIPE_SECRET_KEY

STRIPE_WEBHOOK_SECRET

4️⃣ Create UI pages

Client booking page

These will use the entities you defined.

i thought base 44 already has the automations. can u explain wat your questions mean

Great question — and YES, Base44 does already contain many built-in automations, but there’s a very important distinction you need to understand so you don’t get confused:

✅ THE TRUTH: What Base44 automatically handles vs. what YOU must configure
Base44 gives you:

✔ Automatic backend
✔ Automatic SQL tables
✔ Automatic CRUD APIs
✔ Automatic webhooks/events
✔ Automatic entity relationships
✔ Automatic scheduling
✔ Automatic migrations
✔ Automatic authentication
✔ Automatic role-level security
✔ Automatic triggers when entities change
✔ Automatic logs, analytics, message delivery infrastructure
BUT…
Base44 does NOT magically know your business rules.

It does NOT know:

When a booking should move from "created" → "payment_hold"

When credits should be reserved

When Stripe should collect money

When a cleaner should be notified

When a job should be auto-cancelled

When to compute cleaner earnings

When to add a payout to a payout batch

When to release escrow credits

When to compute refunds

When to auto-approve after 48 hours

When to generate recurring jobs

When to update reliability

When to generate invoices or earnings entries

❗ These business rules must be added by YOU as logic in the Base44 Automations section.
🧩 SO WHAT ARE “AUTOMATIONS” IN BASE44?
Automations in Base44 are:

When X happens

And Y is true

Do Z (update another entity, send notification, run a payment action, etc.)

Example:

When a Booking is created
→ Reserve credits
→ Freeze rate snapshots
→ Create a PaymentIntent
→ Move Booking.status to "payment_hold"

Base44 does NOT automatically run that sequence for you — YOU configure it.

Base44 simply gives you:

Triggers (“on entity created”, “on field changed”…)

The ability to run actions (“update entity”, “call Stripe API”, “send email”, “modify credits”, etc.)

wat are the benifits of doing the blueprint model vs json model

Here’s the clean, co-founder level answer — Blueprint Model vs JSON Model in Base44 — what each one means, what each one gives you, and which one is better depending on the stage you’re at.

I’ll keep it direct and strategic so you can make the right call.

✅ WHAT BLUEPRINT VS JSON REALLY MEANS
Base44 automations can be built in two ways:

🟦 OPTION 1 — BLUEPRINT MODEL
(A human-readable specification of the entire automation system)

This is the version where I write:

When X happens

If Y is true

Then run Z actions

Very structured, very clear, organized like:

Trigger: Booking.status changed → "in_progress"
If: check_in_time exists AND cleaner_email is assigned
Do:
  - calculate duration
  - compute credits
  - update CleanerEarning
  - create CreditTransaction
  - notify client
This is readable, modifiable, and easy to follow.

✔ Benefits of Blueprint Model
1. You fully understand your own system
A blueprint is like an operations manual.

You can:

Edit rules

Combine logic

Add exceptions

Understand dependencies

Change behavior later

JSON is harder to read or reason about.

2. You can build inside Base44 UI without guesswork
You will:

Click “Create Automation”

Pick trigger

Add conditions

Add actions

Blueprint = The script you follow.

3. Easier to debug
If something breaks, you know why because you see the logic laid out cleanly.

With JSON, you’re staring at:

"action_blocks": [ ... ]
and hoping it makes sense.

4. Easier to extend for future features
New feature idea?
Just add a new rule to the blueprint.

5. You can move fast without breaking things
Blueprint is like a step-by-step checklist to implement in Base44 safely.

🟧 OPTION 2 — JSON MODEL
(The machine-readable automation exports Base44 uses internally)

This is the version where I generate long JSON structures representing:

triggers

conditions

entity updates

multi-step pipelines

Something like:

{
  "trigger": {
    "entity": "Booking",
    "event": "update",
    "fields": ["status"]
  },
  "conditions": [
    {
      "field": "status",
      "operator": "equals",
      "value": "completed"
    }
  ],
  "actions": [
    {
      "type": "update_entity",
      "entity": "CleanerEarning",
      "data": {
        "cleaner_email": "{{cleaner_email}}",
        "amount": "{{calculated_amount}}"
      }
    }
  ]
}
✔ Benefits of JSON Model
1. You can import in bulk (if Base44 supports it)
If you have 200 automations, JSON makes it possible to:

import them

clone them

version control them

2. Exact 1:1 representation
No ambiguity.
No misinterpretation.
What you see is what Base44 runs.

3. Good for later stages
When your system has:

lots of automation

staging vs production

automated deployments

📌 BUT — JSON HAS BIG RISKS EARLY ON
❗ JSON is much harder to edit
If:

flow changes

fields change

you add a booking status

you change payout math

You have to update hundreds of JSON entries manually.

❗ JSON makes it easy to break your entire system
A missing comma
A wrong field
A wrong entity reference

→ Entire flow breaks.

❗ JSON makes learning Base44 harder
You won’t fully understand your own business rules if you jump straight to JSON.

🧬 WHICH SHOULD YOU CHOOSE RIGHT NOW?
🔥 My recommendation (100% for your situation):
👉 BLUEPRINT FIRST
👉 JSON LATER (once the system stabilizes)
Here’s why:

You’re still exploring the full advanced mode stack

Blueprints let us design the full business logic perfectly

You can actually understand it

You can paste it into Base44 easily

Once the entire advanced system is built, THEN JSON becomes valuable

If we try JSON first:

You’ll drown in complexity

You won’t understand the system

You won’t know how to edit it

It becomes brittle and hard to modify

Blueprint is faster, safer, clearer.

JSON is powerful but dangerous for early-stage development.

🧱 FINAL RECOMMENDATION
✔ Start with: Blueprints (one module at a time)
✔ After all modules are built + tested:
I can then generate a JSON bundle of the entire automation layer.

This gives you:

🟦 Clarity first
🟧 Power later
And it ensures PureTask is stable, scalable, and understandable.

how do we check and see if base 44 already has these things

Totally fair question — this is exactly where things can get fuzzy if we just “trust” what some AI said about Base44 instead of actually verifying what your app is doing.

You asked:

How do we check and see if Base44 already has these things?

Let’s make this super concrete.

🔍 Big Idea: There are 3 layers to check
For any feature (escrow, payouts, smart match, reliability, etc.) you have to check:

Entities layer – Do we have the right tables/fields?

Automation layer – Is there a rule that does the work when something happens?

Behavior layer – If we run a test booking, does the expected thing actually happen?

You already showed me that the entities layer is stacked (Booking, CreditTransaction, CleanerEarning, Payment, Payout, etc.).

So now the real question is:
👉 Do automations exist?
👉 And do they actually run in reality?

Here’s how we check that, very practically.

1️⃣ Check if Base44 already has automations configured
In your Base44 app:

Open the Automations section
(usually something like: Automations / Flows / Rules in the Base44 dashboard)

Filter by entity

Look for automations where entity = Booking

Then where entity = CreditTransaction, CleanerEarning, Payment, Payout, etc.

For each automation, read:

Trigger:

e.g. “When Booking created”

“When Booking status changes”

Conditions:

e.g. new.status = "completed" and old.status != "completed"

Actions:

e.g. “Create CleanerEarning”

“Create CreditTransaction”

“Update ClientProfile.credits_balance”

“Send email using EmailTemplate X”

If you don’t see any automations tied to Booking, CreditTransaction, CleanerEarning, etc., then:

Base44 (the platform) has the power to do all this,
but your app configuration is not doing it yet.

So:

Entities = ✅ defined

Automations = ❓ maybe missing / partial

2️⃣ Run a live “what actually happens?” test
This is the most honest check.

Do this inside your app / Base44 admin:

Test 1: Booking lifecycle
Create a test client + test cleaner.

Create a test Booking with:

client_email

cleaner_email

date, start_time, estimated_hours, etc.

Manually update fields as if the flow is happening:

Set status = "created" → save

Then status = "payment_hold" → save

Then status = "awaiting_cleaner_response" → save

Then status = "accepted"

Then status = "scheduled"

Then status = "in_progress" with check_in_time

Then status = "completed" with check_out_time

Then status = "approved"

After each change, check the other entities:

CreditTransaction

Did a row get created for:

hold

charge

refund

Payment

Did a Payment get created?

Did status change from pending → completed?

CleanerEarning

When the Booking was approved, did a CleanerEarning row appear with:

credits_earned

payout_percentage

usd_due?

Payout

After some time / batch job, did that earning get moved into a Payout row?

👉 If those records appear automatically while you only change Booking, that means:

There are automations already wired.

👉 If nothing else changes, and only Booking updates:

You have entities, but no automation logic yet.

3️⃣ Check for specific features (per module)
Here’s how you check whether Base44 “already has” each advanced thing you listed.

🔧 A. Smart Cleaner Matching
Check:

Do you see automations that:

Trigger on DraftBooking or “booking started”

Query / filter cleaners based on:

distance (latitude/longitude)

CleanerProfile.reliability_score

tier

specialty tags

Set Booking.primary_cleaner_email and fallback_cleaners[]?

If no automations like this exist = smart match is designed for, but not implemented yet.

💸 B. PricingRule logic / surge / seasonal / occupancy
You already have an entity: PricingRule.

Check:

Are there automations that:

On booking creation / price calculation:

Read from PricingRule

Look at rule_type (time_of_day, day_of_week, surge, holiday, etc.)

Apply multiplier to some base price

Update DraftBooking.total_price or Booking.total_price?

If no automation reads PricingRule and writes to total_price:

Base44 supports advanced pricing (you modeled it)
but your pricing logic is not wired in yet.

📊 C. Reliability & CleanerAnalytics
You have:

CleanerProfile with many metrics

CleanerAnalytics for daily snapshots

ReliabilityBadge & CleanerMilestone

Check:

Are there automations where:

Trigger: Booking status changes to completed / approved, or Review created

Actions:

update CleanerProfile.reliability_score

update attendance_rate, punctuality_rate, no_show_rate, dispute_rate

insert or update CleanerAnalytics rows

create ReliabilityBadge or CleanerMilestone records?

If not: the data model is there, but the math & logic is not yet implemented.

📨 D. Messaging & Notifications
You have:

Message

ConversationThread

MessageDeliveryLog

EmailTemplate

Check:

Automations where:

Trigger: Booking / Payment / Dispute events

Action: create MessageDeliveryLog, send via template, etc.

If your app currently doesn’t send those automatically → logic is missing.

🧾 E. Disputes, Claims, Refund matrix
Entities exist:

Dispute

InsuranceClaim

CreditTransaction

Payment

Check for automations triggered by:

Booking.status set to disputed

InsuranceClaim created

Do they:

adjust credits

adjust payments

update reliability

notify parties?

If not → architecture is there, logic isn’t yet.

4️⃣ How to think about “does Base44 already have this?”
For each feature, you ask:

Is there an entity + fields for it?

Is there an automation that reacts to the right event?

When I run a test, does the correct data appear/ change automatically?

Only if all 3 are “yes”, you can say:

“Base44 already has this implemented for my app.”

Right now, from what we’ve seen:

Entities: ✅ very built out

Automations: ❓ unknown until you actually look in the Automations panel

Behavior: ❓ must be observed through test runs

🧩 Module 1 — Booking Engine Blueprint
(Assuming NO existing automations)

1. What the Booking Engine is responsible for
This module controls everything that happens to a job from the moment a client starts booking until the job is approved or disputed:

Booking creation & drafts

Cleaner selection & fallback cleaners

Response window + timeouts

Instant book vs request

Job day flow: on the way → check-in → in progress → check-out

Photo proof requirements

Completion & client approval

Cancellations, no-shows, reschedules

Dispute entry point

It does not yet define the detailed math for credits/payments/payouts (that’s Modules 2 & 3), but it does trigger those modules.

2. Key entities + fields this module uses
From your Base44 entities:

Booking
Key fields we’ll use:

client_email, cleaner_email, primary_cleaner_email, fallback_cleaners[]

matched_via_smart_algorithm, is_instant_book, subscription_id

date, start_time, hours, estimated_hours

cleaning_type (basic | deep | moveout)

additional_services{ windows, blinds, oven, refrigerator, ... }

insurance_purchased, insurance_amount

(We’ll assume a status field with the lifecycle from your earlier Base44 info doc: created, payment_hold, awaiting_cleaner_response, accepted, checking_fallback, scheduled, on_the_way, in_progress, completed, awaiting_client, approved, cancelled, disputed).

Other entities touched indirectly
ClientProfile – credits_balance, total_bookings

CleanerProfile – instant_book_enabled, availability, tier, reliability_score, etc.

DraftBooking – multi-step flow before final Booking creation

SupportTicket, Dispute, InsuranceClaim – for bad outcomes

Message, ConversationThread, MessageDeliveryLog, EmailTemplate – notifications & messaging

AnalyticsEvent – funnel tracking (start/abandon/submit booking)

3. High-level flows this module must handle
Booking creation flow

Client goes through DraftBooking steps → final Booking created.

Cleaner selection & request flow

Smart Match picks primary_cleaner_email + fallback_cleaners[].

Cleaner accepts/declines within response window.

Job day flow

Cleaner on the way → check-in → in progress → check-out.

Completion & client approval

Photos uploaded → job completed → client approves or disputes → auto-approve timeout.

Cancellations & no-shows

Client cancels (early/late), cleaner cancels, cleaner no-shows, client no-shows.

Dispute

Client (or cleaner) opens a dispute tied to a booking.

4. Automations — Blueprint (ADVANCED)
We’ll write these as “Automation #X” so you can implement them one by one in Base44.

A. Draft → Final Booking Creation
Automation 1 — Create Booking from DraftBooking

Trigger: DraftBooking updated

Condition:

current_step = final step (e.g. 4)

AND client clicks “Confirm & Book” in UI (we can model this as confirmed = true or a dedicated action)

Actions:

Create new Booking record with:

client info (email, address, home details, allergies, instructions) from DraftBooking

selected cleaner_email & fallback_cleaners[]

date, start_time, estimated_hours

cleaning_type, additional_services

total_price from DraftBooking.total_price

matched_via_smart_algorithm flag if applicable

Set Booking.status = "created".

Log AnalyticsEvent with event_type = "booking_submitted".

Optionally soft-delete or mark DraftBooking as converted.

This is where Module 2 (Payments) will hook in to reserve credits + create PaymentIntent on “created”.

B. Cleaner Request & Response Flow
Automation 2 — On Booking.created → send cleaner request or auto-accept

Trigger: Booking created

Condition:

is_instant_book = false

Actions:

Set Booking.status = "awaiting_cleaner_response".

Set request_sent_at = now, request_expires_at = now + X minutes (e.g. 20–30).

Create Message + MessageDeliveryLog to notify primary_cleaner_email (and maybe fallback as silent options).

Log Event with event_type = "booking_created".

Automation 3 — Instant Book path

Trigger: Booking created

Condition:

is_instant_book = true

AND selected cleaner has CleanerProfile.instant_book_enabled = true

Actions:

Set Booking.status = "accepted" & cleaner_email = primary_cleaner_email.

Set client_confirmed = true, cleaner_confirmed = true.

Immediately move to scheduled (Automation 4 below will formalize).

Automation 4 — When Booking moves to accepted → scheduled

Trigger: Booking updated

Condition:

old.status != "accepted" AND new.status = "accepted"

Actions:

Set status = "scheduled".

Ensure client_confirmed = true (client confirmed in UI when they completed booking).

Set cleaner_confirmed = true when cleaner accepted.

Send confirmation messages to both client & cleaner.

Increment ClientProfile.total_bookings by 1 (if first time, also set completed_first_booking=false still).

Automation 5 — Cleaner accepts / declines

These are driven by UI buttons in the cleaner app that update Booking status.

Accept flow:

Trigger: Booking updated

Condition: old.status = "awaiting_cleaner_response" AND new.status = "accepted"

Actions:

Run Automation 4 (move to scheduled, send confirmations)

Log Event: job_accepted_by_cleaner and AnalyticsEvent.

Decline flow:

Trigger: Booking updated

Condition: old.status = "awaiting_cleaner_response" AND new.status = "cleaner_declined"

Actions:

Increment decline-related metrics (Reliability module later).

Set status = "checking_fallback" to trigger fallback logic (Automation 6).

Automation 6 — Fallback cleaner auto-selection

Trigger: Booking updated

Condition: new.status = "checking_fallback"

Actions:

Take the next email from fallback_cleaners[] (not yet tried).

Set primary_cleaner_email = that fallback.

Set status = "awaiting_cleaner_response".

Reset request_sent_at, request_expires_at.

Notify that cleaner (Message + EmailTemplate).

Automation 7 — Response window timeout

Trigger: Scheduled/cron-style automation every few minutes OR event-based with request_expires_at.

Condition:

status = "awaiting_cleaner_response" AND now > request_expires_at.

Actions:

If more fallback cleaners exist → set status = "checking_fallback" (Automation 6 runs).

If no more cleaners:

Set status = "cancelled" with reason "no_cleaner_available".

Trigger refund logic in Credits/Payments module later.

Notify client that no cleaner was found.

C. Day-of-Job Automation (On the way → Check-in → In progress → Check-out)
Automation 8 — “On the way”

Trigger: Booking updated by cleaner action

Condition: old.status = "scheduled" AND new.status = "on_the_way"

Actions:

Log Event: "on_the_way".

Optional: start travel-time tracking (Analytics).

Automation 9 — Cleaner checks in → in_progress

Trigger: Booking updated by cleaner action

Condition:

old.status IN ("scheduled", "on_the_way")

AND new.status = "in_progress"

AND check_in_time set

Actions:

Set check_in_time = now if not already set.

Log Event: "check_in".

Reliability module later uses check_in_time vs start_time for punctuality.

Automation 10 — Cleaner checks out → completed

Trigger: Booking updated

Condition:

old.status = "in_progress"

AND new.status = "completed"

AND check_out_time set

Actions:

Ensure check_out_time = now if not set.

Compute actual_hours = (check_out_time - check_in_time) (rounded rules defined later).

Enforce photos: if PhotoPair count too low, either:

block transition (UI), or

set a flag photo_proof_missing = true.

Log Event: "check_out".

Then we immediately move into the client approval phase.

D. Completion → Client Approval & Auto-Approval
Automation 11 — Completed → awaiting_client

Trigger: Booking updated

Condition:

old.status = "completed" AND new.status = "awaiting_client"

Actions:

Notify client: “Your cleaning is ready to review” (email + push + in-app).

Log Event: "review_requested".

Store client_review_deadline = now + 48 hours (or your chosen window).

Automation 12 — Client approves → approved

Trigger: Booking updated

Condition:

old.status = "awaiting_client" AND new.status = "approved"

Actions:

Trigger Credits/Payments module:

finalize charge, release escrow, compute refunds, etc.

Create Review (if submitted) and feed into Reliability module.

Create CleanerEarning entry that Payment/Payout modules will aggregate later.

Update ClientProfile.completed_first_booking = true if applicable.

Notify cleaner: job approved + earnings available.

Automation 13 — Auto-approve timeout

Trigger: Scheduled automation that runs daily

Condition:

status = "awaiting_client" AND now > client_review_deadline.

Actions:

Set status = "approved" (auto-approved).

Mark auto_approved = true (add this field to Booking if not present).

Run the same actions as Automation 12 (settlement, earnings, notifications).

For Reliability, you may treat auto-approved slightly differently than explicit approval.

E. Cancellations & No-Shows
We’ll model cancel events via a cancellation_reason field added to Booking (client_cancel_early, client_cancel_late, cleaner_cancel, cleaner_no_show, client_no_show, system_no_match).

Automation 14 — Client cancels before match or far in advance

Trigger: Booking updated

Condition:

new.status = "cancelled"

AND cancellation_reason = "client_cancel_early"

Actions:

Trigger Credits/Payments module for full refund.

No penalty for cleaner.

Notify involved parties.

Automation 15 — Client late cancellation

Condition:

status = "scheduled" or "on_the_way"

cancellation_reason = "client_cancel_late"

Actions:

Trigger partial refund or no refund (Payment rules).

Possibly trigger partial payout to cleaner as compensation.

Log SupportTicket if threshold hit (frequent cancels).

Automation 16 — Cleaner cancels

Condition:

new.status = "cancelled"

cancellation_reason = "cleaner_cancel"

Actions:

Create SupportTicket or Dispute entry if severe.

Trigger Reliability module to penalize.

Trigger fallback matching (create a new Booking or rematch) OR cancel with full refund.

Automation 17 — Cleaner no-show

Trigger:

Scheduled job checks jobs where:

status still "scheduled" or "on_the_way"

now > start_time + grace_period

Actions:

Set status = "cancelled" with cancellation_reason = "cleaner_no_show".

Issue credits to client (CreditTransaction with reason "no_show").

Penalty to cleaner (Reliability module later).

Optionally auto-create Dispute or SupportTicket.

F. Disputes & Claims
Automation 18 — Client opens dispute from Booking

Trigger: Dispute created with a booking_id

Actions:

Set Booking.status = "disputed".

Pause payouts / cleaner earnings for this booking (Payment/Payout module).

Notify ops/admin.

Notify cleaner that dispute is opened.

Automation 19 — Dispute resolved

Trigger: Dispute updated

Condition:

old.status != "resolved" AND new.status = "resolved"

Actions:

Apply refund / credit logic from Dispute.refund_amount / credit_issued.

Update Booking.status:

approved but with dispute note, OR

cancelled with dispute outcome.

Update Reliability metrics (e.g. cleaner penalty if they were at fault).

Close any related SupportTicket.

🧩 MODULE 2 — PAYMENTS, CREDITS & ESCROW BLUEPRINT
1. What this module owns
This module decides what happens with money/credits when:

A booking is created

A booking is cancelled (early/late, client/cleaner/system)

A job is completed & approved

A job is disputed & refunded

A referral / promo / no-show credit is granted

It controls:

Wallet balance (ClientProfile.credits_balance)

The credit ledger (CreditTransaction)

Payments (Payment)

Earnings for cleaners (CleanerEarning)

The inputs to payouts (Payout)

Module 3 (Payout Engine) will take over where this stops.

2. Key entities & fields we’ll use
ClientProfile
user_email

credits_balance (number)

CreditTransaction (the ledger)
client_email

transaction_type: "purchase" | "hold" | "release" | "charge" | "refund" | "reversal"

amount_credits (signed: + added, – removed)

booking_id

note

balance_after

Payment
booking_id, client_email, cleaner_email

amount (total in USD)

platform_fee (USD)

cleaner_payout (USD)

status: "pending" | "completed" | "refunded" | "failed"

stripe_payment_intent_id

payment_method, paid_at

CleanerEarning
cleaner_email, booking_id

credits_earned

payout_percentage (0.80 / 0.85)

usd_due = (credits_earned / 10) * payout_percentage

status: "pending" | "batched" | "paid" | "reversed"

payout_id

Payout (Module 3 will use this heavily)
cleaner_email, amount, payout_type (weekly / instant)

status

stripe_transfer_id, booking_ids[]

Credit (for simple promo/no_show buckets)
client_email, amount, reason: "no_show" | "promotion", booking_id, used

We’ll treat:

CreditTransaction = authoritative ledger + balance

ClientProfile.credits_balance = cached view of latest ledger value

3. Important money concepts
We’ll define a few concepts (these are logic-level, not new entities):

Wallet credits:

10 credits ≈ $1 (based on CleanerEarning.usd_due formula).

Estimated job cost:

Calculated from Module 4 (Pricing), but for this module we assume Booking has some total_price_credits or we can derive from hours + cleaner rates.

Escrow:

On booking, we HOLD credits from the client’s wallet.

On approval, we CHARGE the final amount and REFUND leftover.

On cancellation/dispute, we adjust with release / refund / reversal.

4. Core flows this module must support
Wallet top-up (credits purchase via Stripe)

Escrow hold when booking is created

Release/refund when booking is cancelled

Finalize charge when job approved

Create cleaner earnings when job approved

Adjustments from disputes/claims

Promo / referral / no-show credits

Now we’ll convert these into concrete automations.

5. Automations — Blueprint
A. WALLET TOP-UP (Credits Purchase)
Automation 2.1 — On successful payment → create CreditTransaction (purchase)

There are 2 ways to model Stripe in Base44; we’ll keep it simple:
Stripe webhook (outside) updates or creates a Payment with status = "completed".

Trigger: Payment updated

Condition:

old.status != "completed"

new.status = "completed"

booking_id is null/empty → this is a wallet top-up rather than booking-specific.

Actions:

Compute credits_purchased = amount * 10.

Read last CreditTransaction for that client_email to get previous balance_after (or use ClientProfile.credits_balance).

Create new CreditTransaction:

client_email = Payment.client_email

transaction_type = "purchase"

amount_credits = +credits_purchased

booking_id = null

note = "Wallet top-up via Stripe"

balance_after = previous_balance + credits_purchased

Update ClientProfile.credits_balance = balance_after.

Result: Wallet is funded; Payment row tracks the actual card charge, ledger tracks credits.

B. ESCROW HOLD WHEN BOOKING IS CREATED
We’ll extend Module 1 behavior:

When Booking is created and passes payment checks → we hold credits.

Automation 2.2 — On Booking.created → place credits on hold

Trigger: Booking created

Condition:

Booking is not free (i.e., estimated_hours > 0)

Client has enough credits: ClientProfile.credits_balance >= required_credits

Actions:

Calculate required_credits based on pricing:

For now: required_credits = Booking.estimated_hours * cleaner_base_rate_credits_per_hour + add-ons
(Later Module 4 will give an exact formula.)

Fetch previous balance from ClientProfile.credits_balance (or last CreditTransaction).

Create CreditTransaction:

transaction_type = "hold"

amount_credits = -required_credits (negative = temporarily removed from available)

booking_id = Booking.id

note = "Escrow hold for booking"

balance_after = previous_balance - required_credits

Update ClientProfile.credits_balance = balance_after.

Create Payment row with:

booking_id, client_email, cleaner_email (if assigned), status = "pending".

amount in USD ≈ required_credits / 10.

(If you want Stripe pre-auth for backup): create a PaymentIntent for fallback if credits are insufficient.

Now credits are “locked” for this job, but not yet fully spent.

C. CANCELLATIONS & REFUNDS (Refund Matrix)
We’ll define a simple, configurable matrix (you can tweak numbers later):

Scenario	Who pays / keeps what (credits)
system_no_match	Full release of hold to client
client_cancel_early	Full release of hold to client
client_cancel_late	Charge 30% of held amount, release 70%
cleaner_cancel	Full release to client, penalty to cleaner later
cleaner_no_show	Full release + bonus credits to client
client_no_show	Charge 50–100% (policy choice)
We’ll assume Booking.cancellation_reason exists (we can add via Booking schema if needed).

Shared Helper: Release + Charge
When we say:

“Release” = CreditTransaction with transaction_type = "release", amount_credits = +X

“Charge” = CreditTransaction with transaction_type = "charge", amount_credits = -X

And always recompute balance_after and update ClientProfile.credits_balance.

Automation 2.3 — System no-match / early client cancel → full release

Trigger: Booking updated

Condition:

new.status = "cancelled"

cancellation_reason IN ("system_no_match", "client_cancel_early")

Actions:

Look up the original hold transaction H for this booking:

transaction_type = "hold", booking_id = Booking.id.

If found:

Create CreditTransaction:

transaction_type = "release"

amount_credits = +H.amount_credits * -1 (reverse of negative hold)

booking_id = Booking.id

note = "Full release of held credits"

balance_after = previous_balance + released_amount

Update ClientProfile.credits_balance = balance_after.

Update related Payment:

If no card captured: leave as status = "failed" or cancelled.

If card was involved: mark as status = "refunded" (Stripe logic later).

Automation 2.4 — Client late cancellation → partial charge

Trigger: Booking updated

Condition:

new.status = "cancelled"

cancellation_reason = "client_cancel_late"

Actions:

Fetch original hold H as above.

Define percentages (configurable):

charge_pct = 0.30 (30%)

release_pct = 0.70 (70%)

Compute:

to_charge = |H.amount_credits| * charge_pct

to_release = |H.amount_credits| * release_pct

Create two CreditTransactions:

Charge:

transaction_type = "charge"

amount_credits = -to_charge

note = "Late cancellation fee"

Release:

transaction_type = "release"

amount_credits = +to_release

note = "Release unused hold after late cancellation"

balance_after should end at previous_balance - to_charge.

Update ClientProfile.credits_balance.

Update Payment:

amount = (to_charge / 10)

status = "completed" once Stripe captures that partial amount.

Later, CleanerEarning & Payout module can decide whether cleaner gets a part of this fee.

Automation 2.5 — Cleaner cancel / no-show

Trigger: Booking updated

Condition:

new.status = "cancelled"

cancellation_reason IN ("cleaner_cancel", "cleaner_no_show")

Actions:

Full release of held credits, same as Automation 2.3.

Additionally, if cancellation_reason = "cleaner_no_show":

Create Credit record:

reason = "no_show"

amount = bonus credits (e.g. 200)

booking_id = Booking.id

used = false

Also create CreditTransaction "promotion" or "refund" with positive amount to reflect this bonus in ledger.

No Payment is charged to client.

Cleaner penalty handled in Reliability module.

Automation 2.6 — Client no-show

Trigger: Booking updated

Condition:

new.status = "cancelled"

cancellation_reason = "client_no_show"

Actions:

Fetch hold H.

Decide policy (example: charge 80%):

to_charge = |H.amount_credits| * 0.8

to_release = |H.amount_credits| * 0.2

Create CreditTransaction charge + release like in 2.4.

Set Payment.amount = to_charge / 10, Payment.status = "completed" when Stripe capture happens.

CleanerEarning module later gives a portion of this to cleaner.

D. JOB APPROVED → FINAL CHARGE + REFUND + EARNINGS
When job is approved (client or auto-approve), we:

Convert hold to a real charge

Refund any difference (if estimated > actual)

Create CleanerEarning

Finalize Payment

Automation 2.7 — On Booking.approved → settle credits & payment

Trigger: Booking updated

Condition:

old.status = "awaiting_client"

new.status = "approved"

Actions:

1) Compute final job price in credits

Use Module 4 pricing formula, but simplified blueprint:

base = actual_hours * cleaner_base_rate_credits_per_hour

Add-ons: from additional_services (windows, oven, etc) using CleanerProfile.additional_service_pricing.

final_credits = base + add_ons

2) Compare vs hold

Fetch original hold transaction H:

held_credits = |H.amount_credits|

If final_credits < held_credits:

refund_credits = held_credits - final_credits

Else:

refund_credits = 0

(Or optionally additional charge if final > hold)

3) Create charge transaction

Create CreditTransaction:

transaction_type = "charge"

amount_credits = -final_credits

booking_id = Booking.id

note = "Final charge for completed booking"

4) Release leftover from hold

If refund_credits > 0:

Create CreditTransaction:

transaction_type = "release"

amount_credits = +refund_credits

booking_id = Booking.id

note = "Release unused held credits"

5) Compute new balance_after

Start from previous balance before these 2 transactions.

Net effect vs original balance = -(final_credits) (the true cost).

Update ClientProfile.credits_balance = balance_after.

6) Update Payment

Payment.amount = final_credits / 10 (USD)

Split:

platform_fee = Payment.amount * 0.15 (example)

cleaner_payout = Payment.amount * 0.85

Set:

status = "completed"

paid_at = now

Capture Stripe PaymentIntent for Payment.amount if you used card as backup.

7) Create CleanerEarning

Lookup CleanerProfile.payout_percentage (0.80 or 0.85).

Create CleanerEarning:

cleaner_email = Booking.cleaner_email

booking_id = Booking.id

credits_earned = final_credits * CleanerProfile.payout_percentage (?)

Or: credits_earned = final_credits and payout_percentage defines USD conversion.

payout_percentage = CleanerProfile.payout_percentage

usd_due = (credits_earned / 10) * payout_percentage

status = "pending"

8) Trigger Payout module later

Module 3 will batch all CleanerEarning.status = "pending" into Payout.

E. DISPUTES / CLAIMS IMPACT ON MONEY
When a dispute or insurance claim resolves, we may:

Refund some/all of client’s credits

Reverse part/all of cleaner’s earnings

Adjust Payment status

Automation 2.8 — Dispute resolved → apply refund/credit

Trigger: Dispute updated

Condition:

old.status != "resolved"

new.status = "resolved"

Actions:

If refund_amount > 0:

Compute refund_credits = refund_amount * 10.

Create CreditTransaction:

transaction_type = "refund"

amount_credits = +refund_credits

booking_id = Dispute.booking_id

note = "Refund from dispute resolution"

Update ClientProfile.credits_balance.

If credit_issued > 0 in Dispute:

Also create a "promotion" / "refund" type CreditTransaction with positive amount.

Update Payment.status:

If full refund → "refunded"

If partial → stays "completed", but maybe track refunded_amount (add field).

Optionally:

Find CleanerEarning for this booking:

If cleaner found at fault, reduce usd_due and set status = "reversed" for that portion.

Module 3 will ensure it isn’t paid or is clawed back.

F. PROMOS, REFERRALS, MEMBERSHIP CREDITS
You already have:

Referral, ClientReferral with reward amounts.

ClientMembership with benefits.

Automation 2.9 — Referral completed → award credits

Trigger: ClientReferral updated

Condition:

old.status != "rewarded"

new.status = "rewarded"

Actions:

Create CreditTransaction for referrer_email:

transaction_type = "purchase" or "promotion"

amount_credits = reward_amount_credits

note = "Referral reward"

Update their credits_balance.

Optionally, same for referee_discount_credits.

Automation 2.10 — Monthly membership benefit → auto credits

Trigger: Scheduled (monthly)

Condition:

ClientMembership.status = "active"

Actions:

Determine monthly credits benefit (config in ClientMembership.benefits).

Create CreditTransaction:

transaction_type = "promotion"

amount_credits = membership_credits

note = "Membership monthly credits"

Update ClientProfile.credits_balance.

6. How Module 2 ties to Module 1 & Module 3
Module 1 (Booking Engine):

Triggers:

Booking.created → Automation 2.2 (hold)

Booking.cancelled → Automations 2.3–2.6 (release/charge)

Booking.approved → Automation 2.7 (final charge & earning)

Dispute.status = "resolved" → Automation 2.8

Module 3 (Payout Engine):

Will consume:

CleanerEarning.status = "pending" and usd_due

Aggregate into Payout

Trigger Stripe transfers

Update CleanerEarning.status to "paid" and fill payout_id

If this all looks good, next step is:

You can start implementing some of these automations in Base44.

Or we can move on to Module 3 — Payout Engine Blueprint so the money flow from CleanerEarning → Payout → Stripe is fully specified.

If you’re ready, just say:

“Move on to Module 3 — Payout Engine.”


WILL U REVIEW AND ANALYZE MODULE 2 FOR ANY MISTAKES.

Short answer:
Module 2 is conceptually solid (flows all make sense), but there are a few important mistakes / misalignments we should fix so it matches your actual Base44 schema + credit escrow logic.

I’ll walk through the key issues and how to correct them.

1️⃣ Biggest issue: double-charging the client (hold + charge math)
Where it’s wrong:

In my original Module 2, I said:

On booking: create a hold transaction (−H credits).

On approval: create a charge (−F credits) and a release of only the leftover amount.

That math is wrong if we also keep the original hold in the ledger.

Example:

Estimated/held = H = 1000 credits

Final charge = F = 800 credits

I suggested:

T_hold = −1000

T_charge = −800

T_release = +200

Net = −1000 − 800 + 200 = −1600 (client overcharged 2× final amount).

So: we must NOT keep the original hold “active” AND apply charge+partial release on top.

✅ Two safe patterns
We need to pick one of these patterns and stick to it:

Pattern A – “Release full hold, then charge final” (cleanest)
On booking:

T_hold: transaction_type = "hold", amount_credits = -H

On approval:

T_release_full: amount_credits = +H

T_charge_final: amount_credits = -F

Net effect = −H + H − F = −F ✅

This is mathematically clean and easy to debug.

Pattern B – “Don’t log hold in ledger, only use Booking + balance”
This actually matches how your Base44 info describes escrow:

Booking.escrow_credits_reserved tracks the hold

ClientProfile.credits_balance is temporarily reduced

Credit entity (or CreditTransaction) is only used to log refunds / promotions, not the initial hold.

In that model:

On booking:

Decrease ClientProfile.credits_balance -= H

Set Booking.escrow_credits_reserved = H

No Credit/CreditTransaction row for the hold.

On approval:

Set Booking.final_charge_credits = F

Set Booking.refund_credits = H - F

Only record refund (H−F) as a Credit/CreditTransaction entry.

This matches the line:

“refund_credits … returned … (and logged in the Credit entity)”

👉 My Module 2 assumed Pattern A but didn’t fully implement it, so the math was inconsistent.
We need to either:

Commit to Pattern A and always fully release the hold before charging; or

Simplify and use Pattern B (no hold in ledger, only in Booking+balance).

Given your docs talk about escrow_credits_reserved, final_charge_credits, refund_credits on Booking and Credit entity as the ledger, the most aligned path is:

Use Booking for escrow + balance changes, and use Credit/CreditTransaction ONLY for refunds/promos/etc.

We should adjust Module 2 that way.

2️⃣ Credit vs CreditTransaction — which is the actual “ledger”?
From your schema:

CreditTransaction has:

transaction_type (purchase, hold, release, charge, refund, reversal)

amount_credits (signed)

balance_after

Credit has:

amount, reason (no_show, promotion), used

Explanation in docs calls Credit “The ledger”.

So there’s a tiny inconsistency between:

The entities file (which clearly defines CreditTransaction as a rich ledger), and

The narrative doc (which describes Credit as “the ledger”).

✅ Suggested fix
To avoid confusion, I recommend:

Treat CreditTransaction as the canonical ledger (it has the right fields).

Treat Credit as a simple “credit grant” convenience entity (promos, no_show, etc.) that can be reflected into CreditTransaction.

So we tweak Module 2 to:

Use CreditTransaction for all adds/subtracts to the wallet (purchases, refunds, adjustments).

Optionally mirror certain events (like no-show credit grants) into Credit as a human-friendly record.

My original Module 2 blueprint started to do that, but it also mixed in hold events and double-counted them. That’s what we’re cleaning up.

3️⃣ Not using Booking’s financial fields that already exist
Your Booking entity already has:

escrow_credits_reserved

final_charge_credits

refund_credits

payment_held, payment_captured

payout_percentage_at_accept

My initial Module 2 blueprint re-derived values from rates & hours and didn’t explicitly:

Set Booking.escrow_credits_reserved on hold

Set Booking.final_charge_credits & Booking.refund_credits on approval

Use payout_percentage_at_accept directly from Booking for earnings (instead I grabbed it from CleanerProfile)

✅ Correct alignment
We should change Module 2 to:

On booking creation:

Calculate estimated cost once (from snapshot fields or CleanerProfile)

Set Booking.escrow_credits_reserved = estimated_credits

Deduct that from ClientProfile.credits_balance.

On approval:

Set Booking.final_charge_credits = final_credits

Set Booking.refund_credits = Booking.escrow_credits_reserved - final_credits

Use Booking.final_charge_credits + Booking.payout_percentage_at_accept to compute Payment.cleaner_payout and/or CleanerEarning.usd_due.

That matches your doc exactly and avoids re-snapshotting stuff at approval.

4️⃣ Payment / Stripe flags not wired in
The docs say:

Booking stores stripe_payment_intent_id

Payment stores amount, status, stripe_payment_intent_id, and flags like payment_held, payment_captured.

My Module 2 blueprint talked about Stripe conceptually but didn’t explicitly tie:

Booking.payment_held / payment_captured

Payment.status transitions

We should correct it to:

When credits escrow is placed & (optionally) Stripe pre-auth is created:

Booking.payment_held = true

Payment.status = "pending"

When job is approved and we’re ready to charge:

Call Stripe to capture (via webhook/automation)

On successful capture:

Booking.payment_captured = true

Payment.status = "completed"

Payment.paid_at = now

This doesn’t change the high-level flow, but it’s important for correctness.

✅ Good / fine parts of Module 2
Flow structure:

Wallet top-up flow

Escrow on booking

Cancellation matrix (early/late, cleaner/client)

Entity choices:

Escrow fields on Booking (escrow_credits_reserved, final_charge_credits, refund_credits) weren’t explicitly wired into the flows.

Trigger: Payment.status changes
Condition:

new.status = "completed"

AND Payment.booking_id = null (wallet top-up)

transaction_type = "purchase"

amount_credits = +credits_purchased

balance_after = prev_balance + credits_purchased

Wallet is increased. No booking involved.

(Corrected version — no ledger entry for the hold)

Trigger: Booking.created

(Use Pricing Module output when ready):

estimated_credits = Booking.estimated_hours * base_rate + add_ons

Ensure wallet has enough credits:

If not enough → fail booking or require top-up.

Deduct from wallet without creating a ledger transaction:

ClientProfile.credits_balance -= estimated_credits

Store escrow amount on Booking:

Booking.escrow_credits_reserved = estimated_credits

payment_held = true

Create Payment record:

status = "pending"

amount = estimated_credits / 10 (USD preview)

stripe_payment_intent_id (optional pre-auth)

This matches your Base44 escrow logic exactly.

SECTION C — CANCELLATIONS & REFUND MATRIX
(Corrected to avoid double entries & using Booking fields)

We will always:

Reference Booking.escrow_credits_reserved (H)

Decide how much to release to the client

Decide how much to convert into charge (if late cancel)

No ledger entry is made for the escrow deduction, only for release/refunds/charges.

Scenario 1 — Early cancel / No cleaner found
→ Full release

🌟 Automation 2.3 — Booking cancelled early / no_match → Full release
Trigger: Booking.status = "cancelled"
Condition:

cancellation_reason IN ("client_cancel_early", "system_no_match")

Add ledger entry:

amount_credits = +H

note = "Full release of escrow"

Update wallet:

Set booking:

refund_credits = H

payment_captured = false

Payment:

If Stripe pre-auth existed → cancel intent.

Otherwise leave Payment as cancelled.

Scenario 2 — Client late cancellation
→ Partial fee charged, remainder refunded

🌟 Automation 2.4 — Late cancel → charge X%, refund Y%
Trigger: Booking.status = "cancelled"
Condition: cancellation_reason = "client_cancel_late"

Actions:

Let H = escrow amount.
Say charge_pct = 30% (configurable).
Then:

charge_credits = H * 0.30
refund_credits = H * 0.70
Add ledger entries:

Charge:

transaction_type = "charge"

amount_credits = -charge_credits

Refund:

transaction_type = "refund"

amount_credits = +refund_credits

Update wallet:

Net effect = H * (0.70 - 1) = −charge_credits

So:
ClientProfile.credits_balance += refund_credits

Update Booking:

final_charge_credits = charge_credits

refund_credits = refund_credits

Payment:

Payment.amount = charge_credits / 10

Stripe capture happens now

Payment.status = "completed"

Scenario 3 — Cleaner cancels / Cleaner no-show
→ Full refund AND compensation to client

🌟 Automation 2.5 — Cleaner cancel / no-show
Trigger: Booking.status = "cancelled"
Condition:

cancellation_reason IN ("cleaner_cancel", "cleaner_no_show")

Actions:

Let H = escrow amount.

Refund full escrow:

CreditTransaction.refund = +H

Booking.refund_credits = H

Add a bonus credit:

e.g., bonus = 200

transaction_type = "promotion"

amount_credits = +bonus

note = "Cleaner no-show compensation"

Payment:

No charge

Stripe pre-auth cancelled

Payment.status = "cancelled"

Scenario 4 — Client no-show
→ Cleaner compensation & platform fee

charge_credits = H * 0.80
refund_credits = H * 0.20

Refund: +refund_credits

Wallet:
ClientProfile.credits_balance += refund_credits

To be handled in Module 3 (e.g., cleaner gets 50% of charge_credits).

SECTION D — JOB APPROVED → FINAL CHARGE
🌟 Automation 2.7 — On Booking.approved → settle final charge & refund
Trigger: Booking.status = "approved"

Actions:

Let:

H = escrow amount (Booking.escrow_credits_reserved)

F = final job cost (computed via Pricing Engine Module 4)

Compute:

Ledger entry:

transaction_type = "refund"

amount_credits = +refund_credits

Wallet:

ClientProfile.credits_balance += refund_credits

amount_credits = -additional_charge

Wallet:

refund_credits = refund_credits

payment_captured = true

payment_held = false

platform_fee = Payment.amount * 0.15

Capture stripe intent

cleaner_email = Booking.cleaner_email

booking_id = Booking.id

credits_earned = F

payout_percentage = Booking.payout_percentage_at_accept

usd_due = (F / 10) * payout_percentage

status = "pending"

transaction_type = "refund"

🧩 MODULE 3 — PAYOUT ENGINE BLUEPRINT (ADVANCED MODE)
1. What Module 3 is responsible for
This module owns all money flowing to cleaners:

Turning CleanerEarning rows (from Module 2) into payouts

Grouping earnings into weekly batches

Handling instant payouts

Calling Stripe transfers

Handling failed payouts

Supporting reversals (from disputes / clawbacks)

Feeding tax / reporting & analytics

You can think of it like:

Module 2 = “What does the client pay & how much did cleaner earn?”
Module 3 = “When/how does the cleaner actually get paid out?”

2. Key Entities & Fields
From your Base44 entities (names may differ slightly, but conceptually):

CleanerEarning
cleaner_email

booking_id

credits_earned

payout_percentage

usd_due

status: "pending" | "batched" | "paid" | "reversed" | "failed"

payout_id (nullable)

created_date

Created in Module 2 when booking is approved.

Payout
cleaner_email

booking_ids[]

amount_cents (total Payout amount)

payout_type: "weekly" | "instant"

status: "pending" | "processing" | "completed" | "failed" | "cancelled"

stripe_transfer_id

batch_start_date, batch_end_date (for weekly)

created_date

Stripe / External
Stripe Connect transfer (to cleaner’s connected account)

Transfer status mirrored back into Payout.status

3. High-Level Payout Lifecycle
For each cleaner:

Jobs get approved → Module 2 creates CleanerEarning (pending)

Payout Engine:

Weekly: batches all pending earnings into a Payout on a schedule

Instant: cleaner can tap “Cash Out Now” to create a Payout on demand

Stripe transfer is initiated

When Stripe confirms:

Payout.status = "completed"

Linked CleanerEarning rows become paid

If things fail:

Payout.status = "failed"

Earnings go back to pending for retry

If we reverse earnings (dispute etc.), they’re excluded from future payouts or clawed back.

4. Core Rules / Policies
These are config values you can tweak later, but we’ll assume:

Weekly payout day: Friday

Cutoff time: Thursday 23:59 in cleaner’s timezone (simplify: server midnight)

Minimum payout threshold: $20 (2,000 credits)

Instant payout fee: 1–2% (optional)

Payout currency: USD (Stripe side)

5. Automations — Payout Engine Blueprint
We’ll label them 3.x to keep consistent with Modules 1 & 2.

A. After Booking Approved → Ensure CleanerEarning is “pending”
This is mostly Module 2, but Module 3 depends on it being correct.

Automation 3.1 — On Booking.approved → verify CleanerEarning

(You may already do this in Module 2, but we include it for clarity.)

Trigger: Booking.status changes to "approved"

Condition:

No existing CleanerEarning for this booking_id

Actions:

Create CleanerEarning with:

cleaner_email = Booking.cleaner_email

booking_id = Booking.id

credits_earned = Booking.final_charge_credits * Booking.payout_percentage_at_accept OR use the simpler pattern: credits_earned = Booking.final_charge_credits and let payout_percentage only affect usd_due.

payout_percentage = Booking.payout_percentage_at_accept

usd_due = (Booking.final_charge_credits / 10) * payout_percentage

status = "pending"

Result: every approved job creates a “pending earning” entry for that cleaner.

B. Weekly Payout Batching
This is the core of Module 3.

Automation 3.2 — Weekly payout run (batch earnings → Payout)

Trigger: Scheduled (e.g., every Friday at 09:00)

For each cleaner_email:

Select eligible earnings:

CleanerEarning.status = "pending"

created_date <= cutoff_date (e.g., end of previous day)

Sum:

total_usd = SUM(usd_due)

total_cents = round(total_usd * 100)

If below threshold, skip:

If total_usd < MIN_PAYOUT_USD (e.g., 20) → do nothing (leave them pending).

If enough to pay:

Create a Payout:

cleaner_email

booking_ids = [list of booking_ids from these earnings]

amount_cents = total_cents

payout_type = "weekly"

status = "pending"

batch_start_date, batch_end_date = min/max created_date in earnings

Link earnings to payout:

For each CleanerEarning included:

set status = "batched"

set payout_id = new_payout.id

Result: each cleaner gets at most one weekly payout row containing many bookings.

C. Instant Payouts (“Cash out now”)
Assume the cleaner front-end calls an action like “Request Instant Payout”. That might set a flag or call a Base44 endpoint that creates a record.

We’ll model it as: cleaner triggers an action we represent as an InstantPayoutRequest or directly as an automation on command.

Automation 3.3 — Instant Payout request → create Payout

Trigger: Custom action / Mutation (e.g., Cleaner requests instant payout)

Condition:

Cleaner has enough pending earnings:

SUM(pending.usd_due) >= MIN_INSTANT_PAYOUT_USD (maybe same as weekly or lower)

Actions:

Compute instant_total_usd and instant_total_cents.

Optionally compute fee:

fee_pct = 0.02 (2%)

fee_cents = instant_total_cents * fee_pct

net_cents = instant_total_cents - fee_cents

Create Payout:

cleaner_email

booking_ids = [ids of included jobs]

amount_cents = net_cents

payout_type = "instant"

status = "pending"

Link CleanerEarning rows:

status = "batched"

payout_id = Payout.id

Optionally create a PlatformFee or adjust Payment to represent instant payout fee.

Now instant payouts behave like small, ad-hoc weekly payouts.

D. Initiating Stripe Transfers
You can either:

Have Base44 directly call Stripe when Payout is created, or

Use webhooks + external worker.

We’ll blueprint it as Base44 calling Stripe:

Automation 3.4 — On Payout.created (pending) → initiate Stripe transfer

Trigger: Payout.created

Condition: Payout.status = "pending"

Actions:

Call Stripe Connect Transfer API:

Amount = Payout.amount_cents

Destination = cleaner’s Stripe account (stored on CleanerProfile.stripe_account_id)

If API call succeeds:

Set Payout.status = "processing"

Store stripe_transfer_id

If API call fails:

Set Payout.status = "failed"

Write error reason to Payout.error_message (add field)

E. Handling Stripe Webhook / Transfer Result
Stripe will send webhooks like transfer.paid, transfer.failed.
You store those in a StripeEvent or directly update Payout.

Automation 3.5 — On Stripe webhook → update Payout status

Trigger: StripeEvent or direct webhook integration updating Payout

Conditions & Actions:

If event = transfer.paid:

Find Payout by stripe_transfer_id

Set status = "completed"

If event = transfer.failed:

Set status = "failed"

Store error details

F. Completing Cleaner Earnings on Successful Payout
Once Payout is completed, we finalize the CleanerEarning rows.

Automation 3.6 — On Payout.completed → mark earnings as paid

Trigger: Payout.status changes to "completed"

Actions:

For all CleanerEarning where payout_id = this Payout.id:

Set status = "paid"

Log AnalyticsEvent:

type = "payout_completed"

metadata = { cleaner_email, amount_cents, booking_count }

Notify cleaner:

“Your payout of $X has been sent to your bank account.”

Result:

No more money owed for these bookings.

Reporting & tax totals can treat these as final.

G. Handling Failed Payouts
If Stripe or bank rejects the transfer, we must handle it gracefully.

Automation 3.7 — On Payout.failed → return earnings to pending

Trigger: Payout.status changes to "failed"

Actions:

For all CleanerEarning with payout_id = this.id:

Set status = "pending"

Set payout_id = null (so they can be re-batched later)

Notify admin:

Create SupportTicket or log with type “payout_failure”.

Notify cleaner:

“We couldn’t process your payout, please update your bank/Stripe details.”

We do not double-credit or double-charge anything; we just put earnings back into the pool to retry later.

H. Reversals / Dispute Clawbacks
In Module 2, we said:

When Dispute resolves and cleaner is at fault → we may reduce or reverse their earnings.

We need payout logic for:

If earnings are still pending / batched, but not yet paid

If they already have been paid (more complex, but we’ll set up structure)

Case 1 — Earning not paid yet
Automation 3.8 — Dispute resolved before payout → reduce CleanerEarning

Trigger: Dispute.status = "resolved"

Condition:

CleanerEarning for that booking_id exists

AND CleanerEarning.status IN ("pending", "batched") (i.e., not paid yet)

Actions:

Determine clawback_usd (from Dispute resolution logic).

Reduce CleanerEarning.usd_due by clawback_usd.

If usd_due becomes 0 or negative:

Set CleanerEarning.status = "reversed"

(Optionally set reversed_reason)

If it was batched, also:

Reduce Payout.amount_cents for that payout accordingly.

This keeps us from ever paying out money we later decided to claw back.

Case 2 — Earning already paid
This is trickier, usually handled as future offsets (deduct from future payouts).

Automation 3.9 — Dispute resolved after payout → offset future payouts

Trigger: Dispute.status = "resolved"

Condition:

CleanerEarning.status = "paid" for that booking_id

Actions:

Determine clawback_usd and convert to cents.

Create a negative CleanerEarning entry:

usd_due = -clawback_usd

credits_earned = negative equivalent

status = "pending"

note = "dispute_clawback"

Future weekly payout will see this negative earning and reduce the payout amount.

This lets you claw back over time instead of trying to pull money from the bank immediately.

6. Tax & Reporting Hooks (Blueprint)
We won’t implement full tax logic here, but you’ll want:

A CleanerTaxProfile or fields on CleanerProfile:

tax_id, w9_completed, country, etc.

SUM(usd_due) for all CleanerEarning.status = "paid" in year

Can be exported for 1099s, etc.

Automations:

CleanerAnalytics.total_earnings_cents += Payout.amount_cents

Keep monthly/weekly rollups.
