WILL U REVIEW AND ANALZYE MODULE 3 FOR MISTAKES

You’re right to sanity-check this one — payouts are where bugs hurt most 😅
I went back through Module 3 + your Base44 schema/docs and here’s the honest review.

1️⃣ Big picture: is Module 3 basically correct?
Yes:

It correctly treats CleanerEarning → Payout → Stripe transfer as the pipeline.

It matches your docs that say: Booking.final_charge_credits + payout_percentage_at_accept → cleaner share → aggregated into Payout entities.

It uses your actual Payout statuses (pending, processing, completed, failed) and types (weekly, instant).

So structurally it’s solid. The issues are detail-level alignment with your schema / math.

2️⃣ Issue #1 — CleanerEarning.status values
Your CleanerEarning enum is:

"pending" | "batched" | "paid" | "reversed"

In my Module 3 write-up I:

Used those 4 correctly most of the time, but

Once implied an extra status "failed" for CleanerEarning (not allowed by schema).

🛠 Fix:

CleanerEarning must only ever use one of:

pending

batched

paid

reversed

If a payout fails, we:

Set Payout.status = "failed" (that enum allows it)

Put associated CleanerEarning rows back to status = "pending", payout_id = null (as I already described in Automation 3.7).

No CleanerEarning.status = "failed" anywhere.

3️⃣ Issue #2 — Payout.amount vs amount_cents
Your Payout entity has:

amount (number)

fee (number) — “Fee for instant payout (5%)”

There is no amount_cents field in the schema.

In the Module 3 blueprint I slipped into saying:

“amount_cents” on the Payout record

And then using that as the Stripe amount

🛠 Fix:

In Base44 / DB:

Use Payout.amount in USD (decimal).

Use Payout.fee in USD as well (for instant payout fees).

When calling Stripe:

Convert to cents at the Stripe call level, not in the entity:

stripe_amount_cents = Math.round(Payout.amount * 100)

If instant payout fee: stripe_amount_cents = Math.round((Payout.amount - Payout.fee) * 100)

So you should mentally replace all amount_cents in my Module 3 text with:

“Payout.amount in USD, and only convert to cents when calling Stripe.”

4️⃣ Issue #3 — usd_due formula & “two options”
Your CleanerEarning entity explicitly defines:

usd_due: “USD owed to cleaner = (credits_earned / 10) * payout_percentage”

In Module 3, I said something like:

“We can either store credits_earned = full credits or use only payout credits…”

and gave two options conceptually. That’s confusing and doesn’t line up with the description.

🛠 Fix (we must do this):

For every CleanerEarning:

Set:

credits_earned = Booking.final_charge_credits (full credits the client paid)

payout_percentage = Booking.payout_percentage_at_accept

usd_due = (credits_earned / 10) * payout_percentage

This matches both:

The entity description

And the Base44 info doc (final_charge_credits × payout_percentage_at_accept).

So: drop the “two options” and always follow that formula.

5️⃣ Issue #4 — What should Payout.aggregate exactly?
Your docs say:

final_charge_credits × payout_percentage_at_accept → cleaner’s share

That share is stored in Payment.cleaner_payout

Then Payout aggregates those Payment.cleaner_payout amounts

In Module 3 I had Payout aggregating CleanerEarning.usd_due instead.

Mathematically that’s fine if:

CleanerEarning.usd_due === Payment.cleaner_payout for every booking.

But the canonical flow in docs is “via Payment”.

🛠 Best alignment fix:

When booking is approved (Module 2):

Compute cleaner_share_usd = (Booking.final_charge_credits / 10) * payout_percentage_at_accept

Set:

Payment.cleaner_payout = cleaner_share_usd

CleanerEarning.usd_due = cleaner_share_usd (same value)

When batching in Module 3 (weekly / instant):

Aggregate from either:

SUM(Payment.cleaner_payout) for that cleaner and unpaid bookings, or

SUM(CleanerEarning.usd_due) where status = "pending"

Just pick ONE as your implementation source of truth and be consistent.
I’d suggest:

Use CleanerEarning as the “payout ledger” and just make sure its usd_due always matches Payment.cleaner_payout.

6️⃣ Issue #5 — Instant payout fee & Payout.fee field
Your Payout schema includes:

fee: “Fee for instant payout (5%)”

In Module 3 I:

Talked about instant payouts and a % fee

But I didn’t explicitly wire that into Payout.fee (I hand-waved a “PlatformFee” elsewhere)

🛠 Fix:

For instant payouts:

Compute:

gross_usd = SUM(CleanerEarning.usd_due for that batch)

fee_usd = gross_usd * INSTANT_PAYOUT_FEE_PCT (e.g. 0.05)

net_usd = gross_usd - fee_usd

Create Payout with:

amount = net_usd

fee = fee_usd

payout_type = "instant"

If you want separate reporting for platform fees later, you can derive it from Payout.fee, no need for a separate “PlatformFee” entity right now.

7️⃣ Issue #6 — Clawbacks (post-payout disputes) and negative earnings
In Module 3, I said:

For disputes after payout, we could create a negative CleanerEarning as a future offset.

That’s actually fine as long as we obey the formula:

usd_due = (credits_earned / 10) * payout_percentage

I only mentioned setting usd_due negative, but I didn’t explicitly say to also set credits_earned negative in-sync. That’s an incomplete spec.

🛠 Fix:

For post-payout clawbacks:

Pick a clawback in USD, call it clawback_usd.

Let the same payout_percentage apply.

Then create a negative CleanerEarning:

credits_earned = - (clawback_usd * 10) / payout_percentage

payout_percentage = same as original

usd_due = (credits_earned / 10) * payout_percentage → will be -clawback_usd

status = "pending"

Then future Payouts will see a mix of:

normal positive usd_due

one negative usd_due (the clawback)

and the net payout will be reduced correctly.

Key thing: keep credits_earned and usd_due tied by the same formula, even for negative rows.

8️⃣ Issue #7 — Minor naming mismatch in analytics
I said:

“…update CleanerAnalytics.total_earnings_cents…”

But your CleanerAnalytics entity has:

total_earnings (number) — no _cents.

🛠 Fix:

Use CleanerAnalytics.total_earnings and store it in USD.

Increment it by Payout.amount (gross OR net, whichever you decide is the “earnings” conceptually).

9️⃣ Quick summary of what to mentally patch in Module 3
If you want a super short “patch notes” list:

CleanerEarning status

Only: pending | batched | paid | reversed.

No failed.

Payout fields

Use Payout.amount (USD) and Payout.fee (USD).

Do cents conversion only inside Stripe calls.

CleanerEarning math

Always:

credits_earned = Booking.final_charge_credits

payout_percentage = Booking.payout_percentage_at_accept

usd_due = (credits_earned / 10) * payout_percentage.

Aggregation source

Make CleanerEarning.usd_due == Payment.cleaner_payout, then sum one of them (not both).

Instant payout fees

Store fee in Payout.fee, not ad-hoc somewhere else.

Clawbacks

When using negative CleanerEarning rows, set both credits_earned and usd_due negative according to the formula.

Analytics

Use CleanerAnalytics.total_earnings (USD).

If you want, I can now give you a short “corrected Module 3 v2” (not long like before — just the patched version incorporating these fixes) so you have a clean master copy to build from.

🧩 MODULE 3 — PAYOUT ENGINE (FINAL, CORRECTED VERSION)
1. Scope of this module
Module 3 owns everything from “Cleaner has earnings” → “Money sent to their bank”:

Takes CleanerEarning rows (created in Module 2)

Groups them into Payouts (weekly or instant)

Sends payouts via Stripe to cleaners

Handles failures & retries

Handles dispute clawbacks (pre- and post-payout)

Updates analytics / totals

We assume:

Module 1 already drives Booking → status = "approved"

Module 2 already:

settles client payment & credits

creates CleanerEarning with status = "pending"

2. Entities used in Module 3
CleanerEarning
Key fields (we care about):

cleaner_email

booking_id

credits_earned (full job credits)

payout_percentage (e.g. 0.80 / 0.85)

usd_due — must satisfy:
usd_due = (credits_earned / 10) * payout_percentage

status:

"pending" — created, not batched

"batched" — assigned to a Payout, not yet paid

"paid" — money sent successfully

"reversed" — zeroed out / clawed back

payout_id (nullable)

created_date

Important: only use these 4 statuses. No failed state for CleanerEarning.

Payout
Key fields:

cleaner_email

booking_ids[] (or equivalent structure)

amount (number, USD net amount sent to cleaner)

fee (number, USD platform fee for instant payouts; 0 for weekly)

payout_type: "weekly" or "instant"

status: "pending" | "processing" | "completed" | "failed" | "cancelled"

stripe_transfer_id

batch_start_date, batch_end_date

created_date

We store amount and fee in USD in the DB.
Only convert to cents when calling Stripe.

3. Shared assumptions & policy knobs
These are configurable values (you can change them later):

CREDITS_PER_USD = 10

Weekly payout:

Day: Friday

Cutoff: earnings up to Thursday 23:59

Min payout: $20 (or whatever)

Instant payout:

Allowed when pending earnings ≥ $10 (for example)

Instant payout fee: INSTANT_PAYOUT_FEE_PCT = 0.05 (5%)

4. Core Lifecycle
For each cleaner:

Booking is approved

Module 2:

Finalizes credits & payment

Creates CleanerEarning with:

credits_earned = Booking.final_charge_credits

payout_percentage = Booking.payout_percentage_at_accept

usd_due = (credits_earned / 10) * payout_percentage

status = "pending"

Module 3:

Groups pending earnings into:

weekly Payout on Fridays, or

instant Payout on-demand

Calls Stripe → transfer to cleaner account

Marks earnings as paid

Handles failures & reversals

5. Automations — Payout Engine
We number them 3.x.

3.1 — Ensure CleanerEarning exists on booking approval
(You likely already defined this at end of Module 2, but it’s the entry to Module 3.)

Trigger: Booking.status changes → "approved"
Condition:

No existing CleanerEarning row for this booking_id.

Actions:

Let:

C = Booking.final_charge_credits

P = Booking.payout_percentage_at_accept

Create CleanerEarning:

cleaner_email = Booking.cleaner_email

booking_id = Booking.id

credits_earned = C

payout_percentage = P

usd_due = (C / CREDITS_PER_USD) * P

status = "pending"

From here on, Module 3 consumes CleanerEarning.pending.

3.2 — Weekly payout batch
Runs once per week, for ALL cleaners.

Trigger: Scheduled (e.g. every Friday at 09:00).

For each unique cleaner_email:

Query all CleanerEarning rows where:

status = "pending"

created_date <= cutoff_date (end-of-day yesterday)

If none → skip.

Calculate:

gross_usd = SUM(usd_due) across those earnings

If gross_usd < MIN_WEEKLY_PAYOUT_USD (e.g. $20) → skip for now (leave them pending).

Create Payout:

cleaner_email = this cleaner

booking_ids = [all booking_ids from these earnings]

amount = gross_usd (this is the net to cleaner for weekly)

fee = 0

payout_type = "weekly"

status = "pending"

batch_start_date = min(created_date)

batch_end_date = max(created_date)

For each included CleanerEarning:

Set status = "batched"

Set payout_id = new Payout.id

Now the weekly batch is ready to send to Stripe.

3.3 — Instant payout request (Cash Out Now)
Cleaner initiates this from the UI.

We model this as an action (could be a mutation) that triggers an automation.

Trigger: “Instant Payout Request” action (e.g., a mutation or flag that Base44 can react to).

Condition:

For that cleaner_email, SUM(usd_due WHERE status = "pending") ≥ MIN_INSTANT_PAYOUT_USD (e.g., $10).

Actions:

Select pending earnings for that cleaner (status = "pending").

Compute:

gross_usd = SUM(usd_due)

fee_usd = gross_usd * INSTANT_PAYOUT_FEE_PCT

net_usd = gross_usd - fee_usd

Create Payout:

cleaner_email

booking_ids = list of their booking_ids

amount = net_usd

fee = fee_usd

payout_type = "instant"

status = "pending"

For each included CleanerEarning:

Set status = "batched"

Set payout_id = Payout.id

Now instant payout behaves like a special Payout with payout_type = "instant" and a non-zero fee.

3.4 — On Payout.created (pending) → initiate Stripe transfer
This sends money to the cleaner.

Trigger: Payout.created
Condition: Payout.status = "pending"

Actions:

Get cleaner’s Stripe account ID from CleanerProfile.stripe_account_id.

Compute Stripe amount in cents:

stripe_amount_cents = Math.round(Payout.amount * 100)
(We’re using Payout.amount which is already USD.)

Call Stripe Transfer API:

amount = stripe_amount_cents

currency = "usd"

destination = CleanerProfile.stripe_account_id

Include metadata: payout_id, cleaner_email, etc.

If Stripe call is successful (synchronously):

Set:

Payout.status = "processing"

Payout.stripe_transfer_id = returned.id

If Stripe call fails:

Set:

Payout.status = "failed"

Payout.error_message = error.message (add field if needed)

Notify ops & cleaner as needed.

Stripe will then send asynchronous webhooks for final success/failure.

3.5 — Stripe webhook → update Payout status
Your Stripe webhooks (handled via Base44 or a small external hook) will update Payout.

Trigger: Stripe webhook handler updates some StripeEvent or directly the Payout.

We define logic as:

If webhook says transfer succeeded (e.g., type = "transfer.paid" or status = "succeeded"):

Lookup Payout by stripe_transfer_id.

Set Payout.status = "completed".

If webhook says transfer failed:

Set Payout.status = "failed", log the error.

3.6 — On Payout.completed → mark earnings as paid & update analytics
Trigger: Payout.status changes → "completed"

Actions:

For all CleanerEarning where payout_id = this Payout.id:

Set status = "paid"

Update CleanerAnalytics for this cleaner:

For the relevant period (month, year, or total):

total_earnings += Payout.amount (USD)

payout_count += 1 (if such a field exists)

Optionally track:

last_payout_date = now

Notify cleaner:

Message/email: “Your payout of $X has been sent to your bank account.”

At this point, the platform owes no more money for those bookings.

3.7 — On Payout.failed → un-batch earnings & retry later
Trigger: Payout.status changes → "failed"

Actions:

For each CleanerEarning with payout_id = this.id:

Set status = "pending"

Set payout_id = null

Notify admin/ops:

Create a SupportTicket or log an event with:

type = "payout_failure"

cleaner_email, payout_id, reason

Notify cleaner:

“We couldn’t process your payout. Please update your bank info or contact support.”

Earnings are now back in the pool and will be picked up by the next weekly or instant payout.

3.8 — Pre-payout dispute resolution (Earning not paid yet)
If a dispute is resolved before the cleaner gets paid:

Trigger: Dispute.status changes → "resolved"
Condition:

There exists a CleanerEarning for Dispute.booking_id with:

status IN ("pending", "batched")

Actions:

Determine clawback_usd based on Dispute outcome:

e.g., 100% refund → cleaner gets nothing

50% refund → cleaner loses half, etc.

For the CleanerEarning row of that booking:

New usd_due = existing_usd_due - clawback_usd

If usd_due <= 0:

Set:

usd_due = 0

credits_earned = 0

status = "reversed"

If CleanerEarning.status = "batched" and we reduced usd_due:

Decrease Payout.amount by clawback_usd for that Payout.

This prevents overpaying the cleaner for disputed jobs.

3.9 — Post-payout dispute → future clawback via negative earning
If the dispute resolves after the cleaner was already paid:

Trigger: Dispute.status changes → "resolved"
Condition:

CleanerEarning for booking_id has status = "paid"

Actions:

Decide clawback_usd (how much you want to recover from the cleaner).

Use the original payout_percentage (P) that applied to that job.

Create a negative CleanerEarning:

cleaner_email = same cleaner

booking_id = Dispute.booking_id

payout_percentage = same P

Compute:

We want: usd_due = -clawback_usd.

From the formula:
usd_due = (credits_earned / 10) * P
So:

credits_earned = (usd_due * 10) / P
→ credits_earned = (-clawback_usd * 10) / P (negative)

Set:

credits_earned = (-clawback_usd * 10) / P

usd_due = -clawback_usd

status = "pending"

This negative earning will:

Be included in the next weekly or instant payout

Reduce the net payout that cleaner receives

This is how you slowly claw back overpayments instead of trying to yank money out immediately.

6. Summary of Module 3 responsibilities (clean view)
Input:

CleanerEarning.pending created in Module 2 when bookings are approved.

Core Work:

Batch pending earnings → Payouts (weekly / instant)

Initiate Stripe transfers

Mark earnings as paid

Handle payout failure (un-batch, retry later)

Apply dispute-based reductions:

Before payout: reduce or reverse earnings

After payout: negative earnings for future clawback

Output:

Payout rows representing actual money sent

CleanerEarning updated to paid or reversed

CleanerAnalytics.total_earnings increased

Clean Stripe integration

If you’re happy with this Module 3 (final), we can move on to the next big brainpiece:

Module 4 — PricingRule Engine (surge, seasonal, tier, add-ons, membership discounts)
or

Module 5 — Smart Match Engine (distance, reliability, performance, availability, etc.)

Tell me which one you want next:
“Module 4” or “Module 5”.


LETYS MOVE ON TO MODULE 4

Nice. Module 4 is fun—this is where PureTask actually feels premium to clients and fair to cleaners.

We’ll keep assuming: no automations exist yet, only entities.

🧩 MODULE 4 — PRICING ENGINE & PRICINGRULES (ADVANCED)
1. What Module 4 is responsible for
This module decides how a job’s price is calculated, in credits and USD:

Base hourly + cleaning-type add-ons from CleanerProfile

Additional services (windows, oven, fridge, etc.)

Dynamic pricing via PricingRule (time of day, day of week, surge, last minute, holiday, first-booking)

Membership discounts via ClientMembership.benefits.discount_percentage

Bundle/upsell discounts via BundleOffer (multi-service, multi-booking, upgrade)

Producing:

Booking.total_price (final estimated cost)

Booking.escrow_credits_reserved (credits to hold in escrow at booking)

Snapshot of cleaner’s rates on the Booking (snapshot_base_rate_cph, etc.) so changing their prices later doesn’t affect old bookings

This module feeds Module 2 (escrow / final_charge_credits) and Module 3 (cleaner earnings).

2. Key entities & fields
CleanerProfile (pricing source)
From your schema:

base_rate_credits_per_hour

deep_addon_credits_per_hour

moveout_addon_credits_per_hour

additional_service_pricing (windows, blinds, oven, fridge, light_fixtures, inside_cabinets, baseboards, laundry…)

These are in credits.
We’ll assume 10 credits ≈ $1 (same as Modules 2–3).

Booking (pricing snapshot & final estimated price)
From your info doc:

snapshot_base_rate_cph, snapshot_deep_addon_cph, etc.

total_price (client’s total cost)

escrow_credits_reserved (credits held for booking)

final_charge_credits, refund_credits (used later for settlement)

payout_percentage_at_accept

We’ll also assume Booking has:

cleaning_type (basic | deep | moveout)

estimated_hours

additional_services object with counts (windows, oven, etc.)

date, start_time (for time-based rules)

PricingRule (dynamic multipliers)
From schema:

rule_name

rule_type enum:

time_of_day, day_of_week, distance, surge, last_minute, holiday, first_booking_discount

multiplier (1.0 = no change; 1.2 = +20%; 0.8 = −20%)

conditions (JSON object with rule-specific conditions)

is_active

display_label (“Weekend Premium”)

priority (higher = applied first or with special ordering)

BundleOffer (multi-service / multi-booking discounts)
From schema:

offer_type:

multi_service, multi_booking, upgrade_upsell

conditions

discount_amount (USD)

discount_percentage

display_message

ClientMembership (memberships / discounts)
From schema:

tier: Plus, Platinum

monthly_fee

benefits.discount_percentage

benefits.free_cancellations, priority_booking, etc.

status: active | cancelled | past_due

We care now about benefits.discount_percentage and status = "active".

3. Pricing engine responsibilities (high level)
The pricing pipeline at quote/booking time is:

Base price from cleaner rates & job size

Apply PricingRule multipliers (surge, last minute, weekend, etc.)

Apply membership discount

Apply bundle offers / promotions

Convert to credits & USD

Snapshot values to Booking & DraftBooking

We’ll wire this into:

DraftBooking (for live price preview during booking flow)

Booking (on creation / final confirm)

4. Shared formulas & helpers
Let:

CREDITS_PER_USD = 10 (same as Modules 2 & 3)

base_hourly_cph = snapshot of CleanerProfile.base_rate_credits_per_hour

deep_cph / moveout_cph = respective add-on hourly rates

extra_services_cph = computed sum based on selected extras

4.1 Base rate from CleanerProfile
For a given booking:

Determine core hourly rate:

If cleaning_type = "basic":

core_rate_cph = base_rate_credits_per_hour

If cleaning_type = "deep":

core_rate_cph = base_rate_credits_per_hour + deep_addon_credits_per_hour

If cleaning_type = "moveout":

core_rate_cph = base_rate_credits_per_hour + moveout_addon_credits_per_hour

Compute add-ons per job (NOT hourly):

For each additional service, e.g.:

windows_total = windows_count * additional_service_pricing.windows

oven_total = oven_count * additional_service_pricing.oven

etc.

Base estimated credits before dynamic rules:

base_hours_credits = core_rate_cph * estimated_hours
addon_credits = sum(all extra_services_totals)
base_price_credits = base_hours_credits + addon_credits
This matches your docs: Booking.total_price “sum of the hourly rate, selected cleaning type add-ons, and any chosen additional services.”

4.2 Applying PricingRule multipliers
Using the PricingRule entity:

For the booking context (date/time, distance, created_at vs start_time, holiday flag, is first booking, etc.), we:

Fetch all PricingRule where is_active = true.

Filter to those whose conditions JSON matches the booking.

Examples:

rule_type = "day_of_week": conditions might look like:

{ "days": ["sat", "sun"] }
You check if Booking.date is weekend.

rule_type = "time_of_day":

{ "start_hour": 18, "end_hour": 22 }
Check if start_time in that range.

rule_type = "last_minute":

{ "max_hours_before_start": 24 }
Compare now vs Booking.date/start_time.

rule_type = "holiday":

{ "holiday_list": ["2025-12-25", "2025-01-01"] }
Sort remaining rules by priority (highest first)

Apply multipliers to base_price_credits:

Start: price_after_rules = base_price_credits

For each rule in order:

price_after_rules = price_after_rules * rule.multiplier

Optionally collect rule.display_label to show UI labels (“Weekend Premium”, “Last-Minute Surcharge”).

You can choose whether:

All rules multiply cumulatively, or

Only the highest priority rule per rule_type applies.
For simplicity, blueprint assumes cumulative with priority controlling ordering.

4.3 Membership discount
If the client has an active membership:

Lookup ClientMembership:

client_email = Booking.client_email

status = "active"

Get membership discount:

membership_discount_pct = ClientMembership.benefits.discount_percentage (e.g., 10 for 10%)

Apply to price_after_rules:

membership_discount_credits = price_after_rules * (membership_discount_pct / 100)
price_after_membership = price_after_rules - membership_discount_credits
Optional: only apply membership discount to labor, not add-ons—but blueprint uses total for now.

4.4 BundleOffers
Use BundleOffer for extra discounts when:

offer_type = "multi_service":

e.g., if client books deep clean + 2 add-ons → get X% off

offer_type = "multi_booking":

if they schedule 3+ bookings at once (via RecurringBooking or multi-date)

offer_type = "upgrade_upsell":

if they upgrade from basic to deep, get some discount on add-ons

Logic:

Query all active BundleOffer where is_active = true.

Evaluate conditions JSON against booking + possible context (cart/sequence of bookings).

For each matching offer:

If discount_percentage set:

bundle_discount_credits += price_after_membership * (discount_percentage / 100)

If discount_amount (USD) set:

bundle_discount_credits += discount_amount * CREDITS_PER_USD

Final credits after bundles:

final_estimated_credits = price_after_membership - bundle_discount_credits
We should make sure final_estimated_credits never goes below 0.

4.5 Conversion to USD & Booking fields
When we have final_estimated_credits:

Set on Booking:

Booking.total_price = final_estimated_credits / CREDITS_PER_USD (USD)

Booking.escrow_credits_reserved = final_estimated_credits

Snapshot cleaner’s base rates (for reference):

Booking.snapshot_base_rate_cph = CleanerProfile.base_rate_credits_per_hour

Booking.snapshot_deep_addon_cph = CleanerProfile.deep_addon_credits_per_hour

Booking.snapshot_moveout_addon_cph = CleanerProfile.moveout_addon_credits_per_hour

Booking.snapshot_additional_service_prices = CleanerProfile.additional_service_pricing

Optional new fields (nice to have if you want breakdowns):

Booking.pricing_rule_labels[] (list of display_labels applied)

Booking.membership_discount_credits

Booking.bundle_discount_credits

Booking.dynamic_pricing_multiplier (product of all multipliers)

You can add these to your Booking entity if you want better transparency.

5. Automations — MODULE 4
We’ll name them 4.x.

4.1 — Calculate live quote on DraftBooking updates
Used for instant pricing preview in the multi-step client flow.

Trigger: DraftBooking updated

Condition:

client_email set

cleaner_email (or selected cleaner) set

date, start_time, estimated_hours, cleaning_type, and selected additional_services set

Actions:

Load CleanerProfile for cleaner_email.

Run Base Price calculation (4.1) → base_price_credits.

Apply PricingRule engine (4.2) → price_after_rules.

Apply Membership discount (4.3) → price_after_membership.

Apply BundleOffers (4.4) → final_estimated_credits.

Set fields on DraftBooking (you can add these if they’re not there yet):

DraftBooking.estimated_price_credits = final_estimated_credits

DraftBooking.estimated_price_usd = final_estimated_credits / CREDITS_PER_USD

DraftBooking.applied_pricing_labels[] = [rule.display_label, bundle.display_message, ...]

This powers the front-end’s “Your price: $X (includes Y surcharge, Z discount)” view.

4.2 — On DraftBooking → Booking creation, snapshot pricing to Booking
This extends Module 1 Automation 1 (creating Booking from DraftBooking).

Trigger: DraftBooking updated

Condition:

confirmed = true (client hits “Confirm & Book”)

No existing Booking for that DraftBooking

Actions:

Re-run the pricing pipeline (same as 4.1) or trust the last DraftBooking values.

Create Booking with:

Core fields (client, cleaner, date, hours, services, etc.)

total_price = DraftBooking.estimated_price_usd

escrow_credits_reserved = DraftBooking.estimated_price_credits

snapshot_base_rate_cph, snapshot_deep_addon_cph, etc. from CleanerProfile

(Optional) Copy breakdown fields:

pricing_rule_labels, membership_discount_credits, etc.

This Booking then flows into:

Module 2: Automation 2.2 (escrow & credits deduction)

Module 1: cleaner response flow, etc.

4.3 — Recalculate price if key fields change before payment hold
If you allow editing of bookings before they are locked:

Trigger: Booking updated

Condition:

old.status = "created"

new.status = "created" (still not in payment_hold or later)

AND any of these changed: date, start_time, estimated_hours, additional_services, cleaning_type, cleaner_email

Actions:

Re-run the pricing pipeline using latest values.

Update:

Booking.total_price

Booking.escrow_credits_reserved

Snapshot fields if cleaner changed

Important rule:
Once Booking moves to payment_hold or beyond, do not auto-recalculate price—lock it unless changed explicitly by admin.

4.4 — First booking discount (PricingRule rule_type = "first_booking_discount")
Instead of hardcoding, we leverage PricingRule:

Create a PricingRule:

rule_type = "first_booking_discount"

multiplier = 0.8 (20% discount)

conditions = { "require_first_booking": true }

display_label = "First Booking 20% Off"

At pricing time, one of the conditions we check is:

Is this client’s ClientProfile.total_bookings = 0?

If yes, this rule’s multiplier is applied in the PricingRule phase.

No extra automation needed beyond the main pipeline; just the right rule config.

4.5 — Holiday / surge / last-minute rules (examples)
You configure these as rows in PricingRule, not as separate flows. Engine from 4.2 handles them:

Weekend Premium:

rule_type = "day_of_week"

multiplier = 1.15

conditions = { "days": ["sat", "sun"] }

display_label = "Weekend Premium"

Last-minute +25%:

rule_type = "last_minute"

multiplier = 1.25

conditions = { "max_hours_before_start": 24 }

display_label = "Last-Minute Booking"

Holiday surge x1.5:

rule_type = "holiday"

multiplier = 1.5

conditions = { "holiday_list": ["2025-12-25", "2025-01-01"] }

display_label = "Holiday Premium"

Again, no extra automation needed—your engine reads PricingRule and applies as needed.

Module 1 (Booking Engine):

Uses DraftBooking and Booking fields (estimated_hours, date/time, etc.) that Module 4 prices.

Module 1’s “created” → “payment_hold” transition will assume escrow_credits_reserved is set by Module 4.

Module 2 (Payments & Credits):

When Booking is created, Module 2:

Deducts escrow_credits_reserved from ClientProfile.credits_balance

Uses total_price and escrow_credits_reserved as base for escrow & settlement.

Module 3 (Payouts):

Uses final_charge_credits & payout_percentage_at_accept to compute cleaner earnings, but the starting point originated from Module 4’s pricing logic.

🧩 MODULE 4 — PRICING ENGINE (FINAL, CORRECTED VERSION)
1. Scope
Module 4 decides how much a job costs (in credits + USD) by combining:

Cleaner’s tiered hourly rates

Cleaning type (basic / deep / moveout)

Additional services (windows, oven, etc.)

Dynamic PricingRules (time of day, weekend, distance, last-minute, holiday, first-booking, surge)

Membership discounts

Recurring/sequence discounts (weekly/bi-weekly/monthly)

Bundle offers (multi-service / multi-booking / upgrade)

It outputs:

DraftBooking.estimated_price_credits / estimated_price_usd

Booking.escrow_credits_reserved

Booking.total_price (USD)

Snapshot fields used later by Modules 2 & 3.

We assume CREDITS_PER_USD = 10.

2. Entities & Fields
2.1 CleanerProfile (pricing source)
Key pricing fields (already in your Base44):

base_rate_credits_per_hour

deep_addon_credits_per_hour

moveout_addon_credits_per_hour

additional_service_pricing:

windows, blinds, oven, refrigerator, light_fixtures, inside_cabinets, baseboards, laundry

tier:

Developing, Semi Pro, Pro, Elite

We’ll also use CleanerProfile.tier for tier multipliers.

2.2 Booking (pricing snapshot & outcome)
We’ll rely on / add:

Existing / described:

cleaner_email

client_email

cleaning_type (basic | deep | moveout)

estimated_hours

additional_services (object with counts: windows, oven, etc.)

date, start_time

total_price (USD)

escrow_credits_reserved (credits reserved upfront)

final_charge_credits, refund_credits (used later in Modules 2 & 3)

payout_percentage_at_accept

Snapshot fields:

snapshot_base_rate_cph

snapshot_deep_addon_cph

snapshot_moveout_addon_cph

New suggested snapshot fields:

snapshot_membership_discount_pct

snapshot_tier_multiplier

pricing_breakdown (JSON object with breakdown details)

2.3 DraftBooking (live quote view)
Will store:

estimated_price_credits

estimated_price_usd

(optionally) pricing_breakdown

This is the “what you see while booking” pricing.

2.4 PricingRule
Key fields (from your schema):

rule_type:

time_of_day, day_of_week, distance, surge, last_minute, holiday, first_booking_discount

multiplier (float, e.g. 1.2, 0.8)

3. Pricing Pipeline (Step-by-step)
Shared constant:
CREDITS_PER_USD = 10
Step 1 — Load context
Inputs:

Cleaner:

CleanerProfile by cleaner_email

Client:

ClientProfile and ClientMembership by client_email

Job:

cleaning_type

estimated_hours

additional_services (counts per service)

date, start_time

Any recurrence / sequence info (Weekly/Bi-weekly/Monthly) from RecurringBooking or DraftBooking config

Step 2 — Base hourly rate (per cleaning type)
We treat deep/moveout add-ons as hourly premiums on top of base_rate.

base_rate_cph = CleanerProfile.base_rate_credits_per_hour
deep_cph      = CleanerProfile.deep_addon_credits_per_hour
moveout_cph   = CleanerProfile.moveout_addon_credits_per_hour

if cleaning_type = "basic":
    core_rate_cph = base_rate_cph
if cleaning_type = "deep":
    core_rate_cph = base_rate_cph + deep_cph
if cleaning_type = "moveout":
    core_rate_cph = base_rate_cph + moveout_cph
Now compute base hours:

base_hours_credits = core_rate_cph * estimated_hours
Step 3 — Additional service pricing (per job)
Using CleanerProfile.additional_service_pricing:

For each additional service with a count in additional_services:

total_extras_credits =
    windows_count        * additional_service_pricing.windows
  + blinds_count         * additional_service_pricing.blinds
  + oven_count           * additional_service_pricing.oven
  + refrigerator_count   * additional_service_pricing.refrigerator
  + light_fixtures_count * additional_service_pricing.light_fixtures
  + cabinets_count       * additional_service_pricing.inside_cabinets
  + baseboards_flag      * additional_service_pricing.baseboards
  + laundry_count        * additional_service_pricing.laundry
You can treat baseboards_flag as 0 or 1.

Now compute the pre-dynamic base:

base_price_credits = base_hours_credits + total_extras_credits
Step 4 — Tier multiplier (based on CleanerProfile.tier)
Tier pricing:

tier_multiplier =
    Developing -> 0.90
    Semi Pro   -> 1.00
    Pro        -> 1.10
    Elite      -> 1.20
Apply:

price_after_tier = base_price_credits * tier_multiplier
Save tier_multiplier for snapshot.

Step 5 — Dynamic PricingRules
We process PricingRule in two stages:

Select rules whose conditions match Booking

Group by rule_type, then pick highest priority per type

5.1 Find matching rules
Get all PricingRule where is_active = true

For each:

Evaluate conditions against Booking context:

time_of_day:

Extract hour from start_time (e.g., booking_hour = 0–23)

Check conditions.start_hour <= booking_hour <= conditions.end_hour

day_of_week:

Compute booking_day (mon–sun)

Check membership in conditions.days[]

distance:

Compute distance between cleaner’s location and booking address (lat/lng stored somewhere)

Compare against conditions.min_distance, max_distance, etc.

last_minute:

Compare hours_until_start = (Booking.start_datetime - now) vs conditions.max_hours_before_start

holiday:

Check if Booking.date in conditions.holiday_list[]

first_booking_discount:

Check if ClientProfile.total_bookings = 0

Only keep rules whose conditions evaluate to true.

5.2 Apply rules (one per type)
Group matched rules by rule_type

In each group, pick rule with highest priority

Start:

dynamic_multiplier = 1.0
applied_rule_labels = []
For each selected rule:

dynamic_multiplier *= rule.multiplier
applied_rule_labels.append(rule.display_label)
Now apply:

price_after_pr_rules = price_after_tier * dynamic_multiplier
Step 6 — Membership discount
If the client has an active membership:

Look up ClientMembership:

client_email

status = "active"

Get:

membership_discount_pct = ClientMembership.benefits.discount_percentage
Compute:

membership_discount_credits = price_after_pr_rules * (membership_discount_pct / 100)
price_after_membership = price_after_pr_rules - membership_discount_credits
If no active membership:

membership_discount_pct = 0
price_after_membership = price_after_pr_rules
membership_discount_credits = 0
Snapshot:

Booking.snapshot_membership_discount_pct = membership_discount_pct

Step 7 — Recurring booking discount (sequence)
If this booking is part of a RecurringBooking / series:

Determine recurrence type: weekly / bi-weekly / monthly

Define policy, e.g.:

Weekly: recurrence_discount_pct = 15

Bi-weekly: 10

Monthly: 5

Compute:

recurrence_discount_credits = price_after_membership * (recurrence_discount_pct / 100)
price_after_recurrence = price_after_membership - recurrence_discount_credits
If not recurring:

recurrence_discount_pct = 0
recurrence_discount_credits = 0
price_after_recurrence = price_after_membership
Step 8 — BundleOffers
Now apply any BundleOffer that applies to this booking/cart context.

Fetch all BundleOffer where is_active = true.

For each:

Evaluate conditions against:

Selected services

Number of bookings in cart

Upgrades (basic → deep, etc.)

For each matching bundle:

If discount_percentage is set:

Decide base to apply it on (typically price_after_recurrence, or sometimes just total_extras_credits if offer is extras-only).

Example:

this_bundle_discount = target_base * (discount_percentage / 100)
If discount_amount is set (USD):

Convert to credits:

this_bundle_discount = discount_amount * CREDITS_PER_USD
Sum across all applicable bundles:

bundle_discount_credits = SUM(this_bundle_discount)
price_after_bundles = price_after_recurrence - bundle_discount_credits
Ensure:

if price_after_bundles < 0:
    price_after_bundles = 0
Also collect display_message into applied_pricing_labels.

Step 9 — Final price & snapshots
Let:

final_estimated_credits = round(price_after_bundles)
final_estimated_usd     = final_estimated_credits / CREDITS_PER_USD
Write to Booking or DraftBooking:

For DraftBooking:

estimated_price_credits = final_estimated_credits

estimated_price_usd = final_estimated_usd

For Booking:

total_price = final_estimated_usd

escrow_credits_reserved = final_estimated_credits

Snapshots on Booking:

snapshot_base_rate_cph = base_rate_cph

snapshot_deep_addon_cph = deep_cph

snapshot_moveout_addon_cph = moveout_cph

snapshot_additional_service_prices = CleanerProfile.additional_service_pricing

snapshot_membership_discount_pct = membership_discount_pct

snapshot_dynamic_pricing_multiplier = dynamic_multiplier

snapshot_tier_multiplier = tier_multiplier

Optional breakdown:

Booking.pricing_breakdown = {
  "base_hours_credits": base_hours_credits,
  "extras_credits": total_extras_credits,
  "tier_multiplier": tier_multiplier,
  "dynamic_multiplier": dynamic_multiplier,
  "membership_discount_credits": membership_discount_credits,
  "recurrence_discount_credits": recurrence_discount_credits,
  "bundle_discount_credits": bundle_discount_credits,
  "final_estimated_credits": final_estimated_credits
}
Also:

Booking.applied_pricing_labels = applied_rule_labels + bundle display messages

🧩 MODULE 5 — SMART MATCH ENGINE
1. What this module owns
Module 5 decides:

Which cleaners are eligible for a job

How they’re ranked

How we route the offer (primary + fallback cleaners)

How we respect:

Client preferences

Cleaner preferences & availability

Reliability & tier

Favorites / blocks

Recurring “same cleaner” loyalty

It is backed by these entities:

CleanerProfile — skills, availability, tier, reliability metrics, product preferences, service locations, instant_book flags

ClientProfile, SmartMatchPreference — client’s tastes, preferred tier, max distance, product type, “same cleaner” preference

FavoriteCleaner, BlockedCleaner, BlockedUser — relationship-level overrides

DraftBooking, Booking, RecurringBooking — what needs to be matched, and recurring habits

CleanerAnalytics & reliability metrics on CleanerProfile — performance / trustworthiness

AnalyticsEvent — feedback loop (job_viewed_by_cleaner, job_accepted_by_cleaner, etc.)

2. Core Match Concepts
We’ll define the Smart Match as:

Candidate set → Scoring → Sorting → Routing (primary + fallbacks)

2.1 Candidate filters (hard constraints)
Cleaner must:

Be active & visible

CleanerProfile.is_active = true

Not blocked by the client

No BlockedCleaner row for (client_email, cleaner_email)

No BlockedUser row (blocker_email = client, blocked_email = cleaner)

Service the area

Client’s address city/zip in cleaner’s service_locations (array of strings)

AND within SmartMatchPreference.max_distance_miles if we have lat/lng for client + cleaner

Be available at that time

CleanerProfile.availability includes that day and time window covering Booking.start_time + Booking.estimated_hours

Offer required services

Their service_tags and specialty_tags cover the requested cleaning type / extras where necessary

If any of these fail → cleaner is not a candidate.

2.2 Client preference inputs
From SmartMatchPreference + ClientProfile:

preferred_specialty_tags[]

preferred_tier (any | Pro | Elite)

max_distance_miles (default 15)

preferred_product_type (any | eco-friendly | professional-grade)

budget_preference (budget | standard | premium)

same_cleaner_preferred (default true)

From relationship entities:

FavoriteCleaner entries for this client

RecurringBooking with this client (and previous cleaner assignments)

2.3 Cleaner performance & reliability inputs
From CleanerProfile + CleanerAnalytics:

reliability_score (0–100)

attendance_rate, punctuality_rate, cancellation_rate, no_show_rate, dispute_rate

average_rating, total_reviews, total_jobs

tier (Developing | Semi Pro | Pro | Elite)

typical_acceptance_rate_by_time (map of day/timeSlot → acceptance %)

CleanerAnalytics.total_earnings, bookings_count, average_rating

3. SmartMatch Score Formula
For each eligible cleaner, we compute a SmartMatch score.

Think:

score = weighted sum of (distance, reliability, rating, tier, client fit, acceptance odds, loyalty)

You can always tune weights later. I’ll define a concrete baseline.

3.1 Components
For each candidate cleaner C and booking B:

DistanceScore (0–1)

Let d = distance_in_miles(cleaner, booking_address)

Let d_max = SmartMatchPreference.max_distance_miles (default 15)

If d > d_max → candidate was already filtered out

Else:

DistanceScore = 1 - (d / d_max)   // closer = higher
ReliabilityScoreNorm (0–1)

From CleanerProfile.reliability_score (0–100)

ReliabilityScoreNorm = reliability_score / 100

RatingScore (0–1)

Use average_rating (1–5)

RatingScore = (average_rating - 3) / 2 (so 3 → 0, 5 → 1, 1 → -1 but clamp to 0)

TierScore (0–1)
Mapping:

Developing → 0.3

Semi Pro → 0.6

Pro → 0.85

Elite → 1.0

Then adjust for SmartMatchPreference.preferred_tier:

If preferred_tier = Pro and cleaner.tier is Pro/Elite → +bonus 0.05

If preferred_tier = Elite and cleaner.tier is Elite → +bonus 0.1

SpecialtyMatchScore (0–1)

Compare SmartMatchPreference.preferred_specialty_tags with CleanerProfile.specialty_tags

SpecialtyMatchScore = (# overlap / # preferred) (if they specified any).

If client specified none → default 0.5.

ProductPreferenceScore (0–1)

Compare preferred_product_type vs CleanerProfile.product_preference

Exact match → 1.0

preferred = any → 0.7

mismatch → 0.2

LoyaltyScore (0–1)

If booking is part of RecurringBooking with same cleaner_email → 1.0

Else if this cleaner is in FavoriteCleaner for this client → 0.9

Else if SmartMatchPreference.same_cleaner_preferred = true and cleaner did last booking for this client → 0.8

Else → 0.3

AcceptanceLikelihoodScore (0–1)

From CleanerProfile.typical_acceptance_rate_by_time using a key like "Tue_09-12"

If no data → 0.5

Else → rate / 100

BudgetFitScore (0–1)

From SmartMatchPreference.budget_preference and cleaner tier / base_rate_credits_per_hour.

If budget = budget:

Lower base_rate → higher score (normalized vs market)

If budget = premium:

Higher tier & base_rate → higher score

If standard: center them.

We can approximate by ranking cleaners by base_rate and mapping to 0–1.

3.2 Weighting
Baseline weights (sum ≈ 1.0):

DistanceScore: 0.15

ReliabilityScoreNorm: 0.20

RatingScore: 0.10

TierScore: 0.10

SpecialtyMatchScore: 0.10

ProductPreferenceScore: 0.05

LoyaltyScore: 0.20

AcceptanceLikelihoodScore: 0.05

BudgetFitScore: 0.05

Score formula:

SmartMatchScore =
  0.15 * DistanceScore +
  0.20 * ReliabilityScoreNorm +
  0.10 * RatingScore +
  0.10 * TierScore +
  0.10 * SpecialtyMatchScore +
  0.05 * ProductPreferenceScore +
  0.20 * LoyaltyScore +
  0.05 * AcceptanceLikelihoodScore +
  0.05 * BudgetFitScore
Sort candidates by SmartMatchScore desc.

4. Routing Strategy (Primary + Fallbacks)
Smart Match must output:

A chosen primary cleaner

A ranked list of fallback_cleaners (for auto-swap) in DraftBooking.fallback_cleaners

Then we use Module 1’s job lifecycle fields: request_sent_at, request_expires_at, and Booking status.

4.1 Instant Book vs Request / Offer
Instant book:

If any candidate cleaner has:

CleanerProfile.instant_book_enabled = true

Availability confirmed

ReliabilityScoreNorm ≥ threshold (e.g., 0.8)

Then we may auto-assign the top instant-book cleaner as Booking.cleaner_email immediately.

Request / Offer mode:

Otherwise:

Set Booking.cleaner_email = null initially

Set Booking.request_sent_at = now

Set Booking.request_expires_at = now + X minutes (e.g., 20)

We then send offer to primary cleaner, with others as fallback.

4.2 Fallback flow
We’ll use DraftBooking and Booking together:

Module 5 calculates top_N cleaners (e.g., 5–10) by SmartMatchScore.

Set on DraftBooking:

cleaner_email = top[0] (primary)

fallback_cleaners = [top[1], top[2], ...] in order

When Booking is created from DraftBooking:

Booking.cleaner_email = primary

We also store fallback list in Booking metadata (optional field).

Then we define auto-swap behaviors.

5. Automations (Module 5)
5.1 — On DraftBooking submit → compute match & fill primary + fallback_cleaners
Trigger: DraftBooking updated

Condition:

DraftBooking.client_email set

DraftBooking.auto_match = true (or “no specific cleaner chosen” UX path)

Required fields present: date, start_time, address, cleaning_type, estimated_hours

Actions:

Build candidate set:

Query CleanerProfile where:

is_active = true

Filter out cleans not servicing area, blocked, unavailable, etc. (Section 2.1).

For each candidate:

Compute SmartMatchScore (Section 3).

Take top N (e.g., 10) by score:

Sort desc.

Write to DraftBooking:

cleaner_email = top[0].email

fallback_cleaners = [top[1..N].email]

Optionally log an AnalyticsEvent:

event_type = "cleaner_selected"

user_type = "client"

metadata = { "cleaner_email": top[0].email, "fallback_count": N-1 }

5.2 — On Booking.created with auto_match → confirm/override SmartMatch
Trigger: Booking created

Condition:

Booking created from DraftBooking with auto_match = true

Or Booking.cleaner_email = null but SmartMatch needed

Actions:

If Booking created from DraftBooking and cleaner_email / fallback_cleaners already set:

Use those unchanged.

Else (Booking created without DraftBooking or needs re-matching):

Run the exact same SmartMatch pipeline (Sections 2–3).

Set:

Booking.cleaner_email = top[0]

Booking.fallback_cleaners_metadata = [top[1..N]] (custom field, optional).

Initialize job request:

Booking.request_sent_at = now

Booking.request_expires_at = now + configured_window (e.g., 20 min)

Send notification to primary cleaner (via Twilio/OneSignal/etc. later).

5.3 — On cleaner decline OR request_expires_at → auto-swap to next fallback
Trigger:

Booking updated with:

status = "offer_declined" by cleaner, OR

Scheduled check when now > request_expires_at and Booking.status still not accepted/confirmed.

Actions:

From fallback_cleaners list, find the next cleaner not yet tried.

If a next cleaner exists:

Set Booking.cleaner_email = next_cleaner

Update:

Booking.request_sent_at = now

Booking.request_expires_at = now + window

Log AnalyticsEvent:

event_type = "backup_selected"

metadata = { "booking_id": ..., "cleaner_email": next_cleaner }

If no fallback cleaners remain:

Set Booking.status = "unmatched" (or similar)

Notify client & ops that no cleaner accepted.

Optionally re-run SmartMatch with relaxed constraints (larger distance, lower tier).

5.4 — Preference for same cleaner on RecurringBooking
When generating bookings from RecurringBooking:

Trigger: Recurring job generator creates new Booking from RecurringBooking.

Condition:

RecurringBooking.cleaner_email set

SmartMatchPreference.same_cleaner_preferred = true for that client

Actions:

Check if the recurring cleaner is:

Active

Not blocked

Available at recurring date/time

If yes:

Set Booking.cleaner_email = RecurringBooking.cleaner_email

Still compute fallback cleaners (SmartMatch) in case they decline.

If not:

Run SmartMatch as normal, using preferences & RecurringBooking pattern.

This keeps “subscription” clients with the same cleaner whenever possible.

5.5 — Updating acceptance stats & feedback loop
We want the engine to get smarter over time.

Trigger: AnalyticsEvent with:

event_type = "job_viewed_by_cleaner" / job_accepted_by_cleaner / job_declined_by_cleaner

Actions:

For that cleaner + time slot:

Update CleanerProfile.typical_acceptance_rate_by_time for key like "Mon_09-12":

Keep counts of offers vs accepts

Derive % acceptance

This feeds future AcceptanceLikelihoodScore.

5.6 — Respecting SmartMatchPreference.budget_preference & preferred_tier
When running SmartMatch, we:

If budget_preference = "budget":

Prefer lower base_rate cleaners and maybe cap to tiers Developing / Semi Pro

If budget_preference = "premium":

Prefer Pro / Elite only and maybe exclude Developing

If preferred_tier is specified:

Filter to at least that tier where possible, or give a bonus in TierScore.

This logic is part of the scoring, but you can optionally convert some into hard constraints:

Example: If preferred_tier = "Elite" and there are Elite candidates, don’t consider lower tiers.

6. How Module 5 plugs into other modules
Module 1 (Booking Engine):

Calls Module 5 when auto_match is needed at DraftBooking or Booking creation.

Uses request_sent_at, request_expires_at, and status transitions to drive the offer lifecycle.

Module 2 (Payments & Credits):

Not directly involved, but which cleaner you assign controls whose rates and payout_percentage get snapped.

Module 3 (Payout Engine):

Cleaner assignment ultimately determines Booking.payout_percentage_at_accept and thus the cleaner’s CleanerEarning.

Module 4 (Pricing Engine):

Price is based on the chosen cleaner’s CleanerProfile rates & tier, which Smart Match selects.

Module 6 (Reliability Engine):

Will update CleanerProfile.reliability_score, metrics, and possibly affect matching weights or thresholds over time.

If you’re ready, next I can do Module 6 — Reliability & Tier Engine (how all the performance metrics auto-update, how cleaners move between Developing → Semi Pro → Pro → Elite, and how that feeds back into pricing + SmartMatch).


 PLZ REVIW AND ANALYZE MODULE 5 FOR ANY MISTAKES

Here’s the no-BS review of Module 5.

Short version:
Your Smart Match design is strong and aligned with Base44, but there are a few schema mismatches and a couple of status / field naming issues we should clean up so it drops straight into Base44 without surprises.

1️⃣ Schema alignment issues
1. DraftBooking.auto_match doesn’t exist (yet)
In Module 5 I used:

DraftBooking.auto_match = true/false

But the actual DraftBooking schema only has:

cleaner_email (primary)

plus pricing flow fields like total_savings_from_bundles, current_step, expires_at

🔧 Fix:
Either:

Add auto_match (boolean) to DraftBooking schema, or

Infer auto-match mode as:

“auto-match” if cleaner_email is empty when client submits

“manual selection” if cleaner_email is already set

Right now, Module 5 talks about auto_match as if it exists; that should be explicitly defined as a new field.

2. Booking already has fallback_cleaners & primary_cleaner_email
Actual Booking schema already includes:

client_email

cleaner_email

fallback_cleaners (array of emails)

primary_cleaner_email

matched_via_smart_algorithm (boolean)

is_instant_book (boolean)

In Module 5 I mentioned an extra idea like:

That’s unnecessary because Booking.fallback_cleaners already exists.

🔧 Fix:

When we create Booking from DraftBooking:

Set Booking.primary_cleaner_email = top[0]

Set Booking.cleaner_email = top[0]

Set Booking.fallback_cleaners = [top[1..N]]

Set Booking.matched_via_smart_algorithm = true

Set Booking.is_instant_book accordingly

And don’t invent fallback_cleaners_metadata unless you explicitly add it to the schema.

3. Recurring entity name is correct ✅
Module 5 uses RecurringBooking, which is actually a real entity:

client_email, cleaner_email, frequency, day_of_week, start_time, hours, address, etc.

Recurring scheduling description also references RecurringBooking

✅ So all references to RecurringBooking in Module 5 are correct.

(There is also a CleaningSubscription entity, but that’s more billing/subscription oriented; using RecurringBooking for scheduling is aligned with the docs.)

4. Availability & instant book fields are real ✅
CleanerProfile does have:

service_locations (array of strings)

availability (day, available, start_time, end_time)

instant_book_enabled (boolean) and instant_book_hours

specialty_tags, product_preference with eco-friendly | professional-grade | premium-eco etc.

So all the matching & scoring that relies on these fields is compatible with Base44.

Only caveat: distance math (see below).

2️⃣ Status / lifecycle naming issues
5. I used a wrong status name: offer_declined
Job lifecycle in Base44 uses this enum:

created

payment_hold

awaiting_cleaner_response

accepted

cleaner_declined

checking_fallback

scheduled

reschedule_requested

on_the_way

in_progress

completed

awaiting_client

approved

cancelled

disputed

In Module 5 I said:

“on status = offer_declined … then auto-swap”

❌ That status does not exist.

🔧 Fix:

Use:

cleaner_declined → when cleaner explicitly declines

checking_fallback → system is moving to next cleaner

So your auto-swap automation should trigger on:

Booking.status changes to cleaner_declined, OR

now > request_expires_at while status is awaiting_cleaner_response

Then set status to checking_fallback while assigning the next cleaner.

6. I invented unmatched status
I said:

“If no fallback cleaners remain, set Booking.status = unmatched.”

There is no unmatched in the enum.

🔧 Fix:

Choose a realistic fallback:

Either:

Keep status = created or awaiting_cleaner_response and notify ops

Or:

Set status = cancelled and add a reason, OR log an Event / SupportTicket for manual rescue

We can keep the concept (“no match found”), but the STATUS must stick to the existing list unless we explicitly change the Booking schema.

3️⃣ Data / scoring edge cases
7. DistanceScore vs actual data
Module 5 computes:

distance_in_miles(cleaner, booking_address)

Right now:

RecurringBooking has latitude and longitude for the address

But CleanerProfile does NOT currently have latitude/longitude in the schema snippet; it only has service_locations (strings)

So distance-based scoring is conceptually correct, but:

You either need to add lat/long to CleanerProfile

Or treat DistanceScore as:

1.0 if client’s city/zip is in service_locations

Possibly add a simple “zone distance” later

Right now, my formula assumes geo coordinates are available for cleaners; that’s a proposed enhancement, not something you already have.

8. SmartMatchPreference vs ClientProfile overlap
We have:

ClientProfile.preferred_specialty_tags

SmartMatchPreference.preferred_specialty_tags

Module 5 uses SmartMatchPreference.preferred_specialty_tags. That’s fine, but to be exact:

🔧 Clarify rule:

If SmartMatchPreference exists → use it

Else fallback to ClientProfile.preferred_specialty_tags

Not a bug, just something to make explicit later.

9. BudgetFitScore & “market” knowledge
I said:

“Rank cleaners by base_rate and map to 0–1 for BudgetFitScore.”

That’s implementable within the candidate set, but just to be clear:

There’s no global market_average_rate field anywhere; you’d compute relative to the candidate pool for this job.

Again, not a Base44 mismatch, just an implementation detail to remember.

4️⃣ Extra fields I implied but don’t exist yet
These are optional improvements, not errors, but they are not in the current schema:

DraftBooking.auto_match (boolean)

Any enriched Booking.pricing_breakdown / applied_pricing_labels fields (these were introduced in Module 4 too)

A “soft flag” like Booking.auto_match_failed_reason (I only described the concept, not the field)

As long as we label these as new fields we’re adding, it’s fine.

Use of SmartMatchPreference (all fields & defaults)

Use of FavoriteCleaner, BlockedCleaner, BlockedUser for relationship overrides

Conceptually, the candidate filtering, scoring model, and fallback routing are all good — we just needed to align a few field names and statuses.

Replace offer_declined → cleaner_declined and use checking_fallback during auto-swap.

🧩 MODULE 5 — SMART MATCH ENGINE (FINAL VERSION)
1. Scope
Module 5 decides:

Which cleaners are eligible for a booking

How they are ranked

How we choose the primary cleaner

How we build & use fallback_cleaners for auto-swap

How we respect:

client preferences

cleaner availability

geography

reliability / tier

favorites / blocks

recurring “same cleaner” loyalty

instant-book rules

It only selects cleaners & order — it doesn’t change payments, credits, or payouts.

2. Entities Used
2.1 Booking
Key fields for matching:

client_email

cleaner_email

primary_cleaner_email

fallback_cleaners (array of cleaner emails)

matched_via_smart_algorithm (boolean)

is_instant_book (boolean)

date

start_time

estimated_hours

address / location (city, postal, plus lat/lng if available)

Status lifecycle:
created → payment_hold → awaiting_cleaner_response → accepted → cleaner_declined → checking_fallback → scheduled → ...

We’ll use awaiting_cleaner_response, cleaner_declined, checking_fallback, and request_sent_at / request_expires_at for routing behavior.

2.2 DraftBooking
Used in the booking flow before Booking is created:

client_email

cleaner_email (optional — if empty, we auto-match)

fallback_cleaners (array of backup cleaners)

(Optional new field we can add):

auto_match (boolean)

true if client said “find me the best cleaner”

false if they manually picked a specific cleaner

If we don’t add auto_match, we can infer:

Auto-match mode = DraftBooking.cleaner_email is empty when they confirm.

2.3 CleanerProfile
Used for filters & scoring:

user_email

is_active

service_locations (cities/zips)

availability (day / start_time / end_time)

tier (Developing / Semi Pro / Pro / Elite)

reliability_score, attendance_rate, punctuality_rate, cancellation_rate, no_show_rate, dispute_rate

average_rating, total_reviews, total_jobs

service_tags, specialty_tags

product_preference (standard | eco-friendly | professional-grade | premium-eco)

instant_book_enabled, instant_book_hours

typical_acceptance_rate_by_time (map key like "Mon_09-12" → %)

If we add lat/lng for cleaners later, we use that for precise distance; until then we use service area matching.

2.4 Client-related
ClientProfile

preferred_specialty_tags (optional)

other profile info

SmartMatchPreference

preferred_specialty_tags[]

preferred_tier (any | Pro | Elite)

max_distance_miles

preferred_product_type (any | eco-friendly | professional-grade)

budget_preference (budget | standard | premium)

same_cleaner_preferred (boolean)

FavoriteCleaner

relation: client_email, cleaner_email

BlockedCleaner

BlockedUser

RecurringBooking

for recurring “same cleaner” logic

2.5 Analytics / Feedback
AnalyticsEvent

used to record: cleaner_selected, backup_selected, job_viewed_by_cleaner, job_accepted_by_cleaner, job_declined_by_cleaner, etc.

3. Candidate Filters (HARD constraints)
Given a booking B (or draft booking D), a cleaner C is eligible if ALL are true:

Active profile

C.is_active = true

Not blocked

No BlockedCleaner row for (B.client_email, C.user_email)

No BlockedUser row where:

blocker_email = B.client_email

blocked_email = C.user_email

Within service area

B’s area (city/zip) is in C.service_locations

If/when we add lat/lng:

distance_miles(C, B.address) ≤ SmartMatchPreference.max_distance_miles (or a default, e.g. 15)

Available for time window

For Booking.date’s day-of-week:

there exists an availability entry where:

available = true

start_time <= booking.start_time

end_time >= booking.start_time + estimated_hours

Offers required service

Basic / deep / moveout always OK if they do “standard home clean”

For specialized jobs (e.g. post-construction, move-out heavy), ensure C’s service_tags / specialty_tags include required tags

No hard admin flags (optional)

If Reliability Engine marks C as temporarily suspended, exclude.

Only cleaners surviving all these are candidates.

4. SmartMatch Score (SOFT ranking)
For each candidate cleaner C and booking B, compute a SmartMatchScore to rank them.

4.1 Scoring components (0–1 each)
You can tune weights later; we just define a good baseline.

DistanceScore

If we have real geo:

d = distance_miles(C, B.address)

d_max = SmartMatchPreference.max_distance_miles (or default)

DistanceScore = 1 - (d / d_max) (clamped to [0,1])

If we only have service zones:

DistanceScore = 1.0 for same city/zip

DistanceScore = 0.7 for nearby region

DistanceScore = 0.4 otherwise (if still acceptable)

ReliabilityScoreNorm

ReliabilityScoreNorm = C.reliability_score / 100

RatingScore

Use average_rating (1–5)

RatingScore = clamp((average_rating - 3) / 2, 0, 1)

TierScore

Base mapping:

Developing → 0.3

Semi Pro → 0.6

Pro → 0.85

Elite → 1.0

If SmartMatchPreference.preferred_tier = "Pro" and C.tier is Pro/Elite → +0.05 (capped at 1.0)

If preferred_tier = "Elite" and C.tier is Elite → +0.1 (capped at 1.0)

SpecialtyMatchScore

Get preferred_specialties from:

SmartMatchPreference.preferred_specialty_tags if present,

else ClientProfile.preferred_specialty_tags

If none specified → SpecialtyMatchScore = 0.5

Else:

SpecialtyMatchScore = overlap(preferred_specialties, C.specialty_tags) / len(preferred_specialties)

ProductPreferenceScore

Compare SmartMatchPreference.preferred_product_type vs C.product_preference:

Exact match → 1.0

Client says any → 0.7

Mismatch → 0.2

LoyaltyScore

If this booking is part of a RecurringBooking with C.user_email as assigned cleaner → 1.0

Else if FavoriteCleaner exists for (client, cleaner) → 0.9

Else if same_cleaner_preferred = true and C did last booking for this client → 0.8

Else → 0.3

AcceptanceLikelihoodScore

Use C.typical_acceptance_rate_by_time with key like "Tue_09-12"

If missing → 0.5

Else: AcceptanceLikelihoodScore = rate / 100

BudgetFitScore

Based on SmartMatchPreference.budget_preference:

budget:

Lower base_rate_cph = higher score (rank among candidates)

premium:

Higher tier & higher base_rate_cph = higher score

standard:

Middle-of-pack base_rate / tier = higher score

Implementation:
Within the candidate set, normalize cleaners’ base_rate_cph to [0,1] and flip/weight according to preference.

4.2 Weights & score formula
Baseline weights (total ≈ 1.0):

DistanceScore: 0.15

ReliabilityScoreNorm: 0.20

RatingScore: 0.10

TierScore: 0.10

SpecialtyMatchScore: 0.10

ProductPreferenceScore: 0.05

LoyaltyScore: 0.20

AcceptanceLikelihoodScore: 0.05

BudgetFitScore: 0.05

Final:

SmartMatchScore =
  0.15 * DistanceScore +
  0.20 * ReliabilityScoreNorm +
  0.10 * RatingScore +
  0.10 * TierScore +
  0.10 * SpecialtyMatchScore +
  0.05 * ProductPreferenceScore +
  0.20 * LoyaltyScore +
  0.05 * AcceptanceLikelihoodScore +
  0.05 * BudgetFitScore
Sort candidates descending by SmartMatchScore.

5. Routing Logic (Primary + Fallbacks)
5.1 Instant Book vs Request Mode
Instant Book rules:

Instant book is allowed if:

C.instant_book_enabled = true

Booking is at least C.instant_book_hours in the future

Cleaner passes all filters

ReliabilityScoreNorm ≥ some threshold (e.g. 0.8)

When client starts booking:

If they specifically picked a cleaner who is instant-book eligible:

Set is_instant_book = true

If they chose “fastest available” and SmartMatch top cleaner is instant-book eligible:

Optionally auto-set is_instant_book = true and assign them immediately.

Non-instant / Request mode:

Cleaner must explicitly accept job.

Booking uses statuses awaiting_cleaner_response, cleaner_declined, checking_fallback.

5.2 Where SmartMatch writes its output
When SmartMatch runs (on DraftBooking confirm or Booking creation):

Take top N cleaners by SmartMatchScore (e.g., N = 5–10).

Choose:

primary = top[0]

fallbacks = [top[1], top[2], ... top[N-1]]

On DraftBooking:

If auto-match path:

DraftBooking.cleaner_email = primary

DraftBooking.fallback_cleaners = fallbacks

On Booking creation:

Booking.primary_cleaner_email = primary

Booking.cleaner_email = primary (initial assigned)

Booking.fallback_cleaners = fallbacks

Booking.matched_via_smart_algorithm = true

Booking.is_instant_book = true/false (based on logic above)

6. Automations (Module 5)
5.1 — SmartMatch on DraftBooking (auto-match flow)
Trigger: DraftBooking updated

Condition (auto-match mode):

Client reached “Review & Confirm” step

Either:

DraftBooking.auto_match = true, or

DraftBooking.cleaner_email is empty at confirmation

Required fields present: client_email, address, date, start_time, estimated_hours, cleaning_type

Actions:

Build candidate set using filters in Section 3.

For each candidate, compute SmartMatchScore.

Sort desc, take top N.

Set:

DraftBooking.cleaner_email = top[0].email

DraftBooking.fallback_cleaners = [top[1..N].email]

Optionally log AnalyticsEvent:

event_type = "cleaner_selected"

user_type = "client"

metadata = { primary_cleaner_email, fallback_count }

This runs before we convert DraftBooking → Booking.

5.2 — On Booking.created → ensure SmartMatch data is present
This pairs with Module 1’s Booking creation automation.

Trigger: Booking created

Condition:

Booking.matched_via_smart_algorithm is null or false

AND Booking does not have cleaner_email set (or we want to recompute)

Actions:

If Booking was created from a DraftBooking that already has cleaner_email + fallback_cleaners:

Just copy:

primary_cleaner_email = DraftBooking.cleaner_email

cleaner_email = DraftBooking.cleaner_email

fallback_cleaners = DraftBooking.fallback_cleaners

matched_via_smart_algorithm = true

Else:

Run full SmartMatch pipeline (filters + scoring + sort).

Set Booking fields:

primary_cleaner_email = top[0]

cleaner_email = top[0]

fallback_cleaners = [top[1..N]]

matched_via_smart_algorithm = true

If is_instant_book = false:

Set Booking.request_sent_at = now

Set Booking.request_expires_at = now + RESPONSE_WINDOW_MINUTES

Set Booking.status = "awaiting_cleaner_response"

5.3 — Cleaner accepts / declines
These events come from the cleaner UI:

Accept: sets Booking.status = "accepted"

Decline: sets Booking.status = "cleaner_declined"

We’ll piggyback on Module 1’s Booking Engine, but SmartMatch cares about decline to trigger fallback.

5.4 — Fallback auto-swap on decline or timeout
Trigger A: Booking updated

Condition A:

old.status = "awaiting_cleaner_response"

new.status = "cleaner_declined"

Trigger B: Scheduled/cron check every X minutes

Condition B:

Booking.status = "awaiting_cleaner_response"

now > Booking.request_expires_at

Actions (same for A & B):

Mark current cleaner as “tried”. We can track this implicitly by checking if they’re the primary or using an internal index, or by maintaining a tried_cleaners list (optional new field).

From Booking.fallback_cleaners, select the next cleaner not yet tried.

If a next cleaner exists:

Set:

Booking.cleaner_email = next_cleaner_email

Booking.status = "awaiting_cleaner_response"

Booking.request_sent_at = now

Booking.request_expires_at = now + RESPONSE_WINDOW_MINUTES

Log AnalyticsEvent:

event_type = "backup_selected"

metadata = { booking_id, cleaner_email: next_cleaner_email }

Notify that cleaner.

If no fallback cleaner remains:

Do NOT set status to unmatched (it doesn’t exist).

Options:

Set Booking.status = "created" (back to admin/manual handling) and:

create SupportTicket / internal alert, OR

Set Booking.status = "cancelled" and log a cancellation_reason = "system_no_match" for Module 2 to handle refunds.

Also notify client that no cleaner was available (and trigger refund logic via Module 2).

5.5 — Recurring / “Same Cleaner” preference
Trigger: When a new Booking is generated from a RecurringBooking.

Condition:

RecurringBooking.cleaner_email is set

OR the last booking for that recurring series had a given cleaner

SmartMatchPreference.same_cleaner_preferred = true for that client

Actions:

Check if recurring cleaner:

Is active

Not blocked

Available at recurring time

Passes basic filters

If yes:

Set Booking.primary_cleaner_email = recurring_cleaner

Set Booking.cleaner_email = recurring_cleaner

Still compute fallback cleaners using SmartMatch for backup.

If no:

Run SmartMatch as normal to choose a new primary and fallbacks.

5.6 — Acceptance feedback loop
When cleaners receive opportunities and respond, we update their acceptance profile.

Trigger: AnalyticsEvent created with event_type in:

job_viewed_by_cleaner

job_accepted_by_cleaner

job_declined_by_cleaner

Actions:

Derive time-slot key:

e.g., "Mon_09-12" from Booking.date & Booking.start_time

Increment stats for that cleaner + key:

offers_count++

accepts_count++ (for accepted events)

Recalculate:

acceptance_rate = accepts_count / offers_count * 100

Update CleanerProfile.typical_acceptance_rate_by_time[key] = acceptance_rate.

This feeds AcceptanceLikelihoodScore in the future.

7. Summary
Module 5 now:

Uses only real statuses (awaiting_cleaner_response, cleaner_declined, checking_fallback, cancelled, etc.), no fake offer_declined / unmatched.

Uses existing Booking fields:

primary_cleaner_email

fallback_cleaners

matched_via_smart_algorithm

is_instant_book

Treats DraftBooking.auto_match as optional new field, or infers from missing cleaner_email.

Treats distance as:

Real mileage if we add geo to cleaners, or

zone-based approximation until then.

Has a clear candidate filter → scoring → sort → primary + fallback routing pipeline.

Plays nicely with:

Module 1 (Booking engine & statuses)

Module 2 (cancellation_reason = "system_no_match" for refunds)

Module 3 (which cleaner ultimately gets the payout)

Module 4 (price comes from the chosen cleaner’s rates & tier)

If you want, next we can move on to Module 6 — Reliability & Tier Engine and define exactly how all those cleaner metrics move them between Developing → Semi Pro → Pro → Elite and feed back into SmartMatch + pricing.
