🧱 MODULE 6 — RELIABILITY & TIER ENGINE
1. Scope
Module 6 owns:

All cleaner performance metrics

The reliability_score (0–100)

Cleaner tier (Developing → Semi Pro → Pro → Elite)

tier_progress (how close to the next tier)

Badges & milestones (ReliabilityBadge, CleanerMilestone)

How reliability affects:

Smart Match (Module 5)

Pricing / payout percentage

Instant book eligibility

Penalties for no-shows / disputes

It works mostly via booking events + reviews, exactly how Base44 describes its built-in reliability system.

2. Entities Involved
2.1 CleanerProfile (core storage)
From your schema, CleanerProfile already has:

reliability_score (0–100)

tier (Developing | Semi Pro | Pro | Elite)

tier_progress (object: current_jobs, jobs_to_next_tier, current_score, score_to_next_tier)

Metrics:

attendance_rate

punctuality_rate

cancellation_rate

completion_confirmation_rate

photo_proof_rate

communication_rate

average_rating

total_reviews

total_jobs

no_show_rate

dispute_rate

profile_completeness

current_streak_days, best_streak_days

last_score_update

Base44 docs explicitly say these are updated by background automation based on Booking & Review events.

2.2 Booking + Review + Dispute + PhotoPair
Booking – provides:

status, date, start_time, check_in_time, check_out_time, actual_hours

photo_proof_submitted, photo_count

cancellation & no-show/statuses

Review – provides:

rating, on_time, photo_quality, would_recommend, product_quality etc.

Dispute – provides disputes & categories: no_show, late_arrival, quality_issue, damage, etc.

PhotoPair – per-area before/after photo logs.

Docs confirm that all of these feed reliability metrics (attendance, punctuality, cancellation, photo proof, communication, no-show, dispute, rating).

2.3 Analytics & Achievements
CleanerAnalytics – per-day snapshot: total_earnings, bookings_count, hours_worked, average_rating, etc.

ReliabilityBadge – badges like always_on_time, 30_day_streak, great_communicator, etc.

CleanerMilestone – big milestones like first_10_jobs, earnings_1000, reliability_elite.

3. Metric Definitions
We define the canonical formulas for each metric that CleanerProfile stores. These run either:

daily (cron), aggregating all time or last X days, and/or

event-based on booking_complete, review_submitted, dispute_resolved.

3.1 Attendance Rate
How often does this cleaner actually complete jobs they accept?

Numerator:

completed_jobs = count(bookings where cleaner accepted AND status ∈ {completed, approved})

Denominator:

assigned_jobs = count(bookings where cleaner_email = C AND status ∈ {accepted, scheduled, completed, approved, cancelled_by_cleaner, no_show})

Formula:

attendance_rate = (completed_jobs / assigned_jobs) * 100
Edge case: if assigned_jobs = 0, default 100.

3.2 Punctuality Rate
How often do they show up on time?

Using Booking start_time, check_in_time:

On-time if check_in_time ≤ start_time + 10min (configurable).

punctual_jobs = # with on_time
punctuality_rate = (punctual_jobs / completed_jobs) * 100
If no completed jobs, default 100.

3.3 Cancellation Rate
% of jobs they cancel.

cleaner_cancellations = count(bookings where status = cancelled AND cancel_reason = "cleaner_cancelled")

total_accepted = total jobs they accepted (same denominator as attendance)

cancellation_rate = (cleaner_cancellations / total_accepted) * 100
3.4 No-Show Rate
% of jobs where they simply didn’t show.

no_shows = count(bookings where status = "no_show_by_cleaner")

Denominator: total_accepted again.

no_show_rate = (no_shows / total_accepted) * 100
Docs mention No-Show Rate tracked via booking statuses + Dispute.

3.5 Completion Confirmation Rate
Do they correctly confirm jobs via checklist?

jobs_marked_completed_by_cleaner = count(bookings where cleaner marked completed)

jobs_expected_completion = total_accepted - cancelled_by_client_before_start

completion_confirmation_rate =
  jobs_marked_completed_by_cleaner / jobs_expected_completion * 100
3.6 Photo Proof Rate
Do they consistently upload required before/after photos?

Using photo_proof_submitted & photo_count on Booking & PhotoPair:

photo_required_jobs = count(bookings where photo proof required by policy)

photo_compliant_jobs = count of those with photo_proof_submitted = true AND photo_count ≥ MIN_REQUIRED

photo_proof_rate = (photo_compliant_jobs / photo_required_jobs) * 100
If none required yet, default 100.

3.7 Communication Rate
Are they responsive & clear?

This is partly subjective; we can approximate using:

Response time in ConversationThread / messages

Review fields like would_recommend and any communication tag.

Simplified:

good_comms_bookings = bookings where review.would_recommend = true OR flagged as good communication

rated_bookings = bookings with reviews

communication_rate = (good_comms_bookings / rated_bookings) * 100
3.8 Average Rating & Total Reviews
From Review entity:

average_rating = weighted avg of Review.rating
total_reviews = count(Review where cleaner_email = C)
We can weight more recent reviews higher if desired, but baseline is simple average.

3.9 Dispute Rate
How often are jobs disputed?

disputed_jobs = count(disputes where cleaner_email = C AND category != "payment_issue")

completed_jobs as defined above.

dispute_rate = (disputed_jobs / completed_jobs) * 100
We can treat quality_issue, damage, safety_concern, etc. as heavier than others.

3.10 Profile Completeness
Simple checklist:

profile_photo_url present

bio length ≥ X

At least one service_location

At least one service_tag

Product preferences set

Video intro added

profile_completeness = (# completed items / # total items) * 100
3.11 Job Streaks
current_streak_days, best_streak_days

We define a reliable day as: at least one job where:

status ∈ {completed, approved}

no no_show, no cleaner-cancellation

on-time, with photos uploaded if required.

Then:

Sort days chronologically; track current continuous run of reliable days;

Update current_streak_days and best_streak_days.

This feeds badges like 30_day_streak & always_on_time.

4. Reliability Score Formula (0–100)
Now we convert all the metrics → a single reliability_score.

We’ll use a weighted average:

Attendance: 20%

Punctuality: 15%

Cancellation: 10% (inverted)

No-show: 15% (inverted, heavy)

Completion confirmation: 10%

Photo proof: 10%

Communication: 5%

Rating: 10%

Dispute: 5% (inverted)

First, normalize each metric to 0–100 in the “good is high” direction:

attendance_score = attendance_rate

punctuality_score = punctuality_rate

cancellation_score = 100 - cancellation_rate

no_show_score = 100 - no_show_rate

completion_score = completion_confirmation_rate

photo_score = photo_proof_rate

communication_score = communication_rate

rating_score = ((average_rating - 1) / 4) * 100 (1–5 → 0–100)

dispute_score = 100 - dispute_rate

Then:

reliability_score =
  0.20 * attendance_score +
  0.15 * punctuality_score +
  0.10 * cancellation_score +
  0.15 * no_show_score +
  0.10 * completion_score +
  0.10 * photo_score +
  0.05 * communication_score +
  0.10 * rating_score +
  0.05 * dispute_score
Clamp to [0, 100].

Tell Base44 to write:

CleanerProfile.reliability_score = reliability_score

last_score_update = now()

Docs confirm this is exactly what the reliability system is supposed to do.

5. Tier Logic (Developing → Semi Pro → Pro → Elite)
We define clear thresholds using:

reliability_score

total_jobs

no_show_rate

dispute_rate

Example baseline:

Tier	Min Jobs	Min Reliability	Max No-show	Max Dispute
Developing	0	— (any)	—	—
Semi Pro	≥ 10	≥ 70	≤ 5%	≤ 5%
Pro	≥ 30	≥ 85	≤ 3%	≤ 3%
Elite	≥ 75	≥ 95	≤ 1%	≤ 1%
Exact numbers are tunable via config / FeatureFlag later; the important part is consistent rules.

5.1 Tier Assignment
After computing reliability_score and metrics:

Determine highest tier where cleaner meets all conditions.

If none beyond Developing → stay Developing.

5.2 Tier Progress (tier_progress)
tier_progress uses:

current_jobs = total_jobs

jobs_to_next_tier = min_jobs_for_next_tier - total_jobs (or 0 if already there)

current_score = reliability_score

score_to_next_tier = max(0, min_score_for_next_tier - reliability_score)

This is what Base44 docs reference when they say tier_progress tracks movement toward the next tier.

5.3 Tier Effects
Tie back into other modules:

Pricing (Module 4):

Tier → allowed base_rate_credits_per_hour ranges (Developing cheaper, Elite higher).

Payout % (Module 3):

Tier affects payout_percentage (e.g. 0.8 for most, 0.85 for Elite).

Smart Match (Module 5):

TierScore used for SmartMatch ranking.

Instant Book:

Only allow instant_book_enabled = true if tier ≥ Semi Pro & reliability_score ≥ 80.

6. Badges & Milestones
We’ll define automations that write ReliabilityBadge + CleanerMilestone.

6.1 ReliabilityBadge
Schemas already exist for: always_on_time, 30_day_streak, documented_pro, great_communicator, trusted_professional.

Examples:

Condition: punctuality_rate ≥ 95% over last 30 days.

30_day_streak

Condition: current_streak_days ≥ 30.

documented_pro

Condition: photo_proof_rate ≥ 95% over last 50 jobs.

great_communicator

Condition: communication_rate ≥ 90% over last 20 reviews.

trusted_professional

Condition: reliability_score ≥ 95 and dispute_rate ≤ 1% and no_show_rate = 0 over last 6 months.

Automation:

Evaluate all badge conditions.

If condition becomes true and badge not present → create ReliabilityBadge (is_displayed=true by default).

If condition no longer true and we want time-limited badges → optionally set expires_at.

6.2 CleanerMilestone
You already have milestone types like: first_10_jobs, first_50_jobs, perfect_month, earnings_1000, reliability_elite.

Examples:

first_10_jobs:

total_jobs crosses 10 for the first time.

earnings_1000:

cumulative earnings cross $1000.

reliability_elite:

reliability_score ≥ 95 for 30 consecutive days.

Automation:

After daily aggregation:

Check each milestone’s condition.

If achieved and not previously created:

Create CleanerMilestone with:

reward_type (e.g., bonus_percentage, priority_listing, free_instant_payout)

reward_value (like +0.05 payout for 30 days)

Optionally map milestones → FeatureFlags or perks.

7. Automations for Module 6
7.1 Event-based triggers
1) On Booking status changes

Actions:

Once per day (e.g. ~3am platform time):

For each active cleaner:

Aggregate:

bookings for last X days or all-time

disputes

reviews

photo stats

total_jobs

all metric fields

last_score_update = now()

Upsert CleanerAnalytics snapshot for that date.

7.3 Badge & Milestone awarding

Run badge rules (Section 6.1).

Run milestone rules (Section 6.2).

Create any new ReliabilityBadge / CleanerMilestone records.

8. How Module 6 feeds other modules

in SmartMatch scoring.

First: what I’m fixing vs the earlier version
Based on your Base44 docs:

Reliability lives on CleanerProfile + CleanerAnalytics
Metrics like reliability_score, attendance_rate, punctuality_rate, cancellation_rate, average_rating, total_jobs, tier, tier_progress, last_score_update are explicitly mentioned there.

Metrics are sourced from Booking, Review, Dispute + timestamps/flags
Attendance, punctuality, cancellations, completion confirmations, photo proof, communication rate, no-show rate, dispute rate all come from Booking fields & Dispute entities.

Job lifecycle statuses are a fixed enum – we should not invent new status strings like no_show_by_cleaner. We work with what you actually have:
created, payment_hold, awaiting_cleaner_response, accepted, cleaner_declined, checking_fallback, scheduled, reschedule_requested, on_the_way, in_progress, completed, awaiting_client, approved, cancelled, disputed.

✅ MODULE 6 – Reliability & Tier Engine (CLEAN VERSION)
6.1 Goals & Scope
Goal:
Maintain an up-to-date reliability system for cleaners that:

Calculates key performance metrics from Booking, Review, Dispute, and Message/Event data.

Updates CleanerProfile.reliability_score, tier, and tier_progress on a schedule.

Triggers CleanerMilestone records when major achievements happen.

Out of scope for this module (but used):

How bookings are created or priced (handled in Booking/Pricing modules).

How payouts are calculated (handled in Payments/Payout modules).

6.2 Entities Used
We only use existing Base44 entities:

CleanerProfile

Key fields:

user_email

reliability_score

tier (enum: Developing, Semi Pro, Pro, Elite)

tier_progress (object: current_jobs, jobs_to_next_tier, current_score, score_to_next_tier)

attendance_rate, punctuality_rate, cancellation_rate,
completion_confirmation_rate, photo_proof_rate,
communication_rate, average_rating, total_reviews,
total_jobs, no_show_rate, dispute_rate,
current_streak_days, best_streak_days, last_score_update, etc.

CleanerAnalytics

Stores daily/periodic aggregates per cleaner (earnings, booking counts, rating snapshots).

Booking

Fields used:

client_email, cleaner_email

status (job lifecycle statuses)

date, start_time, hours, check_in_time, check_out_time, actual_hours

photo_proof_submitted, photo_count, review_submitted

cancellation_timestamp (and any cancelled_by / equivalent flag if present)

Review

booking_id, cleaner_email, rating, and any performance flags (e.g. communication).

Dispute

booking_id, filed_by, category (includes no_show, quality_issue, etc.), status.

Message / ConversationThread (optional for communication rate)

Used to infer responsiveness (if we want a more advanced comms metric).

CleanerMilestone

cleaner_email, milestone_type, reward_type, earned_date.

6.3 Metric Definitions (How we calculate each one)
We compute metrics over a rolling window (e.g. last 90 days) plus all-time totals. Window length can be a config later.

Let:

BOOKINGS = all Booking records for this cleaner in the window.

COMPLETED = bookings where status ∈ {completed, awaiting_client, approved}.

SCHEDULED = bookings where status reached at least scheduled and wasn’t cancelled before the start.

1. Attendance Rate

Did you actually show up and complete jobs you were scheduled for?

Numerator: count of COMPLETED.

Denominator: count of SCHEDULED.

Formula:
attendance_rate = (COMPLETED / max(1, SCHEDULED)) * 100

2. Punctuality Rate

How often did you arrive “on time”?

Use check_in_time vs start_time.

A job is on-time if check_in_time <= start_time + lateness_threshold (e.g. 10–15 minutes).

Numerator: # of completed bookings where cleaner is on-time.

Denominator: # of completed bookings with a non-null check_in_time.

Formula:
punctuality_rate = (on_time_jobs / max(1, completed_with_checkin)) * 100

3. Cancellation Rate

How often did the cleaner cancel?

From Booking data; Base44 explicitly says cancellation rate is from “cancellations initiated by the cleaner”.

Define cleaner_cancelled bookings as:

status = 'cancelled' AND cancelled_by = 'cleaner' (or equivalent field),

OR, if there’s no explicit field, use Event/Dispute data tagged as cleaner-driven cancellation.

Numerator: # cleaner_cancelled bookings in window.

Denominator: # bookings that reached at least scheduled.

Formula:
cancellation_rate = (cleaner_cancelled / max(1, SCHEDULED)) * 100

4. Completion Confirmation Rate

Do they properly close out jobs?

A job is confirmed if:

status ∈ {completed, awaiting_client, approved}

AND check_in_time and check_out_time are set (job actually worked).

Numerator: completed bookings with valid check-in/out.

Denominator: completed bookings.

Formula:
completion_confirmation_rate = (confirmed_jobs / max(1, COMPLETED)) * 100

5. Photo Proof Rate

Do they upload required before/after photos?

Booking provides photo_proof_submitted and photo_count.

A job is photo-compliant if:

photo_proof_submitted = true

AND photo_count >= min_required_photos (configurable per job type).

Numerator: # photo-compliant completed jobs.

Denominator: # completed jobs.

Formula:
photo_proof_rate = (photo_compliant / max(1, COMPLETED)) * 100

6. Communication Rate

Do they respond and communicate well?

Docs say it’s based on Messages + client reviews.

Implementation suggestion:

From Message / ConversationThread:

Compute median response time to client messages during active bookings.

Flag if they ghost (client messages unanswered for > X hours).

From Review:

Use any communication-related sub-rating, or infer from tags/comments.

We can normalize this to a 0–100 score (where 100 is fast, consistent communication) using thresholds (e.g. <5min avg = 100, >2h avg = 60, ghosting = penalties).

7. Average Rating & Total Reviews

From Review entity.

average_rating = sum(rating) / max(1, count(reviews))

total_reviews = count(reviews)

8. No-Show Rate

Docs say: “No-Show Rate & Dispute Rate: tracked through specific Booking statuses and Dispute entities.”

Implementation:

A job is no-show for the cleaner if:

Either Booking.status hits a dedicated “no_show” status (if configured in your enum),

OR there is a Dispute on that booking with category = 'no_show' and filed_by = 'client'.

Numerator: # no-show bookings in window.

Denominator: # SCHEDULED bookings (same as attendance).

Formula:
no_show_rate = (no_show_bookings / max(1, SCHEDULED)) * 100

9. Dispute Rate

How often do jobs turn into disputes?

Numerator: # bookings with an associated Dispute (any category) where status ∈ {open, investigating, resolved, closed}.

Denominator: # completed/approved jobs.

Formula:
dispute_rate = (disputed_bookings / max(1, COMPLETED)) * 100

10. Streaks & Totals

total_jobs = total Booking records where cleaner was assigned and job reached completed or approved.

current_streak_days / best_streak_days:

Current streak: consecutive days with at least one completed job and no no-shows, no cleaner cancellations.

Best streak: max of all historical streaks.

These values are written back to CleanerProfile.

6.4 Reliability Score Calculation (Single Composite Score)
We map all these metrics into 0–100 and combine with weights.

Component normalized scores (0–100):

attend_score = attendance_rate

punctuality_score = punctuality_rate

cancel_score = max(0, 100 - (cancellation_rate * cancel_penalty_factor))

no_show_score = max(0, 100 - (no_show_rate * no_show_penalty_factor))

dispute_score = max(0, 100 - (dispute_rate * dispute_penalty_factor))

photo_score = photo_proof_rate

comm_score = communication_rate (already 0–100)

rating_score = (average_rating / 5) * 100

Suggested weights (can be tuned later):

Attendance: 20%

Punctuality: 15%

Cancellations: 10%

No-shows: 20%

Disputes: 10%

Photos: 10%

Communication: 10%

Rating: 5%

Formula:

reliability_score =
  0.20 * attend_score +
  0.15 * punctuality_score +
  0.10 * cancel_score +
  0.20 * no_show_score +
  0.10 * dispute_score +
  0.10 * photo_score +
  0.10 * comm_score +
  0.05 * rating_score
Then we:

Clamp: reliability_score = min(100, max(0, reliability_score))

Optionally smooth using a moving average over time (e.g. 70% previous score, 30% new score) to avoid huge swings from one bad job.

6.5 Tier Rules & Tier Progress
Docs say tiers are: Developing, Semi Pro, Pro, Elite, and are determined by reliability + metrics.

Example rules (these can be tuned):

Developing

reliability_score < 70 OR

total_jobs < 10

Semi Pro

reliability_score ≥ 70 AND

total_jobs ≥ 10

Pro

reliability_score ≥ 80 AND

total_jobs ≥ 50 AND

no_show_rate < 2% AND

cancellation_rate < 5%

Elite

reliability_score ≥ 90 AND

total_jobs ≥ 100 AND

no_show_rate < 1% AND

cancellation_rate < 3% AND

average_rating ≥ 4.8

Tier Progress (CleanerProfile.tier_progress):

For the next tier up, we compute:

jobs_to_next_tier = max(0, required_jobs_for_next_tier - total_jobs)

score_to_next_tier = max(0, required_score_for_next_tier - reliability_score)

current_jobs = total_jobs

current_score = reliability_score

So in the profile you can show something like:

“You’re 15 jobs and 4 reliability points away from Pro.”

6.6 Event Sources & Triggers
We’ll design the engine so it can run via:

Nightly Batch (Primary)

Once per day: recompute metrics and reliability for all active cleaners.

Real-time Lightweight Updates (Optional but nice)

React to key Booking status changes:

in_progress → completed

completed → awaiting_client

awaiting_client → approved

any → cancelled

any → disputed

React to new Review or Dispute creation.

For now we assume the batch job is the source of truth, and real-time updates just make the UI feel snappier.

6.7 Batch Job Algorithm (High-level)
For each cleaner:

Gather data window

Get all Bookings for last N days where cleaner_email = this cleaner.

Get all Reviews for those bookings.

Get all Disputes for those bookings.

Optionally get Messages related to those bookings for comm rate.

Compute base metrics

Attendance, punctuality, cancellation, completion confirmation, photo proof.

No-show rate and dispute rate.

Average rating, total reviews, total jobs.

Streaks.

Compute component scores & reliability_score
Using formulas from 6.3–6.4.

Determine tier & tier_progress

Compare to thresholds from 6.5.

Prepare tier_progress object for next tier.

Write to CleanerProfile

Update:

reliability_score

attendance_rate, punctuality_rate, cancellation_rate,
completion_confirmation_rate, photo_proof_rate, communication_rate,
no_show_rate, dispute_rate

average_rating, total_reviews, total_jobs

tier, tier_progress

current_streak_days, best_streak_days

last_score_update = now()

Record analytics

Insert a CleanerAnalytics record summarizing the day's stats (earnings already handled by other modules).

Check for milestones

total_jobs crosses 10, 50, 100 → create CleanerMilestone with milestone_type = first_10_jobs / first_50_jobs / first_100_jobs.

reliability_score crosses Elite threshold → milestone_type = 'reliability_elite'.

Long streaks or high earnings can map to corresponding milestone enums like perfect_month, earnings_1000, etc.

6.8 Edge Cases & Safeguards
New cleaners with very few jobs

Use minimum denominators to avoid wild swings.

Optionally cap reliability ranges until total_jobs ≥ 5.

Old jobs outside rolling window

Still count toward total_jobs and some milestones.

The score focuses on recent performance to keep reliability current.

Disputes reversed in cleaner’s favor

If Dispute.status = 'resolved' and cleaner not at fault, we can:

Exclude that booking from dispute rate and no-show rate.

Optionally credit their reliability slightly.

Hard penalties for extreme events

No-show where a Dispute is confirmed can give a strong one-time penalty (e.g. subtract 10 points) on top of the rate-based effect.

6.9 Admin Controls (Optional UX Hooks)
For the internal admin panel:

View per-cleaner:

All calculated metrics.

History of reliability_score and tier changes.

List of milestones.

Override options:

Manually set tier (with a note + expiry).

Apply a one-time reliability bonus or penalty.

Turn it into Neon SQL + n8n flows, using Base44 webhooks as the data source.

You pick which stack we wire this into first, and I’ll translate Module 6 into implementation instructions.

✅ MODULE 6 – RELIABILITY & TIER ENGINE (FINAL CLEAN SPEC)
Purpose
The Reliability & Tier Engine maintains an always-accurate assessment of cleaner performance across:

Attendance

Punctuality

Cancellations

No-shows

Completion confirmations

Photo proof compliance

Communication

Disputes

Reviews

Rating & volume

Streaks

Tier

Tier progress

Milestones

All calculations write into the existing CleanerProfile entity and produce CleanerMilestone records when achievements are unlocked.

This system powers:

SmartMatch (Module 5)

Pricing Engine (Module 4)

Instant Book rules

Payout percentages

Quality assurance & trust signals

1. Entities Used
1.1 CleanerProfile
(Base44-native fields; all supported in uploaded docs)

Key fields used:

reliability_score

tier (Developing, Semi Pro, Pro, Elite)

tier_progress

attendance_rate

punctuality_rate

cancellation_rate

completion_confirmation_rate

photo_proof_rate

communication_rate

average_rating

total_jobs

no_show_rate

1.2 Booking
Fields used for metrics:

client_email

cleaner_email

status

date, start_time, hours

check_in_time, check_out_time, actual_hours

photo_proof_submitted, photo_count

review_submitted

cancellation_timestamp or any “cancelled_by” equivalent

Valid statuses (as defined in Base44 docs):
created, payment_hold, awaiting_cleaner_response, accepted, cleaner_declined, checking_fallback, scheduled, reschedule_requested, on_the_way, in_progress, completed, awaiting_client, approved, cancelled, disputed

Fields used:

Used for achievements:

cleaner_email

Stores daily aggregates for historical tracking.

2. Canonical Metric Definitions
All metrics compute over a rolling 90-day window (configurable), plus all-time totals where appropriate.

Let:

BOOKINGS = all bookings for the cleaner within window

COMPLETED = bookings with statuses: completed, awaiting_client, approved

SCHEDULED = bookings that reached at least the scheduled status and were not cancelled before start

2.1 Attendance Rate
“How often does the cleaner complete scheduled jobs?”

attendance_rate =
  COMPLETED / max(1, SCHEDULED) * 100
2.2 Punctuality Rate
Based on check-in relative to start_time.

A job is on-time if:

check_in_time <= start_time + 10 minutes
punctuality_rate =
  on_time_jobs / max(1, completed_with_checkin) * 100
2.3 Cancellation Rate
Count cancellations explicitly triggered by the cleaner.

Cleaner-cancelled job definition:

status = cancelled AND cancelled_by = 'cleaner'

OR a Dispute attached indicating cleaner-caused cancellation.

cancellation_rate =
  cleaner_cancelled / max(1, SCHEDULED) * 100
2.4 Completion Confirmation Rate
Did the cleaner properly confirm job completion?

A job is confirmed if:

Status ∈ completed variants

check_in_time and check_out_time exist

completion_confirmation_rate =
  confirmed_jobs / max(1, COMPLETED) * 100
2.5 Photo Proof Rate
A job is photo-compliant if:

photo_proof_submitted = true

AND photo_count ≥ required_min (policy-based)

photo_proof_rate =
  photo_compliant / max(1, COMPLETED) * 100
2.6 Communication Rate
Derived from:

Response time in Messages / ConversationThread

Communication sentiment in Reviews

Normalization example:

<5 min avg response → 100

5–30 min → 90

30–120 min → 70

2 hours → 40

Ghosting → 0

communication_rate = normalized_score(0–100)
2.7 Average Rating & Total Reviews
average_rating = sum(ratings) / count
total_reviews = count
2.8 No-Show Rate
A job counts as cleaner no-show if:

Dispute category = no_show filed by client

OR Booking enters a designated no-show flow (if implemented using status=disputed)

no_show_rate =
  no_show_count / max(1, SCHEDULED) * 100
2.9 Dispute Rate
Includes all disputes except payment issues:

dispute_rate =
  disputed_jobs / max(1, COMPLETED) * 100
2.10 Streaks
A “successful day” = at least one completed job with:

No no-show

No cleaner cancellation

No dispute

On-time arrival

Track:

current_streak_days

best_streak_days

2.11 Totals
total_jobs = total completed + approved bookings
3. Reliability Score (Composite 0–100)
Normalize component metrics to 0–100:

attend_score = attendance_rate

punctuality_score = punctuality_rate

cancel_score = 100 - (cancellation_rate * penalty_factor)

no_show_score = 100 - (no_show_rate * penalty_factor)

dispute_score = 100 - (dispute_rate * penalty_factor)

photo_score = photo_proof_rate

comm_score = communication_rate

rating_score = (average_rating / 5) * 100

Weights (final corrected version):
Metric	Weight
Attendance	20%
Punctuality	15%
Cancellation	10%
No-show	20%
Dispute rate	10%
Photo proof	10%
Communication	10%
Rating	5%
Formula:
reliability_score =
  0.20 * attend_score +
  0.15 * punctuality_score +
  0.10 * cancel_score +
  0.20 * no_show_score +
  0.10 * dispute_score +
  0.10 * photo_score +
  0.10 * comm_score +
  0.05 * rating_score
Clamp to [0, 100].

4. Tier Assignment
Base44 tiers:

Developing

Semi Pro

Pro

Elite

Final tier thresholds:
Tier	Requirements
Developing	total_jobs < 10 OR reliability < 70
Semi Pro	total_jobs ≥ 10 & reliability ≥ 70
Pro	total_jobs ≥ 50 & reliability ≥ 80 & no_show < 2% & cancellation < 5%
Elite	total_jobs ≥ 100 & reliability ≥ 90 & no_show < 1% & cancellation < 3% & avg_rating ≥ 4.8
Cleaner receives the highest tier for which all requirements are met.

5. Tier Progress
Use known thresholds to compute progress toward next tier:

tier_progress = {
  current_jobs: total_jobs,
  current_score: reliability_score,
  jobs_to_next_tier: max(0, next_tier.required_jobs - total_jobs),
  score_to_next_tier: max(0, next_tier.required_score - reliability_score)
}
Appears in CleanerProfile as:

“You are 15 jobs and 4 reliability points away from Pro.”

6. Cleaner Milestones
We use Base44’s existing CleanerMilestone entity.

Triggered when thresholds are crossed:
✔ First 10 jobs
✔ First 50 jobs
✔ First 100 jobs
✔ First $1000 earned (earnings from Payout Engine)
✔ Perfect month (30-day streak)
✔ Reliability Elite (≥ 90 for 30 days)
✔ Zero-dispute month
✔ 100% photo compliance month

When conditions become true AND not previously earned:

Create CleanerMilestone {
  cleaner_email,
  milestone_type,
  reward_type,
  reward_value,
  earned_date: now()
}
Reward types could be:

Bonus payout %

Profile boosting

Instant book enablement

Discount on platform fees

7. Full Reliability Engine Automation Flow
7.1 Daily Batch Job (Primary source of truth)
For each cleaner:

Fetch all Bookings, Reviews, Disputes in last 90 days.

Compute all metrics.

Compute reliability_score.

Determine tier.

Compute tier_progress.

Write all fields into CleanerProfile.

7.2 Real-Time Update Hooks (Optional)
Triggered on:

New Review is submitted

Actions:

Optionally recalc lightweight reliability summary fields

Daily batch job remains the official finalizer.

🧩 MODULE 7 — DISPUTES & CLAIMS ENGINE (FINAL BLUEPRINT)
1. Scope
Module 7 owns everything that happens when something goes wrong with a job:

Client files a complaint or dispute

Cleaner files a dispute (unpaid time, unfair rating, etc.)

We track Dispute lifecycle (open → resolved)

We decide refunds to client

We decide adjustments to cleaner earnings / payouts

We update:

Booking status/flags

Credits ledger (Module 2)

CleanerEarning / Payout (Module 3)

Reliability metrics (Module 6)

Analytics / support tickets

We keep it entity-driven and avoid inventing new Booking statuses beyond what we already have.

2. Entities used
We’re only using things that already exist in your Base44 stack (or we described earlier):

Booking

id, client_email, cleaner_email

status (completed, approved, cancelled, disputed, etc.)

escrow_credits_reserved

final_charge_credits, refund_credits

date, start_time, hours

metadata: photos, notes, etc.

Dispute

id, booking_id

filed_by (client or cleaner)

filed_by_email

category (e.g. no_show, quality_issue, damage, billing_issue, safety_concern)

status (open, investigating, awaiting_client, awaiting_cleaner, resolved, closed)

client_requested_refund_usd

proposed_refund_usd

final_refund_usd

notes, evidence links (photo URLs, message refs)

resolved_outcome (client_favor, cleaner_favor, split, no_action)

created_at, resolved_at

ClientProfile

credits_balance

total disputes, flags, etc.

CreditTransaction

The credits ledger from Module 2:

client_email

transaction_type (purchase, refund, adjustment, etc.)

amount_credits (signed)

balance_after

booking_id, dispute_id (optional link)

CleanerEarning

cleaner_email

booking_id

credits_earned

payout_percentage

usd_due

status (pending, batched, paid, reversed)

payout_id (nullable)

Payout

cleaner_email

amount (USD)

status (pending, processing, completed, failed, cancelled)

Payment

booking_id

amount (USD)

status (pending, completed, refunded, partially_refunded, etc.)

stripe_payment_intent_id

refunded_amount (USD)

CleanerProfile / CleanerAnalytics

For reliability / dispute rate updates.

SupportTicket / AnalyticsEvent (if you want tracking & admin tooling)

3. Dispute Lifecycle
We’ll keep a simple lifecycle on the Dispute.status field:

open — dispute created, needs triage

investigating — support/admin is reviewing

awaiting_client — waiting for more info from client

awaiting_cleaner — waiting for response from cleaner

resolved — decision made (refunds / adjustments applied)

closed — fully done, no further action

And a separate resolved_outcome:

client_favor

cleaner_favor

split

no_action

Booking.status:

When a dispute is created, we do NOT invent a new status.

If Booking was approved or completed, we can set status = "disputed" as part of your existing enum.

Otherwise, for edge cases (before completion), we can keep the original status and use a has_open_dispute flag if needed.

4. Dispute creation: when & how
4.1 Client files a dispute
Trigger: client taps “Report a problem / Request refund” in app for a booking.

Conditions:

Booking.status ∈ {completed, awaiting_client, approved}

And within X days of job (e.g., 7 days).

Actions:

Create Dispute:

booking_id

filed_by = "client"

filed_by_email = Booking.client_email

category:

no_show

quality_issue

damage

billing_issue

safety_concern

status = "open"

client_requested_refund_usd (client can choose full or partial)

Attach any:

photos

notes

selected checklist items

Update Booking:

If currently approved or completed:

Booking.status = "disputed" (if that exists in your enum, which we’ve referenced before).

Optionally set Booking.has_open_dispute = true (custom flag).

Notify:

Cleaner (summary of complaint)

Support team (via SupportTicket or internal channel)

4.2 Cleaner files a dispute
Examples:

Client refused to approve but work was done

Job ran longer than booked time without pay

Rating is abusive or inaccurate

Client no-show but Booking marked as something else

Trigger: cleaner taps “Report issue” on job.

Actions:

Create Dispute:

filed_by = "cleaner"

filed_by_email = Booking.cleaner_email

category e.g. client_no_show, unfair_rating, unpaid_extra_time, safety_concern

status = "open"

client_requested_refund_usd = 0 (since this is cleaner complaint)

notes/evidence

Set Booking.status = "disputed" if job was already approved.

Notify support; optionally notify client.

5. Investigating disputes
Most of this is admin flow, but we define automation hooks.

5.1 Transition to investigating
Trigger: Dispute created (status = "open").

Actions:

Auto-set status = "investigating" once support picks it up or after initial triage.

Attach evidence:

Booking photos

Message history

Check-in/out times

Cleaner’s reliability history

Optionally create a SupportTicket that links to Dispute.

5.2 Request more info from client or cleaner
Admin action:

If more info needed from client:

Dispute.status = "awaiting_client"

Send message asking for photos/details.

If more info needed from cleaner:

Dispute.status = "awaiting_cleaner"

Ask them to respond, upload photos, explain.

After info arrives, set back to investigating.

6. Resolution: outcomes & financial logic
This is the heart of Module 7: how we convert decisions into:

client refunds (credits)

cleaner earnings adjustments

payout/chargeback behavior

reliability impact

6.1 Resolution types
Admin decides:

Outcome A: client_favor — client gets full refund

Outcome B: split — partial refund, shared fault

Outcome C: cleaner_favor — no refund, maybe rating removal

Outcome D: no_action — e.g., duplicate / invalid

Also we need:

final_refund_usd (0 → full price)

notes for audit trail

6.2 Base financial references
From previous modules:

Booking has:

final_charge_credits (what client was charged)

This equals:

final_charge_usd = final_charge_credits / CREDITS_PER_USD

Cleaner’s share:

CleanerEarning.usd_due

Payment.cleaner_payout (same value)

Credits / wallet / ledger:

Client refunds are applied via CreditTransaction and ClientProfile.credits_balance.

We do NOT re-touch escrow here — escrow was settled in Module 2 at approval. We only do post-settlement adjustments.

6.3 Outcome A — Client wins, full refund
When applied:

Eg: no-show by cleaner, very bad quality, confirmed damage.

Actions:

Let:

F = Booking.final_charge_credits

refund_credits = F (full refund)

refund_usd = F / 10

Refund to client wallet:

Create CreditTransaction:

client_email = Booking.client_email

booking_id = Booking.id

dispute_id = Dispute.id

transaction_type = "refund"

amount_credits = +refund_credits

balance_after = previous_balance + refund_credits

Update:

ClientProfile.credits_balance += refund_credits

Booking.refund_credits += refund_credits

Adjust Payment record:

Increase Payment.refunded_amount += refund_usd

Set Payment.status = "refunded" if full amount refunded; partially_refunded if not.

(Actual Stripe refund call happens in Module 2/Stripe handler; here we just set the intent values.)

Adjust cleaner earnings:

If corresponding CleanerEarning is:

pending or batched (not paid yet):

Set CleanerEarning.usd_due = 0

Set CleanerEarning.status = "reversed"

paid:

Create negative CleanerEarning (as defined in Module 3) to claw back on future payouts.

Update Dispute & Booking:

Dispute.status = "resolved"

Dispute.resolved_outcome = "client_favor"

Dispute.final_refund_usd = refund_usd

Optionally:

Booking.status stays approved (job “done” but refunded), or track has_refund = true.

Reliability impact:

If category = no_show or damage or repeated quality_issue:

Mark a strong negative event for Module 6 (increase dispute_count, maybe flagged for review).

This will flow into dispute_rate, no_show_rate, and ultimately reliability_score.

6.4 Outcome B — Split (partial refund)
Example:
Job partly done, some rooms missed; both sides share some responsibility.

Let:

F_usd = final_charge_credits / 10

refund_usd = chosen partial amount (e.g. 30% of F)

refund_credits = refund_usd * 10

Actions:

Refund to client:

CreditTransaction with amount_credits = +refund_credits

Increase ClientProfile.credits_balance accordingly

Booking.refund_credits += refund_credits

Adjust Payment:

Payment.refunded_amount += refund_usd

If partial < F_usd → Payment.status = "partially_refunded"

Adjust cleaner earnings:

If CleanerEarning not paid yet:

Reduce usd_due by cleaner_share_of_refund.

Typically:

Client refund comes out of:

Cleaner’s share FIRST up to a cap (e.g. max 50% of their payout)

Then platform margin if needed.

If already paid:

Create negative CleanerEarning with usd_due = -clawback_usd.

Dispute / Booking fields:

Dispute.status = "resolved"

resolved_outcome = "split"

final_refund_usd = refund_usd

Reliability:

Category-level impacts:

smaller penalty than full refund

still increments dispute count

6.5 Outcome C — Cleaner wins (no refund)
Examples:

Client complaint not supported by evidence.

Work clearly done to spec.

Actions:

Financial:

No changes to credits / Payment / CleanerEarning.

Dispute:

status = "resolved"

resolved_outcome = "cleaner_favor"

final_refund_usd = 0

Rating/Review:

Optionally:

Admin may remove or adjust unfair review rating.

Reliability:

This dispute should not count heavily against cleaner:

You can tag as “non-fault” and exclude from dispute_rate.

6.6 Outcome D — No action / cancelled dispute
Examples:

Duplicate dispute

Client mis-tapped

Issue resolved outside system

Actions:

Close Dispute with:

status = "closed"

resolved_outcome = "no_action"

No financial changes.

7. Automations for Module 7
7.1 Automation 7.1 — On Dispute.created
Trigger: Dispute row created.

Actions:

Set Dispute.status = "open".

Set Booking.status = "disputed" if job was approved/completed.

Notify support team:

Create SupportTicket / internal alert.

Notify cleaner or client (depending on filed_by).

7.2 Automation 7.2 — Admin sets resolution
Trigger: Admin updates Dispute with resolution decision:

resolved_outcome set

final_refund_usd set (could be 0)

Actions (branch by outcome):

If resolved_outcome = "client_favor":

Run Outcome A flow.

If resolved_outcome = "split":

Run Outcome B flow.

If resolved_outcome = "cleaner_favor":

Run Outcome C flow.

If resolved_outcome = "no_action":

Run Outcome D.

Then:

Set Dispute.status = "resolved"

Set Dispute.resolved_at = now()

Optionally after any appeal window:

Dispute.status = "closed"

7.3 Automation 7.3 — Stripe chargeback handling
If Stripe sends a chargeback / dispute (cardholder initiated):

Trigger: Stripe webhook for chargeback tied to Payment.stripe_payment_intent_id.

Actions:

Create a Dispute with category = "payment_issue" if it doesn’t exist.

Set admin-only fields noting chargeback details.

Apply financial logic similar to Outcome A:

Refund is forced by Stripe.

Then we must:

reduce cleaner earnings appropriately

possibly mark as “payment_issue” so it doesn’t count too harshly against cleaner reliability.

7.4 Automation 7.4 — Reliability adjustments hook
Whenever a Dispute is resolved:

Trigger: Dispute.status changed → resolved.

Actions:

Tag a “reliability event” for the cleaner:

no_show, damage, quality_issue, safety_concern, etc.

Increment internal counters used by Module 6:

disputed_jobs

no_show_bookings

At next Reliability batch run (Module 6):

New dispute data will adjust dispute_rate, no_show_rate, and reliability_score.

8. Interaction With Other Modules
Module 2 (Payments & Credits):

Module 7 calls the “refund via credits” behavior:

Adds CreditTransaction

Updates ClientProfile.credits_balance

Updates Booking.refund_credits

Updates Payment.refunded_amount and Payment.status.

Module 3 (Payout Engine):

Module 7 may:

Reduce CleanerEarning.usd_due for unpaid jobs

Create negative CleanerEarning for already paid jobs (future clawback).

Module 4 (Pricing Engine):

Uses Booking final charges / extras; Dispute doesn’t recalc price, it adjusts post-hoc.

Module 6 (Reliability Engine):

Disputes, no-shows, quality issues all feed reliability metrics and tier movement.

Module 5 (Smart Match):

Indirectly affected: repeated disputes lower reliability_score, no_show_rate, etc., which reduce SmartMatchScore.

9. Summary
Module 7 now:

Defines clear Dispute lifecycle (open → investigating/awaiting → resolved/closed).

Full refund

Cleaner wins

No action

🧩 MODULE 7 – DISPUTES & CLAIMS ENGINE (FINAL v2)
1. Scope
Module 7 controls everything when a job goes wrong:

Client or cleaner files a Dispute

Support/admin investigates, chooses outcome

System:

Refunds credits to client (and updates Stripe via Payments)

Updates Booking, CreditTransaction, Payment

Assume:

CREDITS_PER_USD = 10
2. Entities
2.1 Booking
Key fields we touch:

id

client_email

cleaner_email

status (includes completed, awaiting_client, approved, disputed, cancelled, etc.)

final_charge_credits

refund_credits

(From Modules 2–4) all the pricing/charge fields.

2.2 Dispute
Existing Dispute entity + a few explicitly new fields we’re defining for logic:

Existing-ish core fields (conceptual):

id

booking_id

filed_by (client | cleaner | system)

filed_by_email

category (no_show, quality_issue, damage, billing_issue, safety_concern, etc.)

status (open, investigating, awaiting_client, awaiting_cleaner, resolved, closed)

notes / admin_notes

evidence_urls[] (photos, links, etc.)

created_at, resolved_at

New fields we’re adding as part of this design:

requested_refund_credits – what client asked for (can be 0–final_charge_credits)

proposed_refund_credits – internal field support might use during investigation (optional)

final_refund_credits – what we actually decide to refund

resolved_outcome:

client_favor | cleaner_favor | split | no_action

(We can also calculate final_refund_usd = final_refund_credits / CREDITS_PER_USD if needed in Payments.)

2.3 ClientProfile
credits_balance

2.4 CreditTransaction
The credits ledger (from Module 2):

client_email

transaction_type (purchase, booking_hold, charge, refund, adjustment, etc.)

amount_credits (signed)

balance_after

booking_id (optional)

dispute_id (optional)

2.5 CleanerEarning
From Modules 2–3:

cleaner_email

booking_id

credits_earned

payout_percentage

usd_due

status:

"pending" | "batched" | "paid" | "reversed"

payout_id (nullable)

2.6 Payment
Stripe-facing record:

booking_id

total_amount_usd

refunded_amount_usd

status (pending, completed, partially_refunded, refunded)

stripe_payment_intent_id

2.7 Payout
From Module 3:

cleaner_email

amount (USD)

status (pending, processing, completed, failed, cancelled)

2.8 Reliability-related
CleanerProfile / CleanerAnalytics – Module 6 uses dispute_rate, no_show_rate etc. We only signal events; Module 6 recalculates.

3. Dispute Lifecycle
We define Dispute.status like this:

open – newly filed

investigating – support reviewing

awaiting_client – waiting for client reply/info

awaiting_cleaner – waiting for cleaner reply/info

resolved – decision made, money adjustments done

closed – archived / no further changes

resolved_outcome:

client_favor

cleaner_favor

split

no_action

Booking.status:

We use existing disputed status once a dispute is opened on a completed/approved job.

We do not invent any new Booking statuses.

4. Creating Disputes
4.1 Client-initiated
Trigger: client taps “Report a problem / Request refund” on a Booking.

Conditions:

Booking.status ∈ {completed, awaiting_client, approved}

Within X days (e.g. 7 days) of Booking.date

Actions:

Create Dispute:

booking_id

filed_by = "client"

filed_by_email = Booking.client_email

category (client chooses)

status = "open"

requested_refund_credits (based on what they ask for)

notes, evidence_urls

Update Booking:

Booking.status = "disputed" (if previously completed/approved)

Optionally Booking.has_open_dispute = true (new flag)

Notify:

Cleaner

Support/admin

4.2 Cleaner-initiated
Examples:

Client no-show but job “looks like” cleaner cancelled

Extra unpaid work

Abuse/hostility

Trigger: cleaner taps “Report issue” on Booking.

Actions:

Create Dispute:

filed_by = "cleaner"

filed_by_email = Booking.cleaner_email

category (e.g. client_no_show, unpaid_time, safety_concern)

status = "open"

requested_refund_credits = 0 (they’re not asking to refund client)

If job already approved:

Booking.status = "disputed"

Notify support/admin; optionally notify client.

5. Investigation Phase
Mostly support-driven, but we define state behavior.

5.1 Move open → investigating
Trigger: creation of Dispute or support claiming it.

Actions:

Dispute.status = "investigating"

Fetch related context:

Booking details

Photos

Check-in/out timestamps

Messages

Cleaner’s reliability history (from Module 6)

5.2 Ask for more info
Admin action:

Need more from client → Dispute.status = "awaiting_client"

Need more from cleaner → Dispute.status = "awaiting_cleaner"

When info arrives, move back to investigating.

6. Resolution Outcomes + Money Flows
We always decide in credits first:

final_refund_credits (0 → full Booking.final_charge_credits)

and optionally compute final_refund_usd = final_refund_credits / CREDITS_PER_USD for Payment/Stripe.

We also record:

resolved_outcome

Dispute.status = "resolved"

Then the automations handle:

Client credit balance

Payment/refunds

Cleaner earnings adjustments

6.1 Outcome A — Full refund (client_favor)
When: clear no-show, catastrophic quality, damage, safety failure.

Let:

F = Booking.final_charge_credits

refund_credits = F

refund_usd = refund_credits / CREDITS_PER_USD

Steps:

Client wallet:

Create CreditTransaction:

client_email

booking_id

dispute_id

transaction_type = "refund"

amount_credits = +refund_credits

Update:

ClientProfile.credits_balance += refund_credits

Booking.refund_credits += refund_credits

Payment (Stripe side):

Payment.refunded_amount_usd += refund_usd

If refunded_amount_usd == total_amount_usd → Payment.status = "refunded"

Else → Payment.status = "partially_refunded"

A Stripe refund is triggered by your Payments module (Module 2/Stripe integration), using this value.

Cleaner earnings:

Find CleanerEarning for this booking.

If CleanerEarning.status ∈ {"pending", "batched"}:

Set:

CleanerEarning.usd_due = 0

CleanerEarning.status = "reversed"

If CleanerEarning.status = "paid":

Compute clawback_usd = CleanerEarning.usd_due (or some capped percentage).

Create negative CleanerEarning row as in Module 3:

usd_due = -clawback_usd

credits_earned negative, consistent with our earnings formula.

status = "pending"

Dispute fields:

Dispute.final_refund_credits = refund_credits

Dispute.resolved_outcome = "client_favor"

Dispute.status = "resolved"

Reliability:

This event should be tagged as a high-impact negative for Module 6:

increment dispute counters

if category = "no_show" → increment no-show counters as well

6.2 Outcome B — Partial refund (split)
When: work partially done; shared fault.

Let:

F = Booking.final_charge_credits

refund_credits chosen by admin (e.g. 30% of F)

refund_usd = refund_credits / CREDITS_PER_USD

We also decide how much comes from cleaner vs platform margin:

cleaner_share_pct (e.g. 50% of refund)

platform_share_pct (e.g. 50%)

Steps:

Client wallet:

Same as full refund but with refund_credits less than F.

Payment:

Payment.refunded_amount_usd += refund_usd

Update status accordingly (likely partially_refunded).

Cleaner earnings:

Let:

cleaner_refund_usd = refund_usd * cleaner_share_pct

platform_refund_usd = refund_usd * platform_share_pct

If CleanerEarning not yet paid:

Reduce CleanerEarning.usd_due by cleaner_refund_usd (down to a minimum of 0).

If already paid:

Create negative CleanerEarning:

usd_due = -cleaner_refund_usd

status = "pending"

Platform’s share is simply a reduction in platform’s margin and doesn’t require CleanerEarning changes.

Dispute fields:

Dispute.final_refund_credits = refund_credits

resolved_outcome = "split"

Reliability:

Counts as a dispute event but typically a smaller negative weight than a full client-favor refund.

6.3 Outcome C — Cleaner wins (cleaner_favor)
When: complaint not supported by evidence; client being unfair.

Steps:

No changes to:

ClientProfile.credits_balance

Payment

CleanerEarning

Dispute fields:

final_refund_credits = 0

resolved_outcome = "cleaner_favor"

status = "resolved"

Optional:

Admin may:

Adjust/remove unfair review.

Add an internal note on client profile.

Reliability:

This dispute should not hurt cleaner’s reliability.

We can mark it as “no fault” so Module 6 ignores it for dispute_rate.

6.4 Outcome D — No action (no_action)
When: duplicate dispute, user error, cancelled complaint.

Steps:

No financial changes.

Dispute.resolved_outcome = "no_action"

Dispute.status = "closed" (or resolved then closed).

Reliability impact = 0.

7. Automations
7.1 Automation 7.1 — On Dispute.created
Trigger: new Dispute row.

Actions:

If status not set → status = "open".

If Booking is completed/approved:

Booking.status = "disputed" (keeping existing enum).

Notify support/admin (SupportTicket).

Notify other party (client or cleaner) that a dispute opened.

7.2 Automation 7.2 — On Dispute.status → resolved
Trigger: Admin sets resolved_outcome and final_refund_credits, then moves Dispute to status = "resolved".

Actions:

Branch by resolved_outcome:

client_favor → run Outcome A.

split → run Outcome B.

cleaner_favor → run Outcome C.

no_action → run Outcome D.

Set Dispute.resolved_at = now().

Optionally, after some time or once appeals are closed:

Dispute.status = "closed".

Mark Booking:

If we refunded fully:

Booking.has_refund = true (optional)

Status can remain approved/completed or disputed depending on how you want reporting; financially it is already adjusted.

Emit a “reliability event” so Module 6 can use it in next daily recompute.

7.3 Automation 7.3 — Stripe chargeback integration
Trigger: Stripe sends a chargeback/dispute webhook.

Actions:

Locate Payment by stripe_payment_intent_id.

If no Dispute exists:

Create one:

filed_by = "system"

category = "billing_issue"

requested_refund_credits = Payment.total_amount_usd * CREDITS_PER_USD

Treat this as forced client_favor:

Set final_refund_credits based on actual chargeback amount.

Run similar logic to Outcome A, but mark category = "payment_issue" so it doesn’t heavily penalize cleaner reliability unless evidence says otherwise.

7.4 Automation 7.4 — Reliability hooks
Trigger: any Dispute transitions to resolved.

Actions:

Record a reliability signal for the cleaner, including:

category

resolved_outcome

whether full/partial/no refund

Module 6’s nightly job will interpret:

no_show client_favor → heavy no_show+dispute penalty

quality_issue split → moderate penalty

cleaner_favor no_action → zero penalty

8. Integration Summary
Module 2 (Credits & Payments):

Module 7 creates CreditTransaction and sets final_refund_credits; Module 2/Stripe handles actual card refunds using final_refund_credits / 10.

Module 3 (Payout Engine):

Module 7 adjusts CleanerEarning or creates negative earnings for clawbacks.

Module 4 (Pricing):

Unchanged; disputes adjust after price and payment.

Module 5 (SmartMatch):

Indirectly impacted because disputes feed Module 6 metrics.

Module 6 (Reliability):

Uses Dispute stats (frequency, categories, outcomes) to adjust reliability_score, tier, and streaks.

If you want next, we can either:

Move on to Module 8 – Notifications & Messaging Engine, or

Start turning these modules into concrete implementations (e.g., n8n flows, Neon SQL schemas, Base44 automations for one module at a time).

✅ MODULE 7 — DISPUTES & CLAIMS ENGINE (FINAL, CLEAN, CORRECTED VERSION)
1. Purpose & Role in the System
Module 7 manages everything when a job doesn’t go as expected:

Clients or cleaners file disputes

Admin/support investigates

System issues refunds to client wallet (credits)

System adjusts cleaner earnings & payouts

System updates Payment, CleaningEarning, CreditTransactions, Booking

System signals reliability events to Module 6

Stripe chargebacks are handled safely

This module does not touch pricing or booking lifecycle logic — those are in Modules 1–4.
This module handles post-job financial correction.

2. Entities Used (All real Base44 entities)
2.1 Booking
Fields used:

id

client_email

cleaner_email

status (Existing enum: created, scheduled, in_progress, completed, awaiting_client, approved, cancelled, disputed)

final_charge_credits

refund_credits

date, start_time, hours metadata

Photos, notes, review_submitted (if included)

2.2 Dispute
We use the existing entity and define a few new fields explicitly.

Existing-like fields:

id

booking_id

filed_by (client | cleaner | system)

filed_by_email

category (no_show, quality_issue, billing_issue, damage, safety_concern, etc.)

status (open, investigating, awaiting_client, awaiting_cleaner, resolved, closed)

notes, evidence_urls[]

created_at, resolved_at

NEW fields used by Module 7 (final, stable set):

requested_refund_credits

proposed_refund_credits (optional for admin)

final_refund_credits

resolved_outcome
(client_favor | split | cleaner_favor | no_action)

2.3 ClientProfile
credits_balance

2.4 CreditTransaction
Used to apply refunds/adjustments:

client_email

amount_credits

transaction_type (refund, adjustment, purchase, etc.)

balance_after

booking_id

2.5 CleanerEarning
From Modules 2–3:

cleaner_email

booking_id

credits_earned

usd_due

status (pending, batched, paid, reversed)

2.6 Payment
Stripe-facing:

booking_id

total_amount_usd

refunded_amount_usd

stripe_payment_intent_id

status (pending, completed, partially_refunded, refunded)

2.7 Payout
cleaner_email

amount

status (pending, processing, completed, etc.)

2.8 Reliability Entities
CleanerProfile (Module 6 uses dispute/no-show data)

CleanerAnalytics

3. Dispute Lifecycle (Final Approved Flow)
We use this exact lifecycle:

open — created

investigating — support reviewing

awaiting_client — need more info

awaiting_cleaner — need more info

resolved — decision executed (refunds + adjustments)

closed — archived

Booking.status:

If the job was completed/approved, we set:

Booking.status = "disputed"

We do not invent any new statuses.

4. Dispute Creation
4.1 Client Files a Dispute
Trigger: Client taps “Report a problem” on a completed job.

Conditions:

Booking.status ∈ {completed, awaiting_client, approved}

Optional: within X days of service (7 days recommended)

Actions:

Create Dispute with:

filed_by = "client"

filed_by_email = Booking.client_email

requested_refund_credits

category

status = "open"

Set:

Booking.status = "disputed"

Notify cleaner + support.

4.2 Cleaner Files a Dispute
Trigger: Cleaner taps “Report issue”.

Examples:

Client no-show misrepresented

Unpaid extra time

Unsafe environment

Aggressive client behavior

Actions:

Create Dispute:

filed_by = "cleaner"

filed_by_email = Booking.cleaner_email

category

requested_refund_credits = 0 (since they don’t request client refund)

status = "open"

If job was approved:

Booking.status = "disputed"

Notify support; optionally notify client.

5. Investigation Phase
The system must support back-and-forth information gathering.

5.1 Move to Investigating
Trigger: Dispute created OR support agent picks it up.

Action:

Dispute.status = "investigating"

Support loads:

Booking context

Photos

Check-in/out times

Cleaner’s reliability profile

Messages

Previous disputes

5.2 Need more info
If more info needed from client:

Dispute.status = "awaiting_client"

If more info needed from cleaner:

Dispute.status = "awaiting_cleaner"

When info arrives, set:

Dispute.status = "investigating"

6. Resolution + Financial Logic (Credits-First)
All outcomes use:

final_refund_credits (0 → Booking.final_charge_credits)
final_refund_usd = final_refund_credits / CREDITS_PER_USD
We use CleanerEarning, CreditTransaction, and Payment to enforce the decision.

6.1 Outcome A — Client Wins (Full Refund)
(Category typically: no_show, safety_issue, severe_quality_issue)

Let:

F = Booking.final_charge_credits

refund_credits = F

refund_usd = F / CREDITS_PER_USD

Steps
1. Refund to client wallet
Create CreditTransaction:
  transaction_type = "refund"
  amount_credits = +refund_credits
  booking_id = Booking.id
  dispute_id = Dispute.id
Update:

ClientProfile.credits_balance += refund_credits

Booking.refund_credits += refund_credits

2. Stripe Payment adjustment
Payment.refunded_amount_usd += refund_usd

If full refund:

Payment.status = "refunded"

Else:

Payment.status = "partially_refunded"

Stripe refund is executed by Module 2 using refund_usd.

3. Cleaner Earnings Adjustment
Case A: CleanerEarning.status ∈ {pending, batched}

CleanerEarning.usd_due = 0

CleanerEarning.status = "reversed"

Case B: CleanerEarning.status = "paid"

Compute clawback:

clawback_usd = CleanerEarning.usd_due
Create negative CleanerEarning:

CleanerEarning {
  cleaner_email,
  booking_id,
  usd_due = -clawback_usd,
  credits_earned = -(clawback_usd * CREDITS_PER_USD),
  status = "pending"
}
4. Mark Dispute Resolved
Dispute.final_refund_credits = refund_credits

Dispute.resolved_outcome = "client_favor"

Dispute.status = "resolved"

Dispute.resolved_at = now()

5. Reliability impact
Strong negative event for Module 6:

increment no-show count if applicable

increment dispute count

reduce reliability in next nightly batch

6.2 Outcome B — Split Refund (Partial Refund)
Shared fault or partial work done.

Let:

refund_credits = admin_defined
refund_usd = refund_credits / CREDITS_PER_USD
cleaner_share_pct = 0.5   (example)
platform_share_pct = 0.5
Steps
1. Refund client credits
Same as full refund, but with partial credits.

2. Stripe Payment adjustment
Payment.refunded_amount_usd += refund_usd

Payment.status = "partially_refunded"

3. Cleaner Earnings Adjustment
Calculate:

cleaner_refund_usd = refund_usd * cleaner_share_pct
platform_refund_usd = refund_usd * platform_share_pct
If not paid yet:

Reduce CleanerEarning.usd_due by cleaner_refund_usd.

If paid:

Create negative CleanerEarning:

usd_due = -cleaner_refund_usd
status = "pending"
Platform portion affects only internal margin.

4. Mark Dispute Resolved
resolved_outcome = "split"

final_refund_credits = refund_credits

status = "resolved"

5. Reliability impact
Mild penalty
(affects dispute_rate but not as severely as full no-show refund).

6.3 Outcome C — Cleaner Wins
Complaint not supported by evidence.

Actions:
No credit refund.

No Payment change.

No CleanerEarning change.

Dispute.resolved_outcome = "cleaner_favor"

final_refund_credits = 0

Dispute.status = "resolved"

Reliability: does not count against cleaner.

Optional: admin may remove unfair review.

6.4 Outcome D — No Action
Duplicate or invalid dispute.

Actions:
No financial impact

Dispute.resolved_outcome = "no_action"

Dispute.status = "closed"

Reliability: zero impact.

7. Automations (Final Version)
7.1 Automation — When Dispute is Created
Trigger: Dispute.created

Actions:

If status blank → set status = "open"

If Booking was completed or approved → Booking.status = "disputed"

Notify support

Notify cleaner or client (depending on who filed)

7.2 Automation — When Dispute is Resolved
Trigger: Admin sets:

resolved_outcome

final_refund_credits

Then changes Dispute.status → resolved

Actions:

If client_favor → run Outcome A

If split → run Outcome B

If cleaner_favor → run Outcome C

If no_action → Outcome D

Then:

Dispute.resolved_at = now()

Create reliability event → Module 6

Optionally auto-close dispute after X hours

7.3 Automation — Stripe Chargeback
Trigger: Stripe webhook → cardholder dispute

Actions:

Locate Payment & Booking

If no Dispute exists:

Create:

filed_by = "system"

category = "billing_issue"

requested_refund_credits = total_charge_credits

Treat this as mandatory client_favor refund:

Set refund fields

Run Outcome A logic (full refund)

Mark category = billing_issue (so reliability isn’t penalized)

7.4 Automation — Reliability Event Hook
Trigger: Any Dispute → status = "resolved"

Actions:

Create a reliability event for Module 6:

category

amount of refund

outcome

No reliability calculation here — it's done nightly in Module 6.

✅ MODULE 8 — MESSAGING & NOTIFICATION ENGINE (FINAL BLUEPRINT)
1. Purpose
Module 8 is the centralized delivery engine for all communication including:

SMS (Twilio)

Email (SendGrid)

Push notifications (OneSignal)

In-app messaging (Base44 ConversationThread / Message entities)

Admin/internal alerts

It defines:

WHEN messages are sent

WHO they go to

WHAT channel(s) they use

HOW they failover (SMS → email → push)

EXACT TEMPLATES and merge variables

EVENT TRIGGERS from Modules 1–7

DELIVERY RULES (timing, rate limits, quiet hours, etc.)

This module does not define front-end UI — only backend logic + templates + triggers.

2. Entities Used
(Existing in your system or already defined earlier)

Booking

Payment

3. NEW Entity Definitions for Module 8
3.1 NotificationTemplate (NEW)
Stores reusable templates.

NotificationTemplate {
  id,
  code,                     // e.g. "booking_created_client", "cleaner_on_the_way"
  channels[],               // ["sms", "email", "push"]
  title_template,           // email/push title
  body_template,            // message body (with merge fields)
  variables[],              // allowed merge vars
  is_active
}
3.2 NotificationsLog (NEW)
Tracks all sends.

NotificationsLog {
  id,
  user_email,
  booking_id,
  dispute_id,
  template_code, 
  channels_used[],          // e.g. ["sms", "push"]
  delivery_status,          // success | failed | retrying
  error_message,
  sent_at,
  retries
}
Used for:

Support monitoring

Rate limiting

Retry logic

Avoid duplicate sends

4. Channel Strategy (Critical)
Primary rules:
Cleaner = SMS first, then push, then email
Why? Cleaners respond fastest to SMS.

Client = Push first, then email, then SMS (only urgent)
Why? Clients don’t want too many texts.

Admin = Email + Slack/Webhook
For disputes, payments, payouts.

Try push → if fails
Try email → if fails
Try SMS → if fails

Retry schedule:

5 minutes

30 minutes

6 hours

Up to 3 retries.

✅ MODULE 8 — MESSAGING & NOTIFICATION ENGINE (FINAL v2)
This version:

Uses only real booking statuses we’ve been using elsewhere

Clearly marks new entities/fields

Ties directly into Modules 1–7

Is structured so you can literally build it in Base44 / n8n / Neon

1. Purpose
Module 8 is the central brain for all communications in PureTask:

SMS (Twilio)

Email (SendGrid)

Push (OneSignal)

In-app (ConversationThread / Message)

Internal/admin alerts

It decides:

When to send a message (event triggers)

Who to send it to (client, cleaner, admin)

Which channels to use first (priority & failover)

What content to send (templates with variables)

How to track & retry (logging + retry rules)

Everything is event-driven and plugs into Modules 1–7.

2.2 NEW entities for Module 8
2.2.1 NotificationTemplate (NEW)
Stores reusable templates for SMS, Email, Push, In-app.

NotificationTemplate {
  id: string,
  code: string,           // e.g. "booking_created_client"
  channels: string[],     // ["sms", "email", "push"]
  title_template: string, // email/push title
  body_template: string,  // message body with placeholders like {{client_name}}
  variables: string[],    // ["client_name", "booking_date", ...]
  is_active: boolean
}
2.2.2 NotificationsLog (NEW)
Tracks which notifications were sent, through which channels, and whether they succeeded.

NotificationsLog {
  id: string,
  user_email: string,
  booking_id?: string,
  dispute_id?: string,
  template_code: string,
  channels_used: string[],          // e.g. ["sms", "push"]
  delivery_status: string,          // "success" | "failed" | "retrying"
  error_message?: string,
  sent_at: datetime,
  retries: number
}
You can also add:

channel_results JSON if you want per-channel status.

2.3 NEW helper concept: Notification Preferences (optional)
Optional new entity/fields to let users control channels.

NotificationPreference {
  user_email: string,
  allow_sms: boolean,
  allow_email: boolean,
  allow_push: boolean,
  quiet_hours_start?: string, // "22:00"
  quiet_hours_end?: string,   // "07:00"
}
Can also live as a JSON field on ClientProfile / CleanerProfile instead of separate entity.

3. Channel Strategy
3.1 Channel priority
For cleaners (time-sensitive ops):

SMS (Twilio) – primary

Push (OneSignal)

Email (SendGrid)

For clients:

Push (if app installed & opted-in)

Email

SMS only for urgent events:

cleaner cancellations

last-minute time changes

“cleaner on the way”

For admins/support:

Email

Slack/Webhook (via n8n / internal integration)

3.2 Failover and retry
When sending:

Try primary channel allowed by user preferences.

If failure (API error, bounce, etc.):

Try next channel in priority list.

If all channels fail:

Set delivery_status = "failed" in NotificationsLog.

Optionally schedule retries at:

+5 mins

+30 mins

+6 hours

Respect quiet hours for non-urgent messages (e.g., don’t push marketing at 2 AM).

Urgent system alerts (e.g., cleaner on the way, last-minute cancellations) can bypass quiet hours.

4. Event Triggers (Connected to Modules 1–7)
I’ll organize them by module.

4.1 Booking Lifecycle Events (Module 1)
We use the Booking.status state machine you already have.

4.1.1 Booking created (status = created)
To Client (booking_created_client):

Trigger: Booking created from DraftBooking + payment_hold done.

Channels: Push + Email.

Content:

“We’ve received your booking request”

Date, time, address

Estimated price

“We’re matching you with a cleaner”

4.1.2 Cleaner job offer (status = awaiting_cleaner_response)
To Primary Cleaner (job_offer_cleaner):

Trigger: Booking enters awaiting_cleaner_response with cleaner_email set.

Channels: SMS + Push.

Content:

Date/time, area, hours

Pay estimate (credits/$$)

Accept/Decline link

If fallback cleaners exist:

Optionally send “you’re next in line” info to backups, or wait until they’re active.

4.1.3 Cleaner accepts (status = accepted → scheduled)
To Client (booking_accepted_client):

Channels: Push + Email

Content:

Cleaner name, photo, tier

Date/time confirmation

House rules / prep tips

To Cleaner (booking_accepted_cleaner):

Channels: SMS + Push

Content:

Job summary

Address link

Checklist link

Reminder about photos & reliability

4.1.4 Cleaner declines (cleaner_declined) or times out
To Client (booking_still_matching_client):

Trigger: primary cleaner declines OR request_expires_at passes.

Channels: Push or Email (SMS only if job is soon).

Content:

“We’re finding you another cleaner”

Optional: discount if struggling to match.

To Next Fallback Cleaner (job_offer_cleaner again):

As in 4.1.2.

4.1.5 Scheduled reminder (status = scheduled)
To Client (booking_reminder_client):

When: e.g. 24h + 2h before job.

Content:

Date/time

Cleaner name

Prep reminder

To Cleaner (booking_reminder_cleaner):

When: e.g. 24h + morning-of.

Content:

Job time & address

“Don’t forget to check in & upload photos”

Channels: Push + SMS (time-sensitive).

“{{cleaner_name}} is on the way, ETA ~{{eta}}”

4.1.7 Cleaner in progress (status = in_progress)
To Client (job_started_client):

Channels: Push.

Content:

Work has started

Link to chat

4.1.8 Cleaner completed (status = completed)
To Client (job_completed_client):

Trigger: Booking moves to completed by cleaner check-out.

Channels: Push + Email.

Content:

“Work completed”

Link to review

Remind about approval window

To Cleaner (job_completed_cleaner):

“Thanks! Waiting for client approval”

4.1.9 Client approves (status = approved)
This triggers final charge & earnings (Modules 2 & 3).

To Client (job_approved_client):

Receipt

Total credits spent + remaining balance

Link to refer a friend

To Cleaner (job_approved_cleaner):

Confirmed earnings in credits + estimated payout date

Reliability positive reinforcement

4.1.10 Approval reminder / auto-approval
If client hasn’t approved after X hours:

Reminder (approval_reminder_client):

“Please review & approve or report issues”

Auto-approval (auto_approval_notice_client / auto_approval_notice_cleaner):

Sent when system auto-approves.

4.1.11 Client cancels (status = cancelled, cancelled_by = client)

Channels: SMS + Push.

Content:

Cancellation details

Whether cancellation fee applies

To Client (booking_cancelled_client):

Confirmation

Refund / credit messaging

Apology

Auto-rematch info

Possibly bonus credits

Confirmation

Reliability impact warning if last-minute

6. Notification Engine Flow
This is the core logic every time we send something:

Event happens
(Booking status change, Dispute created/resolved, Payment updated, etc.)

Map event → template_code + target user(s)
Example:

Booking.status changed scheduled → use booking_reminder_client and booking_reminder_cleaner.

Load NotificationTemplate by code.

Load user preferences (if implemented) and choose allowed channels.

Order channels by priority (cleaner vs client rules).

Render body + title by substituting merge variables.

Send via channel adapters:

SMS adapter → Twilio

Email adapter → SendGrid

Push adapter → OneSignal

In-app adapter → create Message

Log in NotificationsLog:

template_code

channels_used

success/failure

retries

Retry on failure with backoff, respecting quiet hours.

Internal alerts:

Chargebacks

Repeated no-shows by same cleaner

Dispute volume spike

Payout batch anomalies

System errors (e.g., Twilio/SendGrid outage)

Use:

Email → ops@puretask.com

Slack/Webhook → #ops-alerts channel

Templates like:

alert_chargeback_admin

alert_high_dispute_rate_cleaner

alert_system_error_notification_channel

To make this module extra strong, the design already assumes:

Centralized routing – Instead of scattering Twilio/SendGrid logic across flows, everything goes through the Notification Engine.

Templating – All copy lives in NotificationTemplate rows, so tweaks don’t require code changes.

A/B Testing Ready – Template rows with variant or experiment fields can be added later.

Localization Ready – Add language and translated templates, pick based on user preference.

Rate limiting – You can extend NotificationsLog to enforce “max X messages per Y time per user”.

Nice, this is a fun one. Module 9 is where PureTask starts feeling like magic for repeat customers.
