✅ MODULE 9 — RECURRING JOBS & SUBSCRIPTION ENGINE (DRAFT v1)
1. Purpose
Module 9 covers two related layers:

Recurring Jobs (RecurringBooking)

Auto-generate future Booking rows on a schedule (weekly/biweekly/monthly).

Respect pause, resume, and “next booking date”.

Plug into existing pricing, credits, payouts, matching, notifications.

Subscriptions & Memberships (CleaningSubscription + ClientMembership)

CleaningSubscription = recurring plan for one home + cleaner with a fixed monthly price and discount.

ClientMembership = membership tier (Plus/Platinum) with perks like discounts, free cancellations, priority, etc.

We’ll keep these logically separate so you can:

Launch RecurringBooking (pay-per-job) first.

Layer on CleaningSubscription + ClientMembership later without breaking anything.

2. Entities Used
2.1 RecurringBooking (Base44)
Already defined in Base44:

Key fields:

client_email

cleaner_email

frequency (weekly, biweekly, monthly)

day_of_week

start_time

hours

tasks[], task_quantities

address, latitude, longitude

total_price (per-visit price)

is_active (boolean, default true)

next_booking_date (date)

pause_until (date, optional)

Required: client_email, cleaner_email, frequency, day_of_week, start_time, hours, address, total_price.

2.2 CleaningSubscription (Base44)
Defined as:

client_email

cleaner_email

frequency (weekly, biweekly, monthly)

day_of_week

preferred_time

hours

tasks[], task_quantities

address, latitude, longitude

monthly_price (fixed monthly subscription price)

discount_percentage (vs pay-per-booking)

status (active, paused, cancelled)

paused_until (date)

next_booking_date (date)

started_date (datetime)

total_cleanings_completed

stripe_subscription_id (Stripe recurring billing)

2.3 ClientMembership (Base44)
Membership product:

client_email

tier (Plus, Platinum)

monthly_fee

benefits:

discount_percentage

priority_booking

free_cancellations

insurance_included

dedicated_support

status (active, cancelled, past_due)

started_date

next_billing_date

total_savings

stripe_subscription_id

2.4 Booking (Base44)
Important fields for recurring/subscription:

client_email, cleaner_email

subscription_id (string, “If part of a subscription”)

date, start_time, hours

cleaning_type, additional_services

total_price

Credits + escrow fields (from earlier modules):

escrow_credits_reserved

final_charge_credits

refund_credits

Status lifecycle we already use (scheduled, completed, approved, cancelled, etc.)

We’ll add one suggested new field:

NEW recurring_booking_id (string, optional)

Link each generated Booking back to its RecurringBooking source.

2.5 Payments / Credits / Payouts
From previous modules (no schema change here):

Payment – handles money with Stripe.

Credit / ClientProfile.credits_balance – credit ledger + balance.

CleanerEarning, Payout — used in payouts.

3. RecurringBooking Engine (Pay-per-Job Recurring)
This is the core recurring system. CleaningSubscription and memberships plug into it, not replace it.

3.1 Creation Flows
Three main ways a RecurringBooking can be created:

During checkout

Client selects: frequency (weekly, biweekly, monthly).

We create:

a one-time Booking (for first date) and

a RecurringBooking row using the same config (address, hours, tasks).

From an existing Booking (“Make this recurring”)

Client taps “Repeat every 2 weeks”.

We create RecurringBooking:

Copy Booking config (hours, tasks, address).

frequency = biweekly

day_of_week = Booking.date’s day

start_time = Booking.start_time

next_booking_date = Booking.date + frequency interval

total_price = Booking.total_price (or recomputed based on cleaner snapshot price).

From CleaningSubscription (advanced)

When a subscription is created (Section 4), we optionally also create a RecurringBooking for operational scheduling.

recurring_booking_id can be stored in CleaningSubscription or Booking.subscription_id.

3.2 Scheduler Job (Daily)
A daily (or hourly) background job does:

Find due RecurringBookings

Where:

is_active = true

next_booking_date <= today + X days (e.g., generate 7 days ahead)

pause_until is null OR pause_until < today

Generate Booking for each due record

For each RecurringBooking RB:

Create Booking:

client_email = RB.client_email

cleaner_email = RB.cleaner_email

date = RB.next_booking_date

start_time = RB.start_time

hours = RB.hours

address, latitude, longitude = RB.address etc.

tasks, task_quantities from RB

total_price = RB.total_price (snapshot; pricing engine may also snapshot from CleanerProfile)

subscription_id = null (unless tied to CleaningSubscription)

NEW recurring_booking_id = RB.id

status = "scheduled" (or awaiting_cleaner_response if you want re-confirmation)

Trigger:

Credits escrow & Payment hold (Modules 1–2).

Notifications (Module 8) for reminder messages to client+cleaner.

Advance next_booking_date

After generating a Booking, update RB.next_booking_date:

If frequency = weekly: +7 days

biweekly: +14 days

monthly: +1 month (careful with month boundaries; Base44 or your scheduler can implement standard rules).

Edge: Cleaner inactive / blocked

If cleaner is not active or blocked for this client:

Options:

A) Mark RecurringBooking as is_active = false.

B) Keep RecurringBooking but set cleaner_email = null and let SmartMatch find a new cleaner.

Module 5 (SmartMatch) can be used to fill in a cleaner before job goes live.

3.3 Pause, Resume, Cancel
Pause:

User or support sets:

is_active = false OR

pause_until = some date while staying active.

Logic:

Scheduler skips RecurringBookings where:

is_active = false
OR

pause_until >= today

Resume:

Clear pause_until and/or set is_active = true.

Set next_booking_date to the next appropriate date.

Cancel series:

Set:

is_active = false

pause_until = null

Does not cancel already-created future Bookings; those must be cancelled individually or via a batch admin tool.

3.4 Customer-facing UX implications
“Every 2 weeks” is just RecurringBooking frequency = biweekly.

“Skip next visit”:

You can either:

Move next_booking_date forward by one interval, or

Cancel the specific future Booking that was created for that date.

4. CleaningSubscription Engine (Fixed Monthly + Discount)
Now we add the subscription layer on top.

CleaningSubscription is already structured to be a plan for a single home and cleaner, with: schedule, price, discount, and Stripe subscription ID.

4.1 Business Model (recommendation)
To keep things simple & powerful:

CleaningSubscription:

Charges monthly_price every month via Stripe subscription.

Grants:

A recurring schedule (via RecurringBooking logic).

discount_percentage off each included Booking (or all Bookings tied to this subscription).

Actual Booking flows (credits, escrow, payouts) stay the same as Modules 1–3; we just apply a discount and treat some money as “membership fee”.

4.2 Subscription Creation Flow
When a client chooses a subscription plan:

Collect:

Frequency (weekly/biweekly/monthly)

Day of week, preferred_time, hours

Tasks, address, etc.

Create Stripe Subscription:

Product = “PureTask {{frequency}} plan”

Price = monthly_price

Create CleaningSubscription row:

Fill all schedule + config fields.

monthly_price

discount_percentage

status = "active"

started_date = now()

next_booking_date = first cleaning date

total_cleanings_completed = 0

stripe_subscription_id = from Stripe

Optionally create a linked RecurringBooking:

Same config as CleaningSubscription.

is_active = true

next_booking_date = same as subscription.

Store:

Booking.subscription_id for jobs created under this plan.

Or add NEW field recurring_booking_id on CleaningSubscription.

Notify:

Client & Cleaner via Module 8 (“subscription started” + schedule).

4.3 Applying Discounts to Bookings
When a Booking is created from a CleaningSubscription or has subscription_id set:

Determine base total using pricing engine (Module 4).

Apply:

Subscription discount (CleaningSubscription.discount_percentage), and/or

Membership-based discount (ClientMembership.benefits.discount_percentage).

You can decide stacking rules:

MVP: Take the max of (Subscription discount, Membership discount).

Advanced: Allow stacking up to a cap (e.g., max 30%).

Booking.total_price and the credits charged reflect the discounted price.

4.4 Monthly Billing + Webhooks
When Stripe sends invoice.payment_succeeded for stripe_subscription_id:

Find the CleaningSubscription row.

Confirm:

status is still active.

Optionally log:

A Payment or AnalyticsEvent to track subscription revenue.

If Stripe reports invoice.payment_failed:

Set CleaningSubscription.status = "paused" or cancelled based on dunning strategy.

You can also set ClientMembership.status = "past_due" for membership products.

Cancel/pause future Booking generation for this subscription (by deactivating linked RecurringBooking).

4.5 Pause / Resume / Cancel Subscription
Use existing fields: status, paused_until, next_booking_date.

Pause:

status = "paused"

paused_until = date

Link to Stripe pause or keep billing but skip jobs, depending on your strategy.

Resume:

status = "active"

Clear paused_until

Adjust next_booking_date accordingly.

Cancel:

status = "cancelled"

Cancel Stripe subscription.

Deactivate related RecurringBooking (is_active = false).

5. ClientMembership Engine (Perks Layer)
ClientMembership is like a global membership that can apply across:

one-time bookings

RecurringBooking series

CleaningSubscriptions

Schema recap: membership tier w/ monthly fee, benefits, billing and Stripe subscription ID.

5.1 Recommended behavior
When ClientMembership is active:

Booking pricing step:

Add membership’s benefits.discount_percentage as one of the discounts.

Cancellation logic (Module 1):

Respect benefits.free_cancellations and ClientProfile.grace_cancellations_left.

SmartMatch (Module 5):

If benefits.priority_booking = true, bump member clients in the queue.

Billing:

Similar to CleaningSubscription:

Stripe subscription charges monthly_fee.

next_billing_date updated.

total_savings increases each time a member gets discounted.

6. Automations Overview
6.1 Daily Recurring Scheduler (Core)
Trigger: cron every night (or hourly).

Steps:

Fetch all RecurringBooking with:

is_active = true

next_booking_date within horizon

pause_until < today or null.

For each:

Generate Booking.

Link via recurring_booking_id and optionally subscription_id.

Run through standard Modules:

Pricing (Module 4)

Credits & escrow (Module 2)

Matching (Module 5, if we allow rematching)

Notifications (Module 8)

Advance next_booking_date.

6.2 Stripe Subscription Webhooks
Set up two handlers:

CleaningSubscription webhooks:

On invoice.payment_succeeded:

If subscription was paused due to payment, set status = "active".

On invoice.payment_failed or customer.subscription.deleted:

status = "past_due" or cancelled.

Deactivate linked RecurringBooking.

ClientMembership webhooks:

Similar – update status + next_billing_date + track total_savings.

6.3 Notifications (ties back to Module 8)
Key triggers:

Subscription started → subscription_started_client, subscription_started_cleaner

Subscription paused/resumed → subscription_status_change_client

Membership started/cancelled → membership_status_client

Upcoming recurring job reminder (from RecurringBooking) → reuse booking_reminder_client / booking_reminder_cleaner

Recurring & subscription jobs are just Bookings with extra metadata (recurring_booking_id, subscription_id).

Module 2 — Credits & Payments

Per-job escrow & charge logic stays the same.

Subscription/membership charges are separate Stripe subscriptions (not per-job payments).

Module 3 — Payouts

Cleaner gets paid per job as usual; recurring/subscription only affect how client is charged/discounted.

❌ ERRORS / PROBLEMS / INCONSISTENCIES FOUND
1. Missing or ambiguous linkage between RecurringBooking ↔ CleaningSubscription
In Module 9, you treat RecurringBooking and CleaningSubscription as separate.
However:

If a customer subscribes, we must guarantee future jobs.

CleaningSubscription already contains next_booking_date, tasks, hours, etc.

⚠️ Problem:
You’re duplicating scheduling logic in both entities.

⚠️ Impact:
This can create double bookings, inconsistent schedules, or missed recurring jobs.

✔ Recommended fix
Make RecurringBooking the operational scheduler for both subscription & non-subscription recurring jobs.

CleaningSubscription is billing + configuration, while RecurringBooking is actual schedule engine.

2. Missing logic for handling cleaner unavailability
Current module says:

“If cleaner inactive → deactivate recurring booking or rematch.”

⚠️ Missing critical operational logic:

Cleaner on vacation

Cleaner pauses account

Cleaner removes service area

Cleaner rejects a recurring instance normally

Recurring bookings must survive cleaner issues.

✔ Recommended fix
Add fallback matching logic for recurring jobs, using Module 5:

Try the assigned cleaner first

If cleaner unavailable → SmartMatch fallback

Inform client if a temporary cleaner will be assigned

Allow client to decline fallback (optional)

3. No reliability rules for recurring performance
Recurring clients suffer most from bad cleaners.

⚠️ Mistake: Module 9 does not mention how recurring jobs feed reliability.

Should include:

Recurring cancellations by cleaner = severe penalty

No-shows on recurring bookings = double weight

Recurring completion streak = increases reliability

Recurring client disputes = heavier impact

4. Missing discount precedence logic
You listed:

Subscription discount

Membership discount

Potential recurring loyalty discount

But you didn’t define:

Stacking rules

Cap rules

Precedence (which applies first)

⚠️ Dangerous because it affects revenue.

✔ Recommended fix
Define:

Priority: Subscription > Membership > Loyalty

Max discount cap: 30% total (configurable)

5. Missing job quota logic for subscriptions
Subscriptions usually include:

X jobs per month OR

Unlimited jobs (rare) OR

“Fixed number of scheduled visits”

⚠️ Your subscription model charges a flat monthly price, but does not define:

How many jobs the customer gets per month

How to handle skipped jobs

How to handle extra jobs beyond plan

This will break reconciliation between subscription billing and per-job payouts.

✔ Recommended fix (strongly recommended)
Add to CleaningSubscription:

monthly_included_visits: integer  // e.g. 2 per month
extra_visit_price_credits: number // optional
Or require that subscription always aligns with frequency:

weekly plan = ~4 visits/month

biweekly = ~2 per month

monthly = 1 visit per month

6. No logic for late cancellations within subscriptions
Current Module 9 does not define if:

Subscribers get free cancellations

Recurring bookings follow general cancellation fee policy

Membership overrides subscription rules

Cleaner compensation applies differently

✔ Recommended fix
Define:

Subscription includes X free cancellations per month

Additional cancellations follow normal fee logic

Membership benefits always override subscription rules

7. Missing ability for client to “skip single visit”
You mentioned it briefly but did not define operational behavior:

Does skipping pause subscription billing?

Does skipping shift next_booking_date?

Does skipping keep the next job but skip the immediate one?

✔ Recommended fix
Add explicit logic:

Skip next visit = cancel the already-created Booking + advance next_booking_date by one interval.

8. Missing housekeeping on “future bookings” created already
If the scheduler generates bookings 7 days ahead, and user:

Pauses subscription

Cancels subscription

Changes schedule

We need to handle already-created Booking rows.

⚠️ Missing logic could cause:

Orphan bookings

Jobs happening even after subscription cancellation

✔ Recommended fix
Define:

Any future bookings that have not entered escrow must be cancelled automatically when subscription pauses/cancels.

Bookings already reserved/escrowed follow normal cancellation flow.

9. Missing admin tools
There are no admin capabilities described:

Admins need:

“Cancel all future bookings for this subscription”

“Change schedule for entire recurring series”

“Override next_booking_date”

"Force rebill next month"

10. No mapping between cleaning subscription and billing intervals
You did not define:

WHEN subscriptions bill

Whether billing recurs on the calendar date or based on service start date

How to handle short months (Feb, months with 5 weeks)

✔ Recommended fix:
Keep Stripe billing on sign-up date each month

next_booking_date must be independent

11. No fraud / misuse prevention for subscription
Example issues:

User signs up for subscription → gets discounted cleaning → immediately cancels

User tries to schedule more visits than plan allows

Cleaner tries to create extra jobs under subscription

❌ Critical Missing Section: Subscription + Recurring Sync Rules
You must clearly define:

Who owns the schedule: RecurringBooking

Who owns the billing: CleaningSubscription

Who creates actual Bookings: Scheduler via RecurringBooking

How modifications propagate

Right now, Module 9 has duplication and conflict potential.

0. PURPOSE OF MODULE 9
Module 9 powers all repeat business in PureTask:

1️⃣ Recurring Cleaning (Pay-Per-Visit)
Handled by RecurringBooking
→ Automatically generates future cleaning Bookings on a weekly / biweekly / monthly cycle.
→ Charges credits per job.

Handled by CleaningSubscription
→ Bills monthly via Stripe Subscription
→ Locks in a discounted recurring cleaning schedule
→ Optionally includes a number of visits per month.

Handled by ClientMembership
→ Paid monthly
→ Provides discounts + perks across ALL bookings
→ Can combine with RecurringBooking or Subscriptions.

2. ARCHITECTURE OVERVIEW
THE MOST IMPORTANT DESIGN DECISION:
✅ RecurringBooking = The scheduling engine
❗ CleaningSubscription = Billing + perks
❗ ClientMembership = Global benefits
This gives us:

One reliable place that decides when future bookings occur

One clean pipeline for billing (Subscription)

One universal layer (Membership) that can apply to anything

No duplication. No conflicts.

3. RECURRING BOOKING ENGINE
(Works for both pay-per-visit and subscription users)

3.1 How Recurring Booking is created
Scenario 1 — Client selects “Weekly/Biweekly/Monthly” during checkout
System creates:

A Booking for the first visit

A RecurringBooking for future visits

Scenario 2 — Client taps “Make this recurring”
System creates new RecurringBooking using:

Same cleaner

Same time/day

Same tasks

First recurrence = booking date + frequency interval

Scenario 3 — Client buys a Cleaning Subscription
System creates BOTH:

CleaningSubscription (billing + config)

RecurringBooking tied via recurring_booking_id

3.2 Daily Scheduler (Core Engine)
Runs once per night (or every hour for smoother load balancing).

Algorithm:
Find recurring series due for next job generation
Retrieve RecurringBookings where:

is_active = true
AND (pause_until IS NULL OR pause_until < today)
AND next_booking_date <= (today + generation_window_days)
Recommended generation_window_days = 7.

2. Generate the next Booking
Create Booking with:

client_email, cleaner_email

date = next_booking_date

start_time = RB.start_time

hours = RB.hours

tasks, address

subscription_id = RB.subscription_id

recurring_booking_id = RB.id

status = scheduled

total_price = price snapshot

THEN run:

Pricing Engine (Module 4)

Credits/Escrow (Module 2)

Fallback Cleaner logic (if assigned cleaner is unavailable)

Notifications (Module 8)

3. Advance recurrence date
If weekly → +7 days  
If biweekly → +14 days  
If monthly → +1 month (respect smart month rules)
4. Handle cleaner unavailability or blocked state
If preferred cleaner:

is inactive

blocked by client

blacked out for vacation

removed service location

repeatedly declines recurring bookings

reliability below threshold

🎯 Trigger Fallback Match (Module 5)
→ Find the best cleaner alternative
→ Notify client (“Temporary replacement assigned”)

5. Skip & Pause Logic
Skip next visit
System cancels the already-generated future Booking

System increases next_booking_date by 1 interval

Pause series
Set:

is_active = false
pause_until = date
Scheduler skips until pause ends.

Resume
Set:

is_active = true
pause_until = null
Recalculate next_booking_date = next valid date.

6. Cancel recurring series
Set:

is_active = false
recurring_booking_id removed from future Bookings
pause_until = null
Also:

Cancel future Bookings that have not entered escrow

Future Bookings already escrowed follow cancellation rules

4. CLEANING SUBSCRIPTION ENGINE
(Fixed monthly price + guaranteed recurring cleanings)

4.1 Plan Structure
A CleaningSubscription defines:

✔ Billing:
Stripe subscription ID

Monthly auto-bill

Monthly_included_visits (computed using frequency OR explicit)

✔ Schedule:
Frequency

Day of week

Time window

Tasks/hours/address

next_booking_date

✔ Perks:
Cleaning discount (applies to each visit)

Priority matching for fallback

Optional free cancellations

4.2 Discount and Pricing Rules
When generating a Booking under subscription:

Compute base price from Pricing Engine

Subscription-level discount is applied

Membership discount is also applied

Apply rules:

🟦 DISCOUNT PRIORITY RULES
Subscription discount

Membership discount

Recurring loyalty discount (if enabled)

🟦 DISCOUNT CAP RULE
Total discount cannot exceed 30% (configurable).

4.3 Monthly Included Visits
Define:

If frequency = weekly → monthly_included_visits = 4
If biweekly → monthly_included_visits = 2
If monthly → monthly_included_visits = 1
Track in CleaningSubscription:

total_cleanings_completed

included vs extra visits

extra visit fees (in credits)

4.4 Stripe Billing Webhooks
invoice.payment_succeeded
Set status to active

Update next_billing_date

Reset included visit counters

invoice.payment_failed
Set status to past_due

Pause linked RecurringBooking

customer.subscription.deleted
Set status to cancelled

Disable RecurringBooking

4.5 Pausing, Resuming, Cancelling
Pause Subscription
status = "paused"
paused_until = date
Linked RecurringBooking set to inactive.

Resume Subscription
status = "active"
paused_until = null
Re-enable RecurringBooking.

Cancel Subscription
Cancel Stripe subscription

Set status = cancelled

Deactivate RecurringBooking

Cancel future generated Bookings

No refunds for skipped visits unless explicitly allowed

✅ MODULE 10 — REVIEW & ERROR ANALYSIS (Base44-only version)
Below is a complete professional audit — I am acting as CTO + CPO here.

❌ 1. MAJOR ISSUE: Analytics Entities Were Designed for SQL / Neon — NOT Base44
Base44 is NOT a relational database.
It cannot efficiently store:

Daily snapshot tables

Analytics fact tables

Cohort tables

Complex materialized views

Per-booking/per-cleaner/per-day analytics logs

If you try storing thousands of daily rows in Base44:

❗You will hit:
cost issues

query performance issues

slow admin dashboard

broken analytics

hard-to-query datasets

Base44 is optimized for operational automations, not analytics storage.

✔ FIX:
Instead of creating persistent analytics tables, we must use:

➜ Option A: Base44 Aggregation Automations
Automations that compute metrics dynamically and save:

only high-level metrics

only small aggregated objects

not raw historical analytics data

➜ Option B: Base44 “Analytics Store” JSON fields
Store only summaries inside entities as JSON blobs:

Example:

CleanerProfile.analytics_summary = {
   total_jobs: 34,
   cancel_rate: 4,
   reliability_trend: [92, 94, 95, 96]
}
➜ Option C: Base44 Computed KPIs (no storage)
Compute on demand using:

flow filters

find operations

count operations

aggregations done at runtime

❌ 2. ERROR: Daily Snapshot Tables Won’t Work in Base44
Module 10 currently uses structures like:

AnalyticsDaily

BookingAnalyticsDaily

CleanerAnalyticsDaily

SubscriptionAnalyticsDaily

MembershipAnalyticsDaily

These are fact tables.

Base44 does not support:

large append-only tables (100k–10M rows)

multi-column indexing

heavy aggregation queries

cross-table joins

analytical workloads

✔ FIX:
Replace all analytic fact tables with aggregated metrics stored in dedicated entities, like:

AnalyticsSummary {
   date: string (optional),
   platform_kpis: { ... },
   cleaner_kpis: { ... },
   subscription_kpis: { ... },
   membership_kpis: { ... }
}
Or store:

➜ 1 row per DAY
But NOT per cleaner, per booking, per subscription.

You can store maybe 30–90 rows (one month of daily metrics) safely.

But NOT tens of thousands.

❌ 3. ERROR: “Historical Analytics” Conflicts With Base44’s Storage Model
Stored history like:

CleanerAnalyticsDaily (1 row per cleaner per day)

SubscriptionAnalyticsDaily (1 row per subscription per day)

BookingAnalyticsDaily (1 row per booking per day)

This is impossible inside Base44 for scaling.

✔ FIX:
We should compute historical performance on demand, not store it.

Example:

If admin opens a cleaner profile → Base44 automation generates:

past 30 days performance

jobs_done

cancellations

reliability trend

And simply returns it, without storing it permanently.

❌ 4. ERROR: Module 10 assumes SQL-style aggregations (sum, avg, group by)
Base44 is NOT SQL.
It cannot run raw database queries.

All analytics must be computed via:

find()

filter()

sort()

count()

map()

reduce() through automation logic

This is slower and cannot handle “big data”.

✔ FIX:
Analytics must be:

A. Pre-aggregated at time of event
Example:

When cleaner finishes a job:
→ Immediately update cleaner’s reliability summary object.

B. Stored only as rolled-up fields
Example:

CleanerProfile.reliability_score
CleanerProfile.total_jobs
CleanerProfile.cancellation_rate
CleanerProfile.earnings_monthly
C. Computed on demand for dashboards
Real-time dashboard metrics are calculated dynamically by automation, NOT stored.

✔ 5. GOOD PARTS OF MODULE 10 (KEEP THESE)
The KPI definitions are excellent and correct:

Fill rate

Match time

Cancellation rate

No-show rate

Cleaner acceptance rate

Revenue

Refund leakage

MRR

Subscription churn

LTV, CAC (manual input)

Dispute rate

Reliability distribution

The categories of analytics are perfect.

The alerting logic works well in Base44:

High cancellations

High dispute rate

Cleaner reliability drop

Payment failures spike

Matching delays

Revenue or booking anomalies

All of these can be implemented in Base44.

❌ 6. ERROR: Alerts depend on historical baselines (not easy without storage)
If you want to detect:

“cancellations 3× higher than average”

“disputes spike vs last month”

That requires historical baseline data, which Base44 does NOT store well.

✔ FIX (Base44-compatible):
Store only rolling window aggregates such as:

AnalyticsRolling {
   last_7_days: { ... },
   last_30_days: { ... },
   last_90_days: { ... }
}
This is small, safe, and powerful.

❌ 7. ERROR: SubscriptionAnalyticsDaily & MembershipAnalyticsDaily too heavy
MRR (monthly recurring revenue) and subscription churn do NOT require:

daily per-subscription tracking

Instead:

✔ FIX:
Store these aggregates in a single entity:

SubscriptionMetrics {
   active_subscriptions: 23,
   churn_rate_monthly: 4.7,
   mrr: 1830.00,
   next_billing_events: [...],
   plan_mix: {weekly: 12, biweekly: 8, monthly: 3}
}
And update this entity:

every night

or after major events (new subscription, cancellation, pause)

❌ 8. ERROR: Marketing funnel analytics require events tracking (Base44-complex)
You suggested:

MarketingFunnelAnalytics {
  date,
  funnel_stage,
  count
}
But Base44 does not support event logs well.

✔ FIX:
Use a single entity to store aggregated funnel metrics:

MarketingFunnel {
   visited: number,
   started_booking: number,
   created_account: number,
   completed_booking: number,
   subscribed: number
}
And update counts via automations.

Gotcha — we’re back to the original plan: Base44 for operations + Neon (Postgres) + n8n for analytics ETL. Good call; that’s the right stack for serious KPIs.

1️⃣ Big Picture: Is the original Module 10 direction correct?
Short answer: yes, directionally it’s strong.

Using Neon/Postgres as an analytics warehouse is exactly what you want.

Designing fact tables like AnalyticsDaily, BookingAnalyticsDaily, CleanerAnalyticsDaily, etc. is the right approach for long-term reporting, dashboards, ML later.

Using n8n to:

listen to Base44 webhooks,

transform events,

and insert into Neon
is also correct.

So we don’t need to throw Module 10 away; we just need to:

tighten schemas,

align them with Modules 1–9 more explicitly,

clarify ETL flows,

and add some missing details for implementation.

2️⃣ Issues / Gaps / Places to Tighten
2.1 Revenue + credits can be double-counted if we’re not strict
Right now, we have:

Credits-based internal economy (Module 2).

Stripe USD payments (cards).

Refunds / adjustments.

Payouts to cleaners.

If we just dump “revenue_usd” and “revenue_credits” into AnalyticsDaily without a clear definition, you can:

Double-count revenue (once at credit purchase, again at booking).

Confuse GMV vs revenue vs net profit.

🛠 Fix: you MUST define canonical meanings:

GMV (Gross Marketplace Volume) – sum of booking values in USD (or credits) at time of approval.

Revenue – your platform fee / margin (e.g., 20% of GMV).

Cash In – Stripe payments + other top-ups.

Refunds – Stripe refunds / credit refunds.

Payouts – sum of CleanerEarning → Stripe Connect payouts.

Then in your analytics tables, always be explicit:

gmv_usd

platform_revenue_usd

cash_collected_usd

refunds_usd

payouts_usd

And similarly in credits:

gmv_credits

platform_fee_credits

refunds_credits

2.2 Fact table schemas are good… but missing indices & grain clarity
You defined:

AnalyticsDaily – one row per day

BookingAnalyticsDaily – one row per booking per day

CleanerAnalyticsDaily – one row per cleaner per day

etc.

That’s good, but:

For BookingAnalyticsDaily, we should clarify:
Is it one row per booking per day (snapshot of state each day)
or one row per booking once it’s completed?

If you go with per booking per day, the table can get big quickly and you need:

composite index on (booking_id, date)

plus maybe (date) for time-based reports.

If you go with one row per booking when fully closed, that’s simpler:

More like BookingFact.

Metric recalc / backfill is easier.

Fewer rows.

💡 Suggestion:
Use two main layers:

booking_fact (one row per booking, final state)

analytics_daily (aggregated metrics per day, built from booking_fact, credit transactions, payouts, disputes, etc.)

Only add *_Daily per-entity if you actually need day-by-day dimension.

2.3 Reliability linkage: use Module 6 as source of truth
You proposed CleanerAnalyticsDaily with:

reliability_score

tier

cancellation_rate

no_show_rate

etc.

But those already exist in CleanerProfile and are updated by Module 6.

If CleanerAnalyticsDaily recomputes them again from raw bookings, you’ll get:

mismatches if formulas change,

double work,

inconsistencies between “live” reliability and historical reliability.

💡 Suggestion:

Treat CleanerProfile + Module 6 as authoritative for reliability.

In CleanerAnalyticsDaily, just snapshot the values from CleanerProfile once per day for historical trending:

cleaner_email
date
reliability_score_at_eod
tier_at_eod
attendance_rate_at_eod
...
So CleanerAnalyticsDaily is “whatever Module 6 said at that end of day”, not a different computation.

2.4 Subscription & Membership analytics: granularity overkill
SubscriptionAnalyticsDaily + MembershipAnalyticsDaily are fine in theory, but they might be overkill as full per-day per-subscription/per-membership tables.

In most practical setups:

You track individual subscriptions in a subscription table.

Then compute aggregates per day/month in:

subscription_mrr_daily or

subscription_kpi_daily.

💡 Suggestion:

Keep a subscription_fact table (one row per CleaningSubscription with status, start date, end date, stripe_subscription_id, etc.)

Then build a simpler subscription_kpi_daily (1 row/day):

subscription_kpi_daily {
  date,
  active_subscriptions,
  new_subscriptions,
  cancelled_subscriptions,
  mrr_usd,
  churn_rate,
  expansion_mrr_usd
}
Same pattern for memberships.

2.5 MarketingFunnelAnalytics is too vague for implementation
You had:

MarketingFunnelAnalytics {
  date,
  funnel_stage,
  count
}
That’s fine conceptually, but:

We need to define what triggers each stage:

“visited” – from where? Web analytics? Not Base44.

“started_booking” – DraftBooking created?

“created_account” – ClientProfile created?

“completed_booking” – Booking.status = approved?

“subscribed” – CleaningSubscription or ClientMembership created?

Because Base44 doesn’t see website events like page views, you realistically can only track:

from “started_booking” onward.

💡 Suggestion:

Either:

integrate a separate web analytics tool for top-of-funnel, OR

redefine funnel stages to things inside Base44, like:

started_booking

client_signed_up

first_booking_completed

second_booking_completed

subscription_started

And make MarketingFunnelAnalytics a derived table in Neon populated by n8n.

2.6 Alerting logic lacks concrete thresholds / formulas
You defined:

spikes in cancellations

spikes in no-shows

spikes in disputes

payment failures, etc.

but not:

how we compare (vs what baseline? last 7 days? last 30 days?)

what triggers severity: low / medium / high?

💡 Suggestion:

Define in the spec:

Baseline = rolling 7-day average for each metric.

Trigger if today’s value:

HIGH alert: > 3× baseline

MEDIUM alert: > 2× baseline

LOW alert: > 1.5× baseline

Have n8n compute:

baseline using analytics_daily

compare with current day

send alert to Slack/Email accordingly.

2.7 Time zones & “end of day” not defined
For daily metrics (AnalyticsDaily, CleanerAnalyticsDaily etc.), we must know:

what time zone defines “a day” (e.g., platform time, UTC, local)

what time we run the batch jobs (e.g., 3am in that time zone)

💡 Suggestion:

Use UTC in Neon for all timestamps.

But define a platform_timezone (e.g., America/Los_Angeles) for grouping by day.

In ETL, convert event_time → “platform local date” for daily aggregations.

3️⃣ Suggestions to Make Module 10 Stronger (Neon + Base44 + n8n world)
Now I’ll outline improvements, not just errors.

3.1 Define a clear ETL pattern with n8n
Right now the design assumes “we somehow put data into Neon”. Let’s be explicit:

Event flow:
Base44 emits webhook:

booking.created, booking.updated, payment.captured, dispute.resolved, subscription.created, etc.

n8n receives webhook and:

Normalizes payload into a “event” format

Writes into event_log table in Neon OR directly updates fact tables

Periodic batch jobs in n8n:

Nightly: build/update analytics_daily from booking_fact, credit_transaction, payment, payout, etc.

Hourly: update booking_fact statuses.

Clarify:

Which metrics are computed real-time (e.g., dashboards that refresh often)

Which are nightly (cohorts, LTV, churn)

3.2 Use dimension tables for cleaners, clients, subscriptions
For analytics patterns, it’s best to have:

dim_cleaner

dim_client

dim_subscription

dim_membership

These store relatively static attributes (tier, region, signup date, acquisition channel).

Then fact tables (booking_fact, payment_fact, etc.) reference them by key.

This simplifies:

grouping by tier, region, source

joining in analytics tools

3.3 Clean up and rename some tables to classic analytics style
Instead of:

BookingAnalyticsDaily → use booking_fact

CleanerAnalyticsDaily → either:

cleaner_daily_fact

or rely on cleaner_snapshot from Module 6 (mirrored into Neon)

AnalyticsDaily → platform_kpi_daily

This naming:

makes it obvious what’s “fact” vs “aggregate KPI”.

3.4 Explicit KPI formulas
Add explicit formulas so there’s no ambiguity. For example:

Fill rate =
# bookings with status in (completed, approved) / # bookings created

Cleaner acceptance rate =
# bookings accepted by cleaner / # bookings offered to cleaner

No-show rate =
# bookings with no-show status / # scheduled bookings

Dispute rate =
# bookings with disputes / # completed bookings

Churn rate (subscriptions) =
cancelled_subscriptions_in_period / active_subscriptions_at_period_start

MRR =
sum(monthly_price of all active subscriptions)

Putting these formulas in the Module 10 spec will be a huge win later when we implement.

3.5 Decide on v1 scope vs future scope
You don’t need the full Snowflake-level analytics on day 1.

I’d suggest marking:

v1 must-haves:
booking_fact

platform_kpi_daily

basic cleaner metrics (jobs, earnings, rating, reliability snapshot)

disputes & refunds summary

subscription_kpi_daily & membership_kpi_daily (aggregates)

alerting on:

cancellations, no-shows, disputes, payment failures

v2 later:
cohorts

LTV/CAC

ML models

marketing funnel

deep subscription analytics

fraud detection

4️⃣ Do we need more details inside this module?
Yes, three main areas:

Event → Fact Table Mapping

Which Base44 webhook maps to which fact table write.

For each event type, how we update booking_fact, payment_fact, etc.

Recompute logic (idempotency + backfill)

How to recompute KPIs if a bug is found.

How to backfill historical data if schema changes.

Use created_at vs updated_at semantics properly.

Access patterns (who sees what, how)

Admin dashboards pulling from Neon

Maybe internal Metabase / Supabase Studio / other BI tool reading Neon

Cleaner leaderboard & client stats: either mirrored into Base44 or read directly from Neon via API.

✅ MODULE 10 — ADVANCED ANALYTICS & KPI ENGINE
(Final, corrected, Neon + n8n + Base44 version)

1. Purpose
Module 10 is the data brain of PureTask.

It:

Collects events from operational systems (Base44)

Pipes them into Neon (Postgres) via n8n

Stores them in clean fact & dimension tables

Computes KPIs, dashboards, and alerts for:

CEO (north star metrics)

COO (operations)

CMO (growth/marketing)

CFO (financials)

Product / Ops (reliability, disputes, subscriptions)

This module does not affect customer-facing flows directly; it consumes data from Modules 1–9 and makes the business visible.

2. Architecture Overview
2.1 Systems involved
Base44 — source of truth for:

Bookings, Clients, Cleaners

Payments, Credits, Payouts

Disputes, Subscriptions, Memberships

Reliability scores, tiers

n8n — ETL / integration layer:

Receives webhooks from Base44

Transforms events

Inserts/updates rows in Neon

Neon (Postgres) — analytics warehouse:

Stores fact & dimension tables

Runs aggregations

Serves dashboards & BI tools

3. Canonical Metrics & Financial Definitions
To avoid confusion & double counting, we standardize:

3.1 Currencies
Platform runs on credits, with a fixed exchange:

CREDITS_PER_USD = 10

Stripe deals in USD.

We track both:

*_credits — internal economy

*_usd — financial reporting

3.2 Key financial definitions
GMV (Gross Marketplace Volume)
Total value of completed/approved bookings (before refunds, in USD).

gmv_usd = sum(booking.final_charge_credits) / CREDITS_PER_USD
Platform Revenue
Your margin: the platform fee from each job (before refunds).

platform_revenue_usd = sum(booking.platform_fee_credits) / CREDITS_PER_USD
Cash Collected
Money Stripe actually charged to customers.

Refunds
Refunds issued to clients (via Stripe or credits).

Payouts
Money sent to cleaners (Stripe Connect payouts).

All Neon tables must distinguish:

GMV vs platform revenue vs cash vs payouts vs refunds.

4. Neon Schema — Fact & Dimension Tables
4.1 Dimensions (slowly changing attributes)
4.1.1 dim_client
client_id (PK)

email

created_at

acquisition_channel (optional)

region / city

first_booking_date

is_membership_active (cached flag)

4.1.2 dim_cleaner
cleaner_id (PK)

email

created_at

home_city

initial_tier

current_tier

is_active

4.1.3 dim_subscription
subscription_id (PK)

client_id

cleaner_id

frequency

plan_type (weekly, biweekly, monthly)

monthly_price_usd

discount_percentage

started_date

cancelled_date

status (active, paused, cancelled)

stripe_subscription_id

4.1.4 dim_membership
membership_id (PK)

client_id

tier (Plus, Platinum)

monthly_fee_usd

started_date

cancelled_date

status

stripe_subscription_id

4.2 Fact tables (event-level, granular)
4.2.1 booking_fact
Grain: one row per booking, final state.

Columns:

booking_id (PK)

client_id

cleaner_id

created_at

approved_at (null if never approved)

status_final (approved, cancelled, disputed, etc.)

is_subscription (bool)

subscription_id (nullable)

is_recurring (bool)

recurring_booking_id (nullable)

hours_booked

hours_worked (from check-in/out)

gmv_credits (final_charge_credits)

platform_fee_credits

refund_credits (total)

gmv_usd

platform_fee_usd

refund_usd

was_fallback_used (bool)

time_to_match_seconds

check_in_delta_minutes (late/early vs scheduled)

check_out_delta_minutes

rating (null if no review)

had_dispute (bool)

dispute_category (if any)

cancelled_by (client, cleaner, system, null)

no_show_flag (bool)

This table is built over time by n8n from Base44 booking events.

4.2.2 payment_fact
Grain: one row per Stripe payment / charge.

payment_id

client_id

amount_usd

status (pending, completed, refunded, partially_refunded)

refunded_amount_usd

created_at

booking_id (nullable, for direct booking payments)

source (card, wallet, etc.)

4.2.3 payout_fact
Grain: one row per payout to cleaner.

payout_id

cleaner_id

amount_usd

status (pending, processing, completed, failed)

created_at

completed_at

batch_reference (for weekly payout batches)

4.2.4 dispute_fact
Grain: one row per dispute.

dispute_id

booking_id

client_id

cleaner_id

category

filed_by (client, cleaner, system)

status_final

resolved_outcome (client_favor, cleaner_favor, split, no_action)

final_refund_credits

final_refund_usd

created_at

resolved_at

4.2.5 subscription_fact
Grain: one row per CleaningSubscription lifecycle.

subscription_id

client_id

cleaner_id

started_date

cancelled_date

status (current)

monthly_price_usd

discount_percentage

monthly_included_visits

extra_visit_price_usd

total_visits_lifetime

total_revenue_usd

4.2.6 membership_fact
Grain: one row per membership lifecycle.

membership_id

client_id

tier

started_date

cancelled_date

status

monthly_fee_usd

total_revenue_usd

total_savings_usd

4.3 Snapshot / KPI tables
4.3.1 platform_kpi_daily
Grain: one row per calendar day (platform time zone).

date

new_clients

new_cleaners

active_clients

active_cleaners

total_bookings

completed_bookings

cancelled_bookings

disputed_bookings

gmv_usd

platform_revenue_usd

refunds_usd

payouts_usd

dispute_rate

cancel_rate

no_show_rate

avg_rating

avg_match_time_seconds

active_subscriptions

subscription_mrr_usd

active_memberships

membership_mrr_usd

This is computed nightly from fact tables.

4.3.2 cleaner_daily_snapshot
Grain: one row per cleaner per day (snapshot at end of day).

date

cleaner_id

total_jobs

completed_jobs

cancellations

no_shows

earnings_usd

earnings_credits

reliability_score (copy from Module 6)

tier

attendance_rate

punctuality_rate

cancellation_rate

no_show_rate

dispute_rate

average_rating

Important:
Derived from CleanerProfile and Module 6 results, not recomputed from raw bookings (to keep consistency).

4.3.3 subscription_kpi_daily
Grain: one row per day.

date

active_subscriptions

new_subscriptions

cancelled_subscriptions

subscription_mrr_usd

churn_rate (daily / trailing 30d)

avg_discount_percentage

included_visits_this_period

completed_visits_this_period

4.3.4 membership_kpi_daily
date

active_memberships

new_memberships

cancelled_memberships

membership_mrr_usd

avg_discount_percentage

savings_usd_today

total_savings_usd_cumulative

4.3.5 marketing_funnel_daily
Redefined to only track stages we can see inside Base44:

date

started_booking_count (DraftBooking created)

client_signup_count (ClientProfile created)

first_booking_completed_count

second_booking_completed_count

subscription_started_count

membership_started_count

5. KPI Formulas (Explicit)
Here are the canonical formulas to avoid ambiguity.

5.1 Marketplace Health
Fill Rate
completed_bookings / total_bookings_created

Cancellation Rate
cancelled_bookings / total_bookings_created

No-Show Rate (cleaner)
bookings_with_no_show_flag / scheduled_bookings

Dispute Rate
bookings_with_dispute / completed_bookings

Average Match Time
avg(time_to_match_seconds) over all matched bookings.

5.2 Cleaner Metrics
Cleaner Acceptance Rate
# accepted_offers / # job_offers
(populated via SmartMatch-related logs)

Cleaner Completion Rate
completed_jobs / jobs_assigned

Cleaner Earnings (period)
sum of payout_fact.amount_usd where cleaner_id = X.

Reliability Score
Taken directly from Module 6 and mirrored to Neon.

5.3 Financial Metrics
GMV (Period)
sum of booking_fact.gmv_usd for bookings approved during that period.

Platform Revenue
sum of platform_fee_usd.

Refund Rate
total_refunds_usd / gmv_usd.

Payout Ratio
total_payouts_usd / gmv_usd.

5.4 Subscription & Membership
MRR (Subscriptions)
sum of monthly_price_usd for active subscriptions at period end.

Churn Rate (Subscriptions)
cancelled_subscriptions_in_period / active_subscriptions_at_start.

Membership MRR
sum of monthly_fee_usd for active memberships.

6. ETL Flow (Base44 → n8n → Neon)
6.1 Event ingestion
Base44 emits webhooks for:

booking.created / booking.updated / booking.approved / booking.cancelled

payment.created / payment.refunded

cleaner_earning.updated / payout.created / payout.completed

dispute.created / dispute.resolved

subscription.created / subscription.updated / subscription.cancelled

membership.created / membership.cancelled

reliability.updated (Module 6)

n8n:

Receives each webhook.

Normalizes payload into a standard event format.

Writes/updates the appropriate fact/dim rows in Neon.

6.2 Nightly batch jobs
Once per day (e.g., 3 AM platform time):

Recompute platform_kpi_daily for the prior day.

Append cleaner_daily_snapshot from latest CleanerProfile state.

Update subscription_kpi_daily and membership_kpi_daily.

Compute or update alert baselines (rolling averages).

7. Alerts & Anomaly Detection
Alerts are generated in n8n using Neon queries.

7.1 Baselines
For each metric:

Compute rolling 7-day average:

avg_cancel_rate_7d

avg_no_show_rate_7d

avg_dispute_rate_7d

avg_payment_failure_rate_7d

7.2 Alert thresholds
Example:

HIGH alert:
today’s value > 3× rolling 7-day avg

MEDIUM alert:
today’s value > 2× rolling 7-day avg

LOW alert:
today’s value > 1.5× rolling 7-day avg

Alerts send to:

Slack #ops-alerts

Admin email

Optional SMS for critical issues

Example alerts:

“Cleaner no-show rate is 3.2× higher than weekly baseline”

“Payment failure rate spiked to 12% today”

“Dispute volume for cleaner X is 4× normal”

8. Dashboards (Who Sees What)
These dashboards read from Neon, not Base44.

8.1 CEO / North Star Dashboard
GMV, platform revenue

Weekly active clients & cleaners

Fill rate

Retention curves

LTV/CAC estimates (even if manual at first)

Subscription & membership MRR

8.2 COO / Operations Dashboard
Bookings by status

Cancellation & no-show trends

SmartMatch metrics: time-to-match, fallback usage

Cleaner performance & tier distribution

Dispute and refund trends

8.3 CMO / Growth Dashboard
Funnel: started booking → account → first booking → repeat → subscription

Cohorts by signup month

Subscription & membership adoption

Referral performance (if/when added)

8.4 CFO / Finance Dashboard
GMV vs revenue vs payouts vs refunds

Gross margin & net margin

MRR breakdown

Aging of credits (liability view)

Payout batches & anomalies

8.5 Cleaner Leaderboard (internal or future cleaner app)
Rankings by:

earnings

reliability

rating

streaks

9. v1 vs v2 Scope
To keep implementation sane, we break it into phases.

v1 (Launch-ready)
dim_client, dim_cleaner

booking_fact, payment_fact, payout_fact, dispute_fact

platform_kpi_daily

cleaner_daily_snapshot

Subscription & membership metrics (basic MRR counts)

A few alerts:

cancellation spike

no-show spike

dispute spike

payment failure spike

v2 (Scale-up)
subscription_fact, membership_fact in full detail

marketing_funnel_daily

cohorts, retention curves

LTV/CAC pipeline

ML-style scoring (churn prediction, fraud, etc.)

Cleaner + client segmentation

10. Integration with Modules 1–9
Module 1 (Booking Lifecycle)
Drives booking_fact: status, timestamps, hours.

Module 2 (Credits & Payments)
Drives payment_fact, booking_fact financial fields (gmv, refunds).

Module 3 (Payout Engine)
Drives payout_fact.

Module 4 (Pricing Engine)
Influences booking_fact.gmv_* & platform_fee_*.

Module 5 (SmartMatch)
Feeds into booking_fact.time_to_match_seconds, was_fallback_used.

Module 6 (Reliability & Tier)
Feeds into cleaner_daily_snapshot with authoritative reliability values.

Module 7 (Disputes & Claims)
Feeds dispute_fact and dispute-related fields in booking_fact.

Module 8 (Notifications)
Can be tracked in a future notification_fact if you want engagement analytics.

Module 9 (Recurring & Subscription Engine)
Feeds subscription_fact, membership_fact, and subscription-related fields in booking_fact.

You’re right to call this out, and thank you for pushing on it — I was too pessimistic in how I talked about Base44 before.

I went back through the Base44 docs you uploaded and here’s the corrected, reality-based picture of what Base44 can actually do.

1. What I got wrong
I previously implied things like:

“Base44 can’t really be used for analytics / daily snapshots”

“You really need Neon for any serious KPI tables”

“Base44 is just a no-code layer, not a real backend”

Those were over-simplified and not fully accurate given your actual Base44 setup.

From your docs, Base44 is way more like a full backend platform with:

Real SQL tables under the hood

Automatic migrations

Automatic CRUD APIs

Background jobs / scheduled tasks

Webhooks

A dedicated CleanerAnalytics entity for periodic metrics

A dedicated AnalyticsEvent + Event entities for funnels & event logging

So yeah, I was too restrictive in my earlier “it can’t do X” statements. That’s on me.

2. What Base44 actually supports (based on your docs)
2.1 Real database tables + migrations
Base44 absolutely does maintain SQL tables for each entity and auto-migrates them when you change schemas.

So it’s not some toy KV store — it’s a proper relational backend with managed migrations.

2.2 Auto CRUD API endpoints
For every entity (Booking, ClientProfile, CleanerProfile, Credit, Payment, etc.), Base44 exposes RESTful CRUD endpoints and even bulkCreate + schema endpoints.

That’s already “real backend” behavior.

2.3 Webhooks + scheduled tasks (cron-like)
Base44:

Generates webhooks for entity events (create/update/delete).

Has scheduled tasks / background logic for:

enforcing booking expirations

recurring scheduling

updating reliability metrics regularly

So it does have the engine you’d normally use for nightly jobs, periodic analytics, etc.

2.4 Payment, payout, escrow, recurring, reliability — all baked in
From your docs:

Payment flow & Stripe integration via Payment and Booking.stripe_payment_intent_id

Payouts via Payout + stripe_transfer_id

Credit escrow logic via Booking.escrow_credits_reserved, final_charge_credits, refund_credits + ClientProfile.credits_balance

Recurring scheduling via RecurringBooking + background process generating future Bookings

Reliability system automation using Booking + Review data, updating metrics + CleanerProfile.reliability_score on a schedule

That’s a lot of backend sophistication. You weren’t exaggerating.

2.5 Analytics-related entities already exist
This is the big one where my earlier comments were too limited:

CleanerAnalytics — explicitly described as storing “daily or periodic analytics for cleaners, such as total earnings, bookings count, and average rating.”

Event — logs booking-related events: booking_created, check_in, check_out, dispute_opened, refund_issued, etc.

AnalyticsEvent — full-blown funnel analytics entity for:

page_view

booking_started / abandoned / submitted

client_signup_start / success

cleaner_signup steps

job_viewed / job_accepted / job_declined

payment_success / payment_failed, etc.

And the docs explicitly say reliability metrics are “regularly aggregated and processed by background automation (e.g. cron jobs) updating CleanerProfile and CleanerAnalytics entities.”

So Base44 is already being used as an analytics store for at least:

cleaner performance

funnel events

reliability trends

That directly contradicts my early “Base44 can’t handle analytics tables” vibe. You were right to flag that.

3. So what are Base44’s real capabilities?
From your docs, Base44 can:

Store operational data (Bookings, Payments, Credits, Disputes, etc.)

Store analytics data (CleanerAnalytics, AnalyticsEvent, Event)

Run background jobs/scheduled tasks that:

scan entities

aggregate metrics

update analytics entities periodically

Emit webhooks for any entity change, to integrate with external tools if you want (e.g. n8n, Neon), but it’s not required.

Integrate with:

Stripe for payments & payouts

Core.SendEmail, Core.InvokeLLM, Core.UploadFile, Core.GenerateImage, etc.

So yeah — it does a lot.

For v1, and honestly even v2, you absolutely can:

Keep all operations and analytics inside Base44

Use CleanerAnalytics + AnalyticsEvent + new “PlatformAnalytics” / “Dashboard*” entities

Use scheduled tasks to compute daily / weekly KPIs

A separate warehouse (Neon) becomes a nice-to-have optimization later, not a hard requirement.

4. Where my caution still comes from (but more nuanced now)
I don’t want to pretend Base44 is magically infinite.

Even though Base44 can:

store analytics entities

run cron-like jobs

log events

at very large scale (millions of rows over years), most teams eventually:

move heavy analytics into a dedicated warehouse

connect BI tools directly to that warehouse

keep the app backend focused on operational traffic

But that’s a scale / convenience tradeoff, not a “Base44 can’t do it” limitation.

Given your current stage, a realistic truth is:

You’re totally fine implementing Module 10 inside Base44 only.

You already have entities intended for analytics (CleanerAnalytics, AnalyticsEvent).

You can add PlatformAnalytics, SubscriptionAnalytics, etc. as more entities.

Later, if you feel the pain, you can add Neon for deeper BI — but we don’t need to design around it from day one if you don’t want to.

5. What I’d correct moving forward
Here’s how I’ll treat Base44 from now on in our modules:

Assume Base44 is a full backend with:

SQL tables

migrations

background jobs

analytics storage

webhooks

Stripe + email + file + LLM integrations

Design v1/v2 modules to run entirely in Base44:

Operational flows

Reliability system

Disputes & payouts

Recurring & subscriptions

Analytics & KPIs (using CleanerAnalytics, AnalyticsEvent, and new aggregate entities)

Treat Neon / n8n as:

Optional “Phase 3+” improvements for:

very large historical reporting

plugging in fancy BI tools

hardcore data science

Not as a requirement to make the product work.

✅ MODULE 10 — ANALYTICS & KPI ENGINE (BASE44-ONLY, FINAL VERSION)
0. Goal of this module
Turn PureTask into a data-driven marketplace using only Base44:

No Neon

No external warehouse

No n8n required

Everything runs through:

Base44 entities (Booking, CleanerProfile, CleanerAnalytics, AnalyticsEvent, etc.)

1. Core design principles (Base44-only)
Event-driven updates
Whenever something important happens (booking approved, dispute resolved, payout processed), we update small analytic fields immediately.

Aggregate, don’t hoard raw logs
Base44 can store events, but we don’t want millions of rows.
We use:

Event / AnalyticsEvent for key events

A few aggregated analytics entities for KPIs

Rolling windows & snapshots
We don’t store infinite history.
We store:

Daily snapshot docs (e.g. last 365 days)

Rolling 7-day / 30-day metrics

Per-cleaner/per-platform summary blobs

CleanerProfile & CleanerAnalytics are source of truth for reliability
Module 6 owns reliability math.
Module 10 just reads / snapshots it.

2. Entities we’ll use
2.1 Existing operational entities (no changes here)
Booking

ClientProfile

CleanerProfile

CreditTransaction

Payment

Payout

Dispute

RecurringBooking

CleaningSubscription

ClientMembership

2.2 Existing analytics-ish entities
CleanerAnalytics
Used for per-cleaner aggregates / periodic stats.

Event
General event log (booking_created, check_in, check_out, etc.).

AnalyticsEvent
Funnel and marketing-ish events (booking_started, signup_started, payment_failed, etc.).

We extend these ones conceptually, but don’t break them.

3. New Analytics Entities (Base44)
We’ll add a small set of dedicated entities for platform-wide KPIs and dashboards.

3.1 PlatformAnalyticsDaily (NEW)
Grain: one record per day, platform-wide summary.
Retention: ~365 days max (cleanup old records via cron).

Fields:

PlatformAnalyticsDaily {
  date: string,                // "2025-11-21"
  total_bookings: number,
  completed_bookings: number,
  cancelled_bookings: number,
  disputed_bookings: number,

  gmv_credits: number,         // sum of final_charge_credits
  platform_fee_credits: number,
  refunds_credits: number,
  payouts_credits: number,     // optional, mirror payouts in credits

  gmv_usd: number,
  platform_revenue_usd: number,
  refunds_usd: number,
  payouts_usd: number,

  new_clients: number,
  new_cleaners: number,
  active_clients: number,
  active_cleaners: number,

  dispute_rate: number,
  cancel_rate: number,
  no_show_rate: number,
  avg_rating: number,
  avg_match_time_seconds: number,

  active_subscriptions: number,
  subscription_mrr_usd: number,
  active_memberships: number,
  membership_mrr_usd: number
}
Use this for COO/CFO/CEO daily view.

3.2 CleanerDailySnapshot (NEW)
Even though CleanerAnalytics exists, we want clean, time-based “snapshots” without overloading that entity.

Grain: one row per cleaner per day, but we can limit retention (e.g., last 90 days).

CleanerDailySnapshot {
  date: string,
  cleaner_email: string,

  total_jobs: number,
  completed_jobs: number,
  cancellations: number,
  no_shows: number,

  earnings_credits: number,
  earnings_usd: number,

  tier: string,

  attendance_rate: number,
  punctuality_rate: number,
  cancellation_rate: number,
  no_show_rate: number,
  dispute_rate: number,
  average_rating: number
}
This is how we track trends per cleaner without recomputing from scratch every time.

3.3 SubscriptionAnalytics (NEW)
One entity for platform-level subscription KPIs (not one row per sub per day).

SubscriptionAnalytics {
  id: string,                         // singleton, e.g. "global_subscription_stats"
  last_updated: string,               // datetime

  active_subscriptions: number,
  new_subscriptions_7d: number,
  cancelled_subscriptions_7d: number,

}
We recompute this nightly based on CleaningSubscription + Booking.

Same idea as above but for memberships.

MembershipAnalytics {

}
3.5 DashboardCache (NEW)
Pre-aggregated JSON blobs for specific dashboards (CEO, COO, CMO, CFO), so Admin UI can load fast without deep queries.

DashboardCache {
  id: string,             // e.g. "ceo_dashboard", "ops_dashboard", "finance_dashboard"
  last_updated: string,

}
We can maintain 3–5 of these (CEO, COO/Ops, CMO/Growth, CFO/Finance, CleanerLeaderboard).

3.6 SystemAlert (NEW)
For anomaly detection and ops alerts.

SystemAlert {
  id: string,
  type: string,           // "cancellation_spike", "no_show_spike", "payment_fail_spike", etc.
  severity: string,       // "low", "medium", "high", "critical"

  created_at: string,
  resolved_at?: string,
  is_resolved: boolean
}
Admins see these in an Alerts panel and/or via email/SMS.

4. KPIs (Canonical definitions inside Base44)
We keep the same math, just execute it with Base44 automated workflows.

4.1 Financial scaling
Assume:

CREDITS_PER_USD = 10
4.2 Marketplace KPIs (for PlatformAnalyticsDaily)
total_bookings
Count of Bookings created that day.

completed_bookings
Bookings with status in (completed, awaiting_client, approved) and completed_at/check_out_time that day.

cancelled_bookings
Bookings whose final status is cancelled that day.

disputed_bookings
Bookings with a Dispute created that day.

gmv_credits
Sum of final_charge_credits for bookings approved that day.

platform_fee_credits
Sum of platform_fee_credits (or computed as client_credits - cleaner_credits share).

refunds_credits
Sum of CreditTransaction entries with transaction_type = refund that day.

Convert each to USD with / CREDITS_PER_USD.

dispute_rate = disputed_bookings / completed_bookings.

cancel_rate = cancelled_bookings / total_bookings.

no_show_rate = no_show_bookings / scheduled_bookings.

avg_rating = average of Review ratings for that day’s completed jobs.

avg_match_time_seconds = average time from booking created to cleaner accepted.

4.3 Cleaner KPIs (for CleanerDailySnapshot)
We don’t recalc reliability from scratch. We:

Read CleanerProfile fields (from Module 6) at end of day:

reliability_score

tier

attendance_rate, etc.

average_rating

We add daily counts:

total_jobs: bookings assigned that day.

completed_jobs: bookings completed that day.

cancellations: cancellations initiated by this cleaner that day.

no_shows: disputed no_shows that day.

earnings_credits: sum of earning credits for jobs approved that day.

earnings_usd: convert accordingly.

4.4 Subscription & Membership KPIs
From CleaningSubscription & ClientMembership:

active_subscriptions: count where status = active.

subscription_mrr_usd: sum of monthly_price for active.

new_subscriptions_7d: created in last 7 days.

cancelled_subscriptions_7d: status changed to cancelled in last 7 days.

churn_rate_30d: cancelled_subscriptions_30d / active_subscriptions_30d_start.

Similarly for memberships using ClientMembership.

5. Base44 Automations (How it actually runs)
5.1 Event-driven micro-updates (REAL-TIME)
We use Base44 flows that trigger on entity events:

Example triggers:
Booking.created

Booking.updated (status change → completed / approved / cancelled)

Dispute.created / Dispute.resolved

Payment.created / Payment.refunded

Payout.created / Payout.completed

CleaningSubscription.created / .updated

ClientMembership.created / .updated

CleanerProfile.updated (reliability change from Module 6)

On these events, workflows:

Update CleanerAnalytics (per cleaner totals).

Append appropriate Event and/or AnalyticsEvent.

Increment simple counters in ClientProfile or CleanerProfile if useful.

This keeps per-entity summary fields fresh without waiting for nightly cron.

5.2 Nightly “Analytics Cron” (main batch)
Once per day (e.g., 3am platform time):

Compute PlatformAnalyticsDaily for yesterday

Query Bookings, CreditTransactions, Disputes, Payouts, etc. with date = yesterday.

Compute all fields.

Upsert record into PlatformAnalyticsDaily (by date).

Also enforce retention: delete records older than 365 days.

Compute CleanerDailySnapshot

Fetch all active cleaners.

For each cleaner:

Count bookings/cancellations/no-shows for yesterday via Booking/Dispute.

Sum earnings from jobs approved yesterday.

Read the current CleanerProfile reliability fields.

Upsert into CleanerDailySnapshot for that date+cleaner.

Clean up snapshots older than 90 days (or 180, your choice).

Update SubscriptionAnalytics

Count active/subscriptions, new, cancelled in last 7 days.

Sum monthly price for all active.

Compute churn rate.

Write into singleton SubscriptionAnalytics.

Update MembershipAnalytics

Same as above for membership tiers.

Update DashboardCache

Build:

ceo_dashboard payload

ops_dashboard payload

finance_dashboard payload

growth_dashboard payload

Save them as JSON in DashboardCache.

Run Alert Detection

Compare yesterday’s PlatformAnalyticsDaily vs rolling 7-day averages (which can be computed from last 7 daily records).

If:

cancellation_rate > 2× baseline

no_show_rate > 2× baseline

dispute_rate > 2× baseline

payment failures spike

Create SystemAlert records.

Optionally send email via Core.SendEmail or SMS via Twilio integration.

6. Dashboards (Inside Base44)
Admin UI (or a lightweight front end) will read directly from the analytics entities.

6.1 CEO Dashboard
Source: PlatformAnalyticsDaily (last 30–90 days) + SubscriptionAnalytics + MembershipAnalytics + DashboardCache.ceo_dashboard.

Shows:

GMV trend

Platform revenue trend

Active clients & cleaners

Fill rate, cancellation rate, dispute rate

MRR from subscriptions + memberships

Basic cohort retention graphs (approx via bookings over time)

6.2 COO / Ops Dashboard
Source: PlatformAnalyticsDaily, CleanerDailySnapshot, SystemAlert, plus live Bookings.

Shows:

Daily bookings by status

Cancellations & no-shows trend

Disputes trend by category

SmartMatch health: avg time to match, fallback usage (from Event/AnalyticsEvent)

Cleaner performance grid (from CleanerDailySnapshot)

6.3 CMO / Growth Dashboard
Source: AnalyticsEvent, PlatformAnalyticsDaily, SubscriptionAnalytics, MembershipAnalytics.

Shows (with lightweight Base44 queries):

Funnel stages:

bookings started

client_signups

first booking

second booking

subscription starts

Growth of subscription & membership adoption

Repeat booking rate

6.4 CFO / Finance Dashboard
Source: PlatformAnalyticsDaily, Payment/Payout aggregates, Subscription/MembershipAnalytics.

Shows:

Gross margin, net margin approximations

MRR trend
