✅ MODULE 11 — FRAUD, RISK & TRUST & SAFETY ENGINE (BASE44-ONLY)
0. Purpose
Module 11 protects PureTask from:

Bad actors (clients or cleaners)

Abuse of credits, promos, referrals, disputes, chargebacks

Reliability explosions (serial no-shows, cancellations)

Unsafe behavior (safety issues, harassment, property damage)

Reputational damage (low-quality cleaners, toxic clients)

It does this by:

Monitoring signals from Modules 1–10

Scoring risk per user & per booking

Creating RiskFlags & SystemAlerts

Enforcing automatic limits (soft locks, hard blocks)

Routing cases to manual review when needed

All of this runs in Base44 via:

Entities

Event-triggered automations

Scheduled jobs

Integration with Disputes, Payments, Reliability, Analytics & Notifications

1. Entities Used (Existing)
We lean on entities you already have:

Booking

ClientProfile

CleanerProfile

CreditTransaction

Payment

Payout

Dispute

CleaningSubscription

ClientMembership

PlatformAnalyticsDaily (Module 10)

CleanerDailySnapshot (Module 10)

SystemAlert (Module 10)

AnalyticsEvent / Event (for behavior logs)

2. New Entities for Module 11
2.1 RiskFlag (NEW)
Individual flags on a user, booking, or transaction.

RiskFlag {
  id: string,
  subject_type: string,     // "client" | "cleaner" | "booking" | "payment"
  subject_id: string,       // client_email, cleaner_email, booking_id, payment_id

  category: string,         // "payment_risk", "refund_abuse", "no_show_pattern", "safety_issue", "multi_account", etc.
  severity: string,         // "low" | "medium" | "high" | "critical"

  status: string,           // "open" | "under_review" | "resolved" | "dismissed"
  created_at: string,
  updated_at: string,

  detected_by: string,      // "automation" | "manual"
  triggered_rule: string,   // e.g. "CLIENT_DISPUTE_RATE_HIGH"

  notes: string,            // free text for ops
  metadata: object          // extra context: counts, thresholds, evidence
}
2.2 RiskProfile (NEW)
Aggregated risk score & context per client and per cleaner.

You can have two separate entities:

ClientRiskProfile

CleanerRiskProfile

or one RiskProfile with user_type. I’ll define the generic version:

RiskProfile {
  id: string,
  user_type: string,        // "client" | "cleaner"
  user_email: string,

  risk_score: number,       // 0–100 (higher = riskier)
  risk_tier: string,        // "normal" | "watch" | "restricted" | "blocked"

  open_flags: number,       // # of open RiskFlags
  total_flags: number,

  last_incident_at?: string,
  last_reviewed_at?: string,

  tags: string[],           // ["refund_heavy", "chargeback", "no_show_risk", "safety_reported"]

  metadata: object          // counts: disputes_last_90d, chargebacks, refunds, etc.
}
This entity is updated by Module 11 automations.

2.3 SafetyIncident (NEW)
Serious safety / harassment / property damage incidents that require special handling.

SafetyIncident {
  id: string,
  booking_id: string,
  client_email: string,
  cleaner_email: string,

  reported_by: string,      // "client" | "cleaner" | "support"
  category: string,         // "harassment", "theft", "property_damage", "unsafe_conditions", etc.
  severity: string,         // "medium" | "high" | "critical"

  description: string,
  evidence_urls: string[],  // photo/audio/attachment URLs

  status: string,           // "open" | "investigating" | "resolved" | "escalated"
  created_at: string,
  updated_at: string,

  actions_taken: string[],  // ["client_blocked", "cleaner_blocked", "partial_refund", ...]
}
You’ll likely create these from Disputes with safety categories or manual admin entries.

3. Risk Signals & Rules
Module 11 watches for multiple categories of risk:

Payment / financial risk

Refund / dispute abuse

Reliability & operational risk

Safety & harassment

Multi-account / account sharing

Subscription / promo abuse

Each has specific rules that trigger RiskFlags and adjust RiskProfile.risk_score.

3.1 Payment / financial risk
Signals:

Multiple failed payments in short period.

Chargebacks / cardholder disputes from Stripe.

Suspicious payment patterns (lots of small charges, then chargebacks).

Example rules:

CLIENT_PAYMENT_FAIL_SPIKE
If a client has ≥ 3 payment failures in 7 days → create a RiskFlag (payment_risk, medium).

CLIENT_CHARGEBACK
On Stripe chargeback:

Create Dispute (Module 7).

Create RiskFlag with category payment_risk, severity = high/critical.

Increase RiskProfile.risk_score sharply.

Possibly auto-set risk_tier = "restricted" (no new bookings until reviewed).

CLEANER_PAYOUT_ANOMALY
If a cleaner’s payout amount jumps > X× their average weekly earnings → mark RiskFlag for review.

3.2 Refund / dispute abuse (clients)
Signals:

High dispute rate vs bookings.

Frequent full refunds and client-favor outcomes.

Pattern of nitpicking or “never satisfied” behavior.

Example rules:

CLIENT_DISPUTE_RATE_HIGH

If, in last 90 days:

client_disputes ≥ 3 AND

dispute_rate ≥ e.g. 30% of their bookings

Create RiskFlag (category refund_abuse, severity = medium/high).

Mark RiskProfile.tags += ["refund_heavy"].

CLIENT_REFUND_VOLUME_HIGH

If total refunds_usd in past 90 days > threshold (e.g. > $500).

Create RiskFlag and potentially move to risk_tier = "restricted" (limits on refunds, more manual review).

3.3 Reliability & operational risk (cleaners)
Signals:

High no-show rate.

High cancellation rate.

Low reliability_score from Module 6.

High dispute rate.

Low ratings with specific tags (“rude”, “rough”, “careless”).

Example rules:

CLEANER_NO_SHOW_PATTERN

If no_show_rate ≥ 5% in last 30 days OR ≥ 2 no-shows in last 10 jobs:

Create RiskFlag (no_show_pattern, high).

Possibly auto-disable InstantBook for that cleaner.

Reduce reliability or send to Module 6 as a strong negative event.

CLEANER_DISPUTE_PATTERN

If cleaner has ≥ 3 client_favor disputes in past 60 days:

Create RiskFlag (quality_risk, medium/high).

RiskProfile.risk_tier = "watch" or restricted depending on severity.

CLEANER_SAFETY_INCIDENT

When a SafetyIncident is created against a cleaner with severity = high/critical:

Auto-set risk_tier = "blocked" pending review.

Auto-disable their bookings.

3.4 Safety & harassment (both sides)
Signals:

SafetyIncident created.

Disputes with category = safety_concern, harassment, theft, property_damage.

Cleaners or clients reported multiple times across different bookings.

Example rules:

SAFETY_CRITICAL

If SafetyIncident.severity = critical:

Immediate RiskFlag for both parties with high/critical severity.

Auto-block or restrict accounts until human review.

Auto-create SystemAlert of type safety_critical.

SAFETY_REPEAT_OFFENDER

If more than 1 SafetyIncident or safety-category dispute for the same user:

risk_tier = "blocked" until manual decision.

3.5 Multi-account / account sharing
Base44 won’t magically detect IP/device fingerprint, but we can approximate with what we have (and add fields later):

Potential signals (if you choose to track them):

Same phone number used by multiple ClientProfiles.

Same payment method used across multiple accounts.

Same address but multiple different client emails with abnormal behavior.

Cleaners working via multiple emails (same SSN / payout info, once you add that).

Example rules:

MULTI_ACCOUNT_PAYMENT

When Payment is created, check if card fingerprint / last4 is associated with multiple clients.

If # distinct client_emails using same card > X:

Create RiskFlag for each account.

SHARED_PHONE

If same phone_number is used by > N accounts with poor behavior (disputes, refunds):

Flag.

You can start simple and expand later; just make sure RiskProfile.metadata can store these counts.

3.6 Subscription / promo abuse
Signals:

Subscription started → first cleaning → immediate cancellation + refund request.

Client churn & re-subscribe cycles to game discounts.

Overuse of promo codes, referral abuse.

Example rules:

SUBSCRIPTION_CHURN_GAMING

If client has ≥ 2 short-lived subscriptions in last 6 months:

Flag RiskFlag (subscription_abuse, medium).

Potentially restrict future intro discounts.

PROMO_ABUSE

If client uses more than allowed promo codes or abnormal number of referrals with overlapping data:

Flag and require manual review.

4. Risk Scoring & Tiers
The RiskProfile uses a simple 0–100 risk_score.

Example weightings:

Payment risk (chargebacks, failed payments) → up to +40

Dispute/refund abuse → up to +25

Safety incidents → up to +50

Reliability risk (cleaner) → up to +25

Multi-account / promo abuse → up to +20

You can define a simple additive scoring:

risk_score = payment_risk_points
           + dispute_risk_points
           + safety_points
           + reliability_points
           + abuse_points
Suggested mapping:
0–19 → normal

20–39 → watch

40–69 → restricted

70–100 → blocked

Automations adjust:

risk_tier based on risk_score

And trigger enforcement actions.

5. Enforcement Actions
Depending on RiskProfile.risk_tier and specific flags:

For Clients:
watch:

No blocking, but highlight in support UI.

Disputes require more evidence.

restricted:

Limit # of active bookings.

Require prepayment only (no partial/“pay later” options).

Dispute refunds go to manual review.

blocked:

Cannot create new bookings.

Existing future bookings reviewed or cancelled.

Membership/subscriptions auto-cancelled or paused.

Support required to reinstate.

For Cleaners:
watch:

Show warnings in internal tools.

Monitor reliability more closely.

restricted:

Disable InstantBook.

Lower priority in SmartMatch.

Limit # new clients per week.

blocked:

Remove from marketplace.

Cancel future assigned bookings or reassign to other cleaners.

Freeze payouts under review (careful with legal/compliance; usually only freeze disputed amounts).

All enforcement should be implemented as:

Base44 automations triggered on RiskProfile update:

Update CleanerProfile flags (is_active, instant_book_enabled).

Update ClientProfile (is_blocked or can_book boolean).

Re-route or cancel future bookings.

6. Automations (Flows in Base44)
6.1 Event-driven: On risk-related events
Triggers:

Dispute.created / Dispute.resolved

SafetyIncident.created / updated

Payment.failed / chargeback webhooks

Payout.created / Payout.completed

Booking.status changes (especially to cancelled or disputed/no_show)

CleanerProfile.reliability_score updates

Actions:

Recalculate relevant user’s risk stats.

Update/create RiskProfile for the client/cleaner.

If thresholds exceeded, create RiskFlag.

If risk_tier escalates, trigger enforcement flows + maybe SystemAlert.

6.2 Nightly “Risk Cron”
Once per day:

Scan all RiskProfiles:

Decay risk over time if no new incidents (e.g., lower risk_score by 1–2 points / week of clean behavior).

Automatically move restricted → watch → normal for long-term good behavior.

Summary checks:

Top risk clients and cleaners.

High-risk SafetyIncidents still open (escalate to SystemAlert).

Create SystemAlerts for patterns:

Many new RiskFlags of the same type.

Spike in high-risk profiles in a region.

6.3 Admin-initiated flows
Admins can:

Manually create or edit RiskFlag.

Manually adjust RiskProfile.risk_tier (override automation).

Resolve/dismiss flags and safety incidents.

Add notes and actions.

Each admin action updates:

RiskProfile.last_reviewed_at

Optionally logs an Event for audit.

7. Integration With Other Modules
Module 1 – Booking Lifecycle

Risk tier can affect ability to book, acceptance flow, and fallback behavior.

Module 2 – Credits & Payments

High-risk clients might get stricter refund handling and prepay-only.

Module 3 – Payout Engine

Risky cleaners may have payouts delayed for disputed bookings.

Module 4 – Pricing

You might charge upfront or add insurance fees for high-risk scenarios later.

Module 5 – SmartMatch

Avoid assigning high-risk clients to new cleaners.

Avoid high-risk cleaners for new clients.

Use RiskProfile in match scoring.

Module 6 – Reliability

Feeds risk for cleaners (no-show, dispute, etc.), not recalc.

Module 7 – Disputes

Each dispute outcome adds risk or reduces it depending on resolution.

Module 8 – Notifications

Risk-related communications:

“Your account is under review”

“Your booking ability is temporarily restricted”

Internal alerts for ops.

Module 9 – Recurring & Subscriptions

Risk tier may auto-cancel or pause subscriptions/memberships.

Module 10 – Analytics & KPIs

Risk distribution metrics:

% users in watch/restricted/blocked

Financial impact: fraud losses, refunds from risky accounts

Safety incidents trend.

Module 11 is very strong structurally.
It aligns with professional trust & safety systems used by:

Uber

Doordash

and integrates nicely with Modules 1–10.

But — like all risk systems — it has holes and missing layers.

I’ll go through everything section by section.

❗1. ENTITY DESIGN REVIEW
1.1 RiskFlag — GOOD but missing two important things
✔ Correct:
Has category, severity, metadata

Tracks status (open/resolved)

Stores triggered rule

Attaches to subject (client/cleaner/booking/payment)

❌ Missing:
❌ 1. A “cooldown / expiration” field
Some risk flags should automatically expire after days/weeks/months.

Add:

expires_at?: string
❌ 2. A “confidence score”
Risk flags are not binary; many are probabilistic.

Add:

confidence: number  // 0–1 or 0–100
This matters for machine-learning driven enhancements later.

1.2 RiskProfile — GOOD but missing some essentials
✔ Strong features:
risk_score

risk_tier

tags

metadata

❌ Missing fields:
❌ 1. lifetime_booking_count and recent_booking_count
Risk algorithms need context.

Example:

1 dispute out of 1 = high risk

1 dispute out of 300 = very low risk

❌ 2. Velocity metrics
(Count of actions over short periods)

Add:

actions_last_24h
actions_last_7d
payments_last_24h
payments_last_7d
❌ 3. Geo / ZIP for cleaner & client
Helps detect bad neighborhoods, repeat safety issues, etc.

Optional but useful:

region: string
zip_code: string
1.3 SafetyIncident — Good but missing categories
Missing categories:
“Weapons present”

“Unsafe pets”

“Illegal activity”

“Hostile environment”

“Biohazard”

These occur in real home-cleaning marketplaces.

Add them to category.

injuries_reported

❗2. RISK SIGNALS & RULES REVIEW
✔ Overall: VERY STRONG
Your structure mirrors real risk models.

But you’re missing some highly profitable & necessary rules.

Let’s list the gaps.

❌ 2.1 Missing the most important rule category: Identity Risk
Because cleaners enter homes, identity is critical.

Base44 does NOT enforce these unless YOU do:

Missing signals:
Suspicious name mismatch (profile name ≠ payout name)

Suspicious phone behavior (frequent changes)

Suspicious email patterns (temporary emails)

Same identity used across multiple accounts

Incomplete profile (missing profile photo, missing address, missing payout info)

Add rule:
“IDENTITY_INCOMPLETE_RISK”
If cleaner_profile completeness < 80% → restrict work until completed.

❌ 2.2 Missing: Cleaner Credential Risk
Think:

Background check expiration

Missing W9 / tax info

Invalid SSN format

Payout account mismatches

Even if you don’t enforce these now, the module should support it later.

❌ 2.3 Missing: Address-based risk (clients)
Real cleaning companies track this:

“Bad locations”

“Past safety events at this address”

“Property with repeat disputes”

Add:

HomeRiskProfile entity or at least:

address_risk_score
address_tags: ["previous_safety_incident", "hostile_client", ...]
Bookings should inherit risk from client + address + cleaner.

❌ 2.4 Missing: Cleaner fatigue / overscheduling risk
Cleaners taking too many jobs per day → quality drops.

Add rule:

“CLEANER_OVERLOAD_RISK”

If:

more than 3–4 jobs per day

too many same-day bookings

too little rest between jobs

→ reduce SmartMatch priority
→ raise risk_score slightly

❌ 2.5 Missing: Subscription fraud logic
You mentioned subscription abuse but missed deeper layers.

Common fraud patterns:

Client buys subscription discount

Does one job

Immediately cancels

Repeats with new account / new card

Add rules:

Detect repeated short-term subs

Detect refund-then-restart patterns

Detect multiple subs linked to same address

❗3. RISK SCORING SYSTEM REVIEW
✔ The tiers (normal → watch → restricted → blocked) are perfect.
But the scoring system needs:

❌ 1. Risk SCORE DECAY rules
You mentioned daily cron, but you need explicit rules:

Example:

If no incidents for 30 days → reduce risk_score by 15%

For cleaners with perfect reliability for 20 jobs → reduce risk_score

❌ 2. Ceiling values per category
Prevents runaway scores.

❌ 3. Interaction between scores and Module 6 Reliability
Cleaner reliability MUST influence risk_score.

You should define:

if reliability_score < 70 → +10 risk
if reliability_score < 50 → +25 risk
if reliability_score < 30 → AUTO restrict
❗4. ENFORCEMENT ACTIONS REVIEW
✔ Correct:
watch / restricted / blocked

limit bookings

restrict InstantBook

reroute jobs

freeze payouts (carefully)

❌ Missing:
4.1 Soft Locks (MOST IMPORTANT)
Before blocking a user, platforms usually implement:

“Profile Verification Required”

“Update Payment Method”

“Contact Support”

“Identity Verification Needed”

Add:

RiskProfile.requires_identity_verification
RiskProfile.requires_payment_update
4.2 Escalation Workflow
Safety incidents require:

escalation to safety team

24-hour auto check-ins

high-urgency alerts

Add:

SafetyIncident.escalation_level
❗5. AUTOMATIONS REVIEW
✔ Good: event-driven + nightly cron + admin override.
❌ Missing:
5.1 Risk Feedback Loop Into SmartMatch (Module 5)
You mentioned it indirectly, but it should be explicit:

high-risk cleaners → lower SmartMatch score

high-risk clients → avoid assigning new cleaners

This protects quality AND safety.

5.2 Risk → Pricing (Module 4)
Future improvement:

Charge deposits for high-risk clients

Increase payouts for high-risk bookings

Reduce booking acceptance windows for risky clients

6.1 Module 10 Analytics → Module 11 Risk

6.2 Module 3 Payout → Module 11 Risk

Something like:

UserBehavior {

  avg_cancellation_window,

}
“Behavior risk” is a huge predictor.

Photos and videos uploaded in disputes should count toward risk.

Example:
If cleaners frequently upload poor-quality “before photos” → adjust risk.

If any SafetyIncident:

suspend user

lock upcoming bookings

notify safety ops

generate dashboard alert

require identity verification

Every enforcement action should be logged.

You need an entity:

RiskActionLog {

  timestamp,

For compliance + audits.

2. New Entities (Corrected + Improved)
2.1 RiskFlag (NEW + FIXED)
Individual risk markers for clients, cleaners, bookings, or payments.

RiskFlag {
  id: string,
  subject_type: "client" | "cleaner" | "booking" | "payment",
  subject_id: string,             // email or booking_id or payment_id

  category: string,               // e.g. "payment_risk", "refund_abuse", "safety_issue"
  severity: "low" | "medium" | "high" | "critical",
  confidence: number,             // 0–100

  status: "open" | "under_review" | "resolved" | "dismissed",
  triggered_rule: string,         // e.g. "CLEANER_NO_SHOW_PATTERN"
  detected_by: "automation" | "manual",

  expires_at?: string,            // auto-expire for mild risks
  created_at: string,
  updated_at: string,

  metadata: object,
  notes: string
}
2.2 RiskProfile (NEW + FIXED)
Every client & cleaner gets an evolving risk score.

RiskProfile {
  id: string,
  user_type: "client" | "cleaner",
  user_email: string,

  risk_score: number,               // 0–100
  risk_tier: "normal" | "watch" | "restricted" | "blocked",
  tags: string[],                   // indicators e.g. ["refund_heavy", "safety_risk"]

  open_flags: number,
  total_flags: number,

  lifetime_booking_count: number,
  recent_booking_count: number,      // last 30–90 days

  actions_last_24h: number,
  actions_last_7d: number,

  payments_last_24h: number,
  payments_last_7d: number,

  last_incident_at?: string,
  last_reviewed_at?: string,

  metadata: object                 // aggregated metrics, dispute_rate, etc.
}
2.3 SafetyIncident (NEW + EXPANDED)
SafetyIncident {
  id: string,
  booking_id: string,
  client_email: string,
  cleaner_email: string,

  reported_by: "client" | "cleaner" | "support",
  category: string,                 // harassment, theft, unsafe_pets, biohazard, etc.
  severity: "medium" | "high" | "critical",

  description: string,
  evidence_urls: string[],

  injuries_reported: boolean,
  requires_escalation: boolean,
  escalation_level: number,         // 1–3

  status: "open" | "investigating" | "resolved" | "escalated",
  created_at: string,
  updated_at: string,

  actions_taken: string[]
}
2.4 RiskActionLog (NEW)
Tracks every enforcement action for compliance & internal audit.

RiskActionLog {
  id: string,
  user_type: "client" | "cleaner",
  user_email: string,

  action_type: string,             // "restricted_account", "blocked_account", "soft_lock_payment", etc.
  performed_by: "automation" | "admin",
  timestamp: string,

  metadata: object
}
3. Risk Categories & Detection Rules
This section now includes all missing categories + improvements.

3.1 Financial / Payment Risk
Signals:
Multiple payment failures

Chargeback / cardholder dispute

Suspicious payment velocity

Payment mismatch with booking behavior

Rules:
Rule: CLIENT_PAYMENT_FAIL_SPIKE
If:

3+ failed payments in 7 days

→ create RiskFlag (payment_risk, medium)

Rule: CLIENT_CHARGEBACK
When Stripe reports a chargeback:

RiskFlag (payment_risk, critical)

risk_score += 40

risk_tier = "restricted"

require new card before next booking

Rule: CLEANER_PAYOUT_ANOMALY
If cleaner payouts in last 14 days > 3× typical average:

Create RiskFlag (payment_risk, medium)

Force manual payout review

3.2 Refund & Dispute Abuse (Clients)
Signals:
High dispute rate

Pattern of complaining

Refund-heavy client

Rules:
Rule: CLIENT_DISPUTE_RATE_HIGH
If dispute_rate > 30% over last 90 days:

RiskFlag (refund_abuse)

risk_score += 20

risk_tier = “watch”

Rule: CLIENT_REFUND_VOLUME_HIGH
If refunds_usd > $500 in last 60 days:

restrict ability to request refunds automatically

disputes must be manually reviewed

3.3 Cleaner Reliability & Operational Risk
Integrated with Module 6 (reliability).

Rules:
Rule: CLEANER_NO_SHOW_PATTERN
If cleaner has:

≥2 no-shows in last 10 jobs OR

no_show_rate > 5%

→ RiskFlag (high)
→ auto-disable InstantBook
→ reduce SmartMatch priority

Rule: CLEANER_DISPUTE_PATTERN
3+ client-favor disputes in 60 days:

risk_tier = “restricted”

manual review required

3.4 Safety & Harassment Risk
Rules:
Rule: SAFETY_CRITICAL
If SafetyIncident.severity = critical:

auto-block the user (client or cleaner)

require manual review to restore

Rule: SAFETY_REPEAT_OFFENDER
If user has more than 1 serious safety-related dispute:

risk_tier = “blocked”

cancel upcoming bookings

3.5 Identity Risk
NEW & IMPORTANT
Signals:
name mismatch

missing profile photo

frequently changing phone/email

suspicious payout account changes

Rule: IDENTITY_INCOMPLETE_RISK
If profile_completeness < 80%:

risk_tier = “restricted”

require verification before next booking/accepting job

3.6 Multi-Account / Shared Account Risk
Signals:
Same phone number across multiple accounts

Same address but multiple new accounts

Same card used across many accounts

Rule: MULTI_ACCOUNT_PAYMENT
If same card used by >2 clients:

RiskFlag

require verification

3.7 Cleaner Overload / Fatigue Risk
Important for quality.

Rule: CLEANER_OVERLOAD_RISK
If a cleaner has:

3 jobs in a day OR

<90 minutes gap between jobs

→ lower SmartMatch priority
→ small risk_score increase

3.8 Subscription / Promo Abuse
Signals:
Short-lived subs

Abuse of discounts

Repeated signups & cancellations

Rule: SUBSCRIPTION_GAMING
If 2+ short-term subs in 6 months:

risk_tier = “watch”

deny discount codes

Rule: PROMO_ABUSE
If promo codes used above limit:

RiskFlag

block further promos

4. Risk Scoring Engine (Corrected)
Base formula:
risk_score = payment_risk
           + dispute_risk
           + safety_risk
           + reliability_risk
           + identity_risk
           + multi_account_risk
           + behavior_risk
Risk Tier Mapping:
0–19 → normal

20–39 → watch

40–69 → restricted

70–100 → blocked

Risk Decay (NEW):
Every 30 days without incidents:

reduce risk_score by 10–20%

remove minor flags that expired

reduce severity of tags

5. Enforcement Actions (Corrected + Improved)
Soft Locks (before blocking):
require identity verification

require payment update

require address verification

require profile completion

Hard Restrictions:
limit bookings

prepay-only requirement

disable ability to initiate disputes

disable subscription enrollment

remove promo eligibility

Blocking:
block account entirely

cancel upcoming bookings

pause payouts (only disputed amounts)

escalate safety cases automatically

All actions must create:
RiskActionLog

6. Automations (Improved + Expanded)
6.1 Event-Driven Risk Automations
Triggers:

Dispute created

Payment failed

Chargeback

Booking cancelled

Booking no-show

Cleaner reliability drop

Subscription cancelled early

SafetyIncident created

Actions:

update RiskProfile

generate RiskFlags

enforce risk tier rules

6.2 Nightly Risk Cron (Corrected)
Runs daily at 3am:

Risk Decay

Recalculate risk_score for all flagged users

Expire aged RiskFlags

Escalate unresolved SafetyIncidents

Generate SystemAlert for risk spikes

Sync with AnalyticsDaily & CleanerDailySnapshot

Auto-lower priority of high-risk cleaners in SmartMatch

Prepare Risk DashboardCache

6.3 Safety Incident Workflow
When a SafetyIncident is created:

if critical → immediate block

if high → auto-escalate to safety team

if medium → put user on watch tier

require evidence uploads

notify support team

6.4 Admin Manual Overrides
Admins can:

resolve flags

override risk tier

unblock accounts

merge multi-account identities

record actions in RiskActionLog

7. Integration With Modules 1–10 (Corrected)
Module 1 Booking Lifecycle
→ risk affects booking creation & assignment

→ high-risk clients = prepay only
→ refund abuse limited

→ risky cleaners = payout review

Approve / deny onboarding

Oversee payouts, credits, billing

Everything is still powered by Base44 entities + automations, this module just defines:

Admin-facing entities

Permissions / roles

Core screens & flows

Audit logging

How admin actions hook into Modules 1–11

1. Admin Personas & Roles
We’ll define a few “default” internal roles:

Super Admin

Full read/write everywhere

Can modify roles, config, pricing

Can hard block users

Ops Admin (Operations)

Booking management

Cleaner/client management

Rescheduling, reassigning cleaners

Manual booking creation

Support Agent

View bookings, clients, cleaners

Handle disputes, refunds (within rules)

Create/update SupportTickets

Cannot change pricing or global config

Finance / Payouts

View/reconcile payments & payouts

Approve manual payouts / adjustments

Refund approvals above threshold

Trust & Safety

Manage RiskFlags, RiskProfiles, SafetyIncidents

Block/unblock users

Oversee enforcement actions

Growth / Marketing

View KPIs & funnels

Manage promo codes & membership / subscription plans

Manage NotificationTemplate content

We’ll encode these in AdminUser and permissions.

3. New Entities for Module 12
3.1 AdminUser (NEW)
Represents internal staff.

AdminUser {
  id: string,
  email: string,
  full_name: string,

  roles: string[],            // ["super_admin", "support", "ops", "finance", "trust_safety"]
  is_active: boolean,

  last_login_at?: string,
  created_at: string
}
3.2 AdminAuditLog (NEW)
Tracks all sensitive admin actions.

AdminAuditLog {
  id: string,
  admin_email: string,
  action_type: string,        // e.g. "UPDATE_BOOKING_STATUS", "ISSUE_REFUND", "BLOCK_USER"
  target_type: string,        // "booking" | "client" | "cleaner" | "dispute" | "risk_profile"
  target_id: string,
  timestamp: string,

  before_state?: object,      // optional snapshot (may be partial)
  after_state?: object,
  metadata: object            // extra details (reason, notes)
}
This is crucial for trust, compliance, and debugging “who changed what”.

3.3 SupportTicket (NEW)
Centralized record for support tickets (might be a thin wrapper around Dispute, but more general).

SupportTicket {
  id: string,
  type: string,               // "booking_issue", "payment_issue", "account_issue", "feedback"
  status: string,             // "open", "in_progress", "resolved", "closed"
  priority: string,           // "low", "medium", "high", "urgent"

  client_email?: string,
  cleaner_email?: string,
  booking_id?: string,
  dispute_id?: string,

  subject: string,
  description: string,

  assigned_to?: string,       // admin_email
  created_at: string,
  updated_at: string,

  tags: string[],             // ["refund", "cleaner_no_show", "app_bug"]
  internal_notes: string[]
}
Disputes (Module 7) may automatically create SupportTickets for support routing.

3.4 AdminSavedView (NEW, optional but nice)
Lets admins save filters/sorts for repeated use (e.g., “All open disputes”, “Risky cleaners”, etc.).

AdminSavedView {
  id: string,
  admin_email: string,
  name: string,               // "High-risk clients (last 30d)"
  target: string,             // "bookings" | "disputes" | "risk_profiles" | "payouts"
  filters: object,            // JSON of filter conditions
  sort: object,
  created_at: string
}

Disable/enable InstantBook

Initiate or update SafetyIncidents

Link to Payout history

Again, everything goes through AdminAuditLog + possibly RiskActionLog.

Entities: Dispute, Booking, CreditTransaction, Payment, RiskProfile, SafetyIncident, SupportTicket.

Create SafetyIncidents if it’s safety-related

Add SupportTicket internal notes

When a dispute is resolved:

Module 7 handles credits, payments, earnings.

Module 11 updates risk profiles.

Module 8 sends notifications.

Module 10 counts this into analytics.

4.6 Payout & Finance Center
Entities: Payout, CleanerProfile, Payment, CreditTransaction, SubscriptionAnalytics, MembershipAnalytics, PlatformAnalyticsDaily.

Admins (Finance role) can:

View scheduled/processed payouts.

Force re-issue/hold payouts when risk flags are present.

Check RiskProfile

5. Permissions & Access Control
We can model permissions in two layers:

Role-based: each role has capabilities.

Action-based: check capabilities before performing operations.

Example capabilities:

can_view_bookings

can_edit_bookings

can_issue_refunds

can_modify_pricing

can_block_users

can_view_financials

can_view_risk_center

can_modify_risk_tier

These can either be:

Hard-coded per role, or

Stored in a small AdminRole entity if you want configurable permissions.

Every admin-triggered flow in Base44 should:

Check AdminUser.roles / capabilities before mutating data.

6. Automation Hooks for Admin Actions
Golden rule: Admins never bypass business rules.

Whenever admin changes something:

Admin UI calls a Base44 workflow, not a raw entity write.

Workflow:

Validates permission

Validates business constraints

Performs entity updates

Fires cross-module updates (e.g., Module 2, 3, 7, 10, 11)

Writes AdminAuditLog (and possibly RiskActionLog)

Examples:

“Admin cancels booking with refund”:

Check can_edit_bookings, can_issue_refunds

Update Booking.status using same logic as user-initiated cancellation

Create CreditTransaction refund

Update Payment if needed

Update PlatformAnalyticsDaily next cron

Audit log

“Admin blocks cleaner”:

Check can_block_users

Update CleanerProfile.is_active

Update RiskProfile.risk_tier = "blocked"

Cancel or reassign their future Bookings

Notify affected clients (Module 8)

Log RiskActionLog + AdminAuditLog

7. v1 vs v2 Scope for Module 12
v1 (necessary for launch)

Client & Cleaner consoles (view, basic adjustments)

Dispute center with manual resolution tools

Risk & Safety basics:

view RiskProfile & RiskFlag

manually block/unblock

Basic Analytics dashboard (PlatformAnalyticsDaily)

Config for NotificationTemplates & a few pricing knobs

v2 (pro-level internal tools)
Saved views (AdminSavedView)

More complex risk & safety center (auto-playbooks)

Advanced search/filter UX

Cleaner leaderboard & incentive tooling

Dual-approval for sensitive actions

Embedded AI assistant for support (suggest dispute resolutions, refund recommendations, message templates)

Acts as the human control plane for Modules 1–11.

Uses Base44 workflows for every admin action.

Keeps a full audit trail for security & compliance.

Surfaces all KPIs & risk in a way humans can act on quickly.

REVIEW AND ANALYZE FOR MISTAKES

Absolutely — here is a full, CTO-level REVIEW + DEBUG + DEEP ANALYSIS of Module 12 (Admin Portal & Ops Engine).
I’ll cover:

🔴 Mistakes / Structural Weaknesses

🟠 Missing Parts

🟡 Ambiguities That Need Clarification

🟢 Strengths

🔵 Suggestions & Improvements

🟣 Security / Compliance Gaps

⚫ v2+ Enhancements

This review is highly detailed, like an internal architecture audit.

Let’s begin.

🔴 SECTION 1 — Critical Mistakes / Architectural Weaknesses
These MUST be corrected before finalizing Module 12.

❌ 1. Admin actions currently bypass critical business logic (dangerous)
You wrote:

“Admin UI calls a Base44 workflow, not raw writes.”

Correct idea — but the spec does not make this strict enough.

Base44 will allow direct entity updates unless you explicitly lock down:

Booking.status

Payment.status

ClientProfile.credits_balance

Payout.status

CleanerProfile.is_active

CleanerProfile.tier

Pricing data

RiskProfile.risk_tier

If any admin has ability to directly update these values, it can break:

Module 2 (Credits)

Module 3 (Payouts)

Module 6 (Reliability)

Module 10 (Analytics)

Module 11 (Risk Engine)

Fix:
All critical fields must be write-protected and only modifiable by:

Base44 automations

Admin workflows (with business checks)

NOT direct writes in the console

You need a table:

ProtectedFieldsConfig
listing all fields requiring protected updates.

❌ 2. No definition for Admin Permissions Matrix
You defined roles (support, ops, etc.) but the capabilities list is:

incomplete

not tied to specific entity actions

not formalized

This creates risk of “role drift” where:

Support accidentally gets refund authority

Ops gets ability to block accounts

Finance modifies subscription pricing

Fix:
Define a strict permissions matrix, e.g.:

Capability	Support	Ops	Finance	Trust	SuperAdmin
View bookings	✔	✔	✔	✔	✔
Edit bookings	✖	✔	✖	✔	✔
Issue refunds	✖	✖	✔	✖	✔
Block users	✖	✖	✖	✔	✔
Manage pricing	✖	✖	✖	✖	✔
…	…	…	…	…	…
Without this, Module 12 is dangerously open to misconfiguration.

❌ 3. Missing definitions for Admin Authentication & Security
You never defined:

password requirements

MFA (2-factor)

session expiration

token revocation

IP whitelisting / geofencing

admin device fingerprinting

failed login limits

For a payments + safety-sensitive marketplace, this is high-risk.

Admins have the power to:

issue refunds

override payouts

block/unblock users

modify pricing

modify risk tiers

This is sensitive access.

Fix:
Define:

MFA required (SMS or authenticator app)

12-hour session expiration

AdminPasswordReset logs

AdminLoginAttempt logs

Support role cannot elevate privileges

❌ 4. No audit for viewing sensitive data
AdminAuditLog tracks actions, not views.

But in trust & safety systems:

viewing customer addresses

viewing cleaner payout data

viewing chat logs or dispute photos

viewing safety incident evidence (photos inside homes)

…are all highly sensitive events.

Fix:
Add:

AdminDataAccessLog {
  admin_email,
  target_type,
  target_id,
  timestamp,
  ip_address,
  metadata
}
This is industry standard (Airbnb, Uber, Doordash).

❌ 5. SupportTickets entity misses SLA timers
There must be:

“time since opened”

“time since last customer reply”

“SLA deadline”

“auto-escalation triggers”

Without SLA logic, support workflow becomes unmanageable at scale.

❌ 6. Booking modification rules not tied to pricing engine
Rescheduling, editing time, changing add-ons require:

recalculation via Module 4 Pricing

recalculation of credits through Module 2 Credits Engine

updates to escrow

updates to earnings (Module 3)

Module 12 currently allows admins to:

“reschedule or alter booking duration/tasks”

BUT WITHOUT ANY GUARANTEE OF:

pricing recalculated

cleaner rate recalculated

escrow adjusted

payout adjusted

client charged more/less correctly

This is a huge bug.

Fix:
All booking modifications must call a:

Admin_AdjustBooking_Workflow
that triggers:

pricing engine

credit engine

escrow engine

payout engine

Yeah, you’re not wrong – that last review was enterprise Uber/Airbnb-level and you do not need all of that to launch PureTask. 😅

Let me answer your question directly:

Yes, it was overboard for where you are now.

It’s still useful as a future map, but we should dramatically simplify what we actually implement for Module 12 right now.

Think of it like this:

That review was: “Here’s everything a $500M marketplace would care about.”
You’re building: “Version 1 that actually launches and runs smoothly.”

So let’s reframe Module 12 into something lean and realistic.

What you actually need for Admin v1
Here’s the minimum viable Admin Portal I’d recommend we keep from Module 12:

1. Basic roles (keep it simple)
For now, you can survive with just:

Admin (full access – you + 1 trusted person)

Support (limited: can view everything, issue small refunds, reschedule/reassign, add notes)

We don’t need 6 roles on day 1.

2. Core screens only (5 main sections)
You really only need these pages at launch:

Bookings Console

Search & view bookings

Reschedule

Reassign cleaner

Cancel booking

Trigger refund (through the normal credits/payments logic)

Client Page

View client profile, bookings, credits

Give goodwill credits

See disputes tied to this client

Cleaner Page

View profile, reliability, jobs, earnings summary

Activate/deactivate cleaner

Change tier manually (if needed)

Dispute Center

List of open disputes

See evidence & messages

Choose outcome (client wins / split / cleaner wins)

That outcome calls the existing dispute logic (Module 7) → credits, earnings, refunds auto-handled

Simple Analytics / Dashboard

Today’s bookings

Completed / canceled

Basic revenue summary

Few top-line numbers from Module 10

That’s it.
No crazy case management, no complex queues, no deep permission system yet.

3. Minimal extra entities
For v1, I’d keep only these new ones from Module 12:

AdminUser – so we can know who did what

AdminAuditLog – so major actions are tracked

SupportTicket – optional but nice if you want to track non-dispute issues

You do not need:

AdminDataAccessLog

AdminSavedView

SystemHealthDashboard entity

Case management object

Etc.

Those are v2/v3 problems.

4. Risk & safety: keep it light at launch
You already have:

RiskProfile / RiskFlag / SafetyIncident from Module 11

For Admin v1, you don’t need a huge “Risk Center” UI. You just need:

On Client page → show risk_tier + a list of risk flags

On Cleaner page → same thing

A simple way for you to:

Manually block/unblock

Manually add a note/flag if something is sketchy

The aggressive automated playbooks / queues can come later.

5. Security & permissions (practical level)
You don’t need full SOC2-grade madness right this second, but you should aim for:

Strong passwords for Admins

2 roles (Admin, Support)

Basic audit log for:

refunds

booking changes

block/unblock actions

We don’t need to overbuild MFA flows and IP whitelisting to launch.
We just don’t want “no logging, everyone can touch everything”.

REWRITE IT FOR LEAN V1

Perfect, let’s trim this thing down to something you could actually build and run without wanting to cry. 😄

Here’s Module 12 – Lean v1 Admin Portal / Ops Engine, rewritten to be simple, focused, and launchable.

✅ MODULE 12 — ADMIN PORTAL & OPS ENGINE (LEAN V1, BASE44-ONLY)
1. Purpose (v1)
The Admin Portal is a simple internal control panel for you + a tiny team to:

See what’s happening (bookings, clients, cleaners)

Fix problems (reschedule, reassign, cancel, refund)

Resolve disputes

Do basic safety & risk actions (block/unblock)

See top-level KPIs

No crazy role matrix, no heavy case system, no enterprise security circus (yet). Just enough to reliably operate PureTask.

2. Scope of v1
In scope:
Basic admin accounts

Audit log for important changes

5 core admin screens:

Bookings

Clients

Cleaners

Disputes

Simple Dashboard / KPIs

Hooks into:

Credits & Payments (Module 2)

Payouts (Module 3)

Disputes (Module 7)

Analytics lite (Module 10)

Risk & Safety basic view (Module 11)

Not in v1 (future):
Complex roles & permission matrix

Case management

System health dashboards

Content moderation tools

Bulk action tools

Deep risk center UI

We’ll keep those as “future v2+”.

3. Roles (v1)
Just two internal roles:

3.1 Admin
Full access to everything in v1

Can:

Change bookings

Issue refunds

Block/unblock users

Change cleaner tier/active status

View KPIs

Resolve disputes

3.2 Support
Read-only for most data, plus limited actions:

Reschedule bookings

Reassign cleaners

Add support notes

Propose refunds (optional) OR issue small refunds/credits within a cap

Cannot:

Block/unblock users

Change pricing or tiers

Touch payouts directly

We’ll represent these with a simple role field.

4. New Entities (v1 minimal)
4.1 AdminUser (NEW)
AdminUser {
  id: string,
  email: string,
  full_name: string,
  role: "admin" | "support",
  is_active: boolean,
  created_at: string,
  last_login_at?: string
}
You’ll manage these manually at first (no self-signup).

4.2 AdminAuditLog (NEW)
Log important changes, not every tiny click.

AdminAuditLog {
  id: string,
  admin_email: string,

  action_type: string,      // "CANCEL_BOOKING", "ISSUE_REFUND", "BLOCK_CLEANER", etc.
  target_type: string,      // "booking" | "client" | "cleaner" | "dispute"
  target_id: string,        // booking_id, email, dispute_id

  timestamp: string,
  metadata: object          // { reason, amount_credits, old_status, new_status, notes }
}
We log when admins:

Cancel a booking

Issue a refund / credit adjustment

Block / unblock client or cleaner

Change cleaner tier

Resolve a dispute

4.3 SupportTicket (OPTIONAL, v1-lite)
This is optional. Only add if you want a proper place to track random support issues.

SupportTicket {
  id: string,
  type: string,             // "booking_issue" | "payment_issue" | "account_issue"
  status: string,           // "open" | "in_progress" | "resolved"
  priority: string,         // "low" | "medium" | "high"

  client_email?: string,
  cleaner_email?: string,
  booking_id?: string,

  subject: string,
  description: string,
  internal_notes: string[],

  created_at: string,
  updated_at: string
}
If you don’t want this yet, you can use Dispute + notes and add SupportTicket later.

5. Core Admin Screens (v1)
These are the 5 pages your internal tool needs.

5.1 Bookings Console
Entities used: Booking, ClientProfile, CleanerProfile, RiskProfile (read-only).

Admin/Support can:

Search by booking_id, client email, cleaner email, date, status.

See details:

status

date/time

client & cleaner

hours, tasks

credits / charges

dispute status (if any)

Actions:

For Admin:

Reschedule booking

Reassign cleaner

Cancel booking

Trigger refund via proper Module 2 workflow

Add internal note (could be stored in Booking.metadata or SupportTicket)

For Support:

Reschedule

Reassign cleaner

Add internal note

(Optionally) issue small goodwill credit under a threshold

Every booking-changing action goes through a Base44 workflow:

Admin_RescheduleBooking

Admin_ReassignCleaner

Admin_CancelBooking

Admin_IssueRefundOrCredit

Each workflow:

Validates role

Calls normal booking + pricing + credit logic

Writes AdminAuditLog

5.2 Client Page
Entities used: ClientProfile, Booking, Dispute, CreditTransaction, RiskProfile, CleaningSubscription, ClientMembership.

Admin/Support sees:

Client contact info

Credits balance

Summary: total bookings, cancellations, disputes, refunds

Risk tier (from Module 11, read-only)

Active subscriptions/memberships

Actions:

Admin:

Adjust credits (e.g. add 100 credits goodwill)

Manually block / unblock client via ClientProfile.is_blocked & RiskProfile.risk_tier

Cancel subscription/membership if needed

Support:

Propose credits (e.g. add “suggested 50 credits” note) or directly apply small credit if allowed

Add internal notes

Important: all monetary actions call a normal credits workflow (Module 2) and log to AdminAuditLog.

5.3 Cleaner Page
Entities used: CleanerProfile, CleanerAnalytics (or snapshots), Booking, RiskProfile, Dispute, Payout.

Admin/Support sees:

Cleaner profile details

Reliability_score + key stats (attendance_rate, cancellation_rate, no_show_rate)

Tier

Basic earnings summary (last 30 days, total)

List of recent bookings

Risk tier & flags (read from Module 11)

Actions:

Admin:

Activate / deactivate cleaner (is_active)

Change tier (manual override)

Disable / enable InstantBook

Block cleaner (risk_tier = "blocked")

Support:

View only, maybe add support notes

Again, these actions go through workflows and write AdminAuditLog.

5.4 Dispute Center
Entities used: Dispute, Booking, ClientProfile, CleanerProfile, CreditTransaction, RiskProfile.

Admin/Support sees:

List of open disputes (sorted by age / amount / severity)

For each dispute:

booking info

client & cleaner

description

photos/evidence

proposed resolution (optional)

any SafetyIncident flag (if Module 11 escalated it)

Actions (mostly Admin, support can assist):

Choose outcome:

client_favor

split

cleaner_favor

no_action

For each outcome, call Module 7 dispute resolution workflow that:

updates Dispute

adjusts credits & refunds (Module 2)

adjusts cleaner earnings / payouts (Module 3)

updates RiskProfile (Module 11)

triggers notifications (Module 8)

Log to AdminAuditLog with details:

dispute_id

resolution

amounts refunded

notes

5.5 Simple Dashboard / KPIs
Entities used: PlatformAnalyticsDaily (Module 10), maybe DashboardCache.

For v1, we keep it super light:

Show for today & last 7 days:

bookings created
bookings completed
bookings cancelled
disputes opened
GMV (approx, credits or USD)

Basic completion % (completed / total)

Cancellations %

Later you can add:

more detailed charts

cleaner leaderboards

subscription MRR

risk distributions

But you don’t need complex analytics in v1.

6. Automations & Flows (v1)
Key idea: Admins never directly flip core fields. They trigger workflows.

6.1 Workflows to implement
Admin_RescheduleBooking

Inputs: admin_email, booking_id, new_date/time

Steps:

Check role: admin or support

Enforce business rules (cutoff times, cancellation policy, etc.)

Update Booking fields

Adjust notifications (Module 8)

Log AdminAuditLog

Admin_ReassignCleaner

Inputs: admin_email, booking_id, new_cleaner_email

Ensure new cleaner is valid, available, active

Update Booking.cleaner_email

Trigger notifications to both parties

Log AdminAuditLog

Admin_CancelBooking

Inputs: admin_email, booking_id, cancellation_reason

Call the same cancellation logic as user cancellations (Module 1–2):

apply fees or waivers as needed

handle refunds/credits

Log AdminAuditLog

Admin_IssueRefundOrCredit

Inputs: admin_email, client_email, amount_credits, reason, booking_id?

Run through Credit/Payment logic (Module 2)

Log AdminAuditLog

Admin_BlockUser / Admin_UnblockUser

Inputs: admin_email, user_email, user_type

Update RiskProfile + Profile (ClientProfile/CleanerProfile)

Cancel or reassign future bookings if cleaner blocked

Log AdminAuditLog

Admin_ResolveDispute

Inputs: admin_email, dispute_id, outcome

Delegate to Module 7 dispute resolution

Log AdminAuditLog

That’s enough for v1.

7. Security (v1 level, not insane)
You don’t need enterprise stuff yet, but do this minimum:

Strong passwords for AdminUser

Only you create AdminUser rows (no public signup)

Log out Admins after some idle time (if front-end supports it)

Use AdminAuditLog for all money- and risk-related actions

Do not show full payment info (Stripe handles that)

We’re not implementing MFA, IP whitelisting, or full view-logging yet. That can be v2.

8. v2+ Ideas (just for later, not now)
Extra roles beyond Admin/Support

Risk Center UI with queues

SupportTickets as a full case system

Content moderation tools

System health dashboard

More dashboards (CFO, CMO views)

Bulk tools (bulk reassign during outages, etc.)

MFA & stricter access control

9. Summary
Lean v1 Module 12 gives you:

✅ Simple Admin portal that you & a small team can actually use

✅ The essential screens to operate PureTask: bookings, clients, cleaners, disputes, basic KPIs

✅ AdminUser + AdminAuditLog so you don’t lose track of who did what

✅ Clean hooks into your existing modules (1–3, 7, 10, 11)

❌ None of the overkill enterprise complexity (for now)

If you want next, we can:

Turn this Lean v1 Module 12 into:

a Base44 entity+automation blueprint, or

start building a “Master Index” of Modules 1–12 so we know exactly what’s defined where.
